<h1 id="mcetoc_1euiupec21fq">INTRODUCTION OPERATIONS MANUAL<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[IOHE]</span></h1>
<h2 id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiimcf">[0.0] Introduction Operations Manual</h2>
<p>In this chapter, the structure of the document is explained.&nbsp;</p>
<p>This Operations Manual (OM) has been drawn up by [OPERATOR] to be able to perform safe UAS operations. In this OM, it is clearly stated who is responsible for what during an operation, how the drone can be deployed correctly and safely and according to which rules and procedures must be worked. It also contains information necessary for the safe operation of a flight.</p>
<p>These procedures must be followed by all persons involved in a mission. [OPERATOR] ensures that the personnel of the organisation have easy access to the parts of the operational manual that relates to their function(s).</p>
<p>[OPERATOR] expects to guarantee safety during the operational UAS activities with the help of this OM.</p>
<article id="article_FPNQRXvwPf7aHL6v2hkU" class="not_editable" data-id="FPNQRXvwPf7aHL6v2hkU">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="FPNQRXvwPf7aHL6v2hkU"><span class="shortcode">[0.1]</span> <span class="name">Safety Statement</span></h2>
<p>I, the undersigned, hereby declare that the UAS operation will comply with:</p>
<ul>
<li>any applicable Union and national rules related to privacy, data protection, liability, insurance, security and environmental protection (article 12, regulation EU 2019/947);</li>
<li>liability coverage of <span class="s2">the </span>policy which is in accordance with the<span class="s2">&nbsp;</span>European Union Regulations Nr.785/2004 <span class="s2">dated </span>21 <span class="s2">April </span>2004. [OPERATOR] is insured against war risk and hijacking.;</li>
<li>the applicable requirement of Regulation (EU) 2019/947; and</li>
<li><span style="font-weight: 400;">[OPERATOR]s documentation;</span></li>
<li>the limitations and conditions defined in the authorisation provided by the competent authority.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p><strong>For Approval [OPERATOR]</strong></p>
<p>Danny Dijkshoorn&nbsp;</p>
<p></p>
<article id="article_JsNw38oLz6LLhS7dxSeI" class="not_editable" data-id="JsNw38oLz6LLhS7dxSeI">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="JsNw38oLz6LLhS7dxSeI" id="mcetoc_1h4is3ulmvk"><span class="shortcode">[0.2]</span> <span class="name">Structure</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The Operations Manual is structured as follows:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><strong>Part A: General.</strong> This part contains organisation, the concept of operations, general operational policies, company rules, instructions and procedures needed for a safe operation.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><strong>Part B: UAS Operating Information.</strong>&nbsp;This part contains all type-related instructions and procedures needed for a safe operation. It takes account of any differences between types, variants or individual UAS used by the operator.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><strong>Part C: Specific Operating Procedures. </strong>This part contains all instructions and information needed for the area of operation.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><strong>Part D: Training &amp; Instructions.</strong> This part contains regulations, all training instructions and general knowledge of personnel required for a safe operation.&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">This structure is commonly used by airline operators and will therefore be recognised by those who are familiar&nbsp; with avation.&nbsp;</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_7OogLEjE3JmPwfM9Gict" class="not_editable" data-id="7OogLEjE3JmPwfM9Gict">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="7OogLEjE3JmPwfM9Gict" id="mcetoc_1h4is3ulmvl"><span class="shortcode">[0.2.1]</span> <span class="name">A structure according to AMC1 UAS.SPEC.030 (3)(e)</span></h2>
<p class="Heading2OrgManual" filtered-topic="true"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">A</span><span data-preserver-spaces="true">ll items mentioned in <a href="https://www.easa.europa.eu/document-library/easy-access-rules/online-publications/easy-access-rules-unmanned-aircraft-systems?page=1&amp;kw=template">AMC1&nbsp;UAS.SPEC.030(3)(e)&nbsp;Application for an operational authorisation </a>are written in this OM, however the sequence of the items is different.<br></span></p>

<p><strong></strong></p>
<article id="article_7YQwY32lVpuYNqf6jkwa" class="not_editable" data-id="7YQwY32lVpuYNqf6jkwa">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="7YQwY32lVpuYNqf6jkwa" id="mcetoc_1h4is3ulmvm"><span class="shortcode">[0.4]</span> <span class="name">System for Amendment and Revision of the OM</span></h2>
<p><strong>RESPONSIBILITIES</strong></p>
<div class="page" title="Page 10">
<div class="section">
<div class="layoutArea">
<div class="column">
<p>The operations manual shall include all the changes which are required by ILT. The accountable manager shall inform all the changes to all operating staff so that they will be able to conduct the drone-operations according to the latest operations manual. Furthermore, the Accountable manager is responsible for maintaining the up-to-date information of the operations manual and its appendices. Each operating staff is responsible for possessing the latest version of the operations manual.</p>
<p><strong>REVISING PROCEDURE</strong></p>
<p>Handwritten amendments are not permitted except in situations requiring immediate amendment or revision in the interest of safety. Therefore any amendments shall be performed following the revising procedure.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Each version of the operations manual is identified with a version number. Version numbers are divided into sets of numbers, separated by decimal points. A change in the leftmost number indicates a major change in the manual. The major change of the manual means that almost the entire contents are replaced. Changes in the rightmost number typically indicate a minor change.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The revision date of the operations manual is the date when the new version is compiled.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Once the operator receives approval from the ILT, the operations manual shall not be changed or revised. When an amendment is made with regard to a flight operation, the whole operation procedure and/or risk analysis and/or mitigations should be reviewed by ILT. For any urgent amendments, it is possible to request approval from ILT afterwards if only the (flight) safety permits.&nbsp;</p>
<p>For the amendments, the extra costs will be charged by ILT. Minor changes, corrections of texts, typos, adding extra information and modification of the layout are however not included.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Suggestions or changes to the OM shall be processed by or on behalf of the Accountable Manager (AM). When the suggestions are approved by the AM, they shall be updated in the OM.</p>
<ul>
<li>After these changes are implemented, a meeting will be scheduled by the AM where all stakeholders within the flight organisation (as described in [A1.1] ) are briefed and required to attend, this can be carried out physically and/or through an online meeting.</li>
<li>The AM makes a short report after this meeting with point-by-point adjustments made, in addition to registering the attendance of all staff members. This report is sent via email to all staff members and stored on the central data storage.</li>
</ul>
<p>Only after this meeting the new OM is active and available as a PDF file via the company network to all staff members. CAA-NL (ILT) shall in be a possession of the most recent version of the OM.</p>
<p>There are two types of amendments:</p>
<p>Minor amendments</p>
<ul>
<li>Additional pilots or changes to existing pilots</li>
<li>Additional observers or changes to existing observers</li>
<li>New UAS Type</li>
</ul>
<p>Major amendments</p>
<ul>
<li>Improving/addition of operational procedures</li>
<li>Change of Accountable Manager</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</article>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="ghpKkFiKvaPCbGBuOgQs" id="article_ghpKkFiKvaPCbGBuOgQs">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="ghpKkFiKvaPCbGBuOgQs" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja70239"><span class="shortcode">[0.5]</span> <span class="name">Definitions, Abbreviations and Acronyms</span></h2>
<p class="not_editable" data-id="ghpKkFiKvaPCbGBuOgQs"><span style="font-size: 12pt;"><strong>Definitions</strong></span></p>
<ol>
<li>‘Airspace observer’ means a person who assists the remote pilot by performing unaided visual scanning of the airspace in which the unmanned aircraft is operating for any potential hazard in the air;</li>
<li>‘Assemblies of people’ means gatherings where persons are unable to move away due to the density of the people present;</li>
<li>'Atypical Airspace' is a part of the airspace that is:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type: none;">
<ul>
<li class="p1">Prohibited, restricted and danger areas;</li>
<li class="p1">Airspace where manned aircraft normally cannot go (e.g. airspace within 30 metres of buildings or structures);</li>
<li>Airspace where it can be demonstrated that the collision speed of manned aircraft (collision is defined as a distance of 3000 ft. Horizontal and ± 350 ft. vertical) is less than 1E-6 per flight hour during the operation);</li>
<li>Airspace that does not fall under Airspace Encounter Categories (AEC) 1 to 12.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>‘Autonomous operation’ means an operation during which an unmanned aircraft operates without the remote pilot being able to intervene;</li>
<li>‘Beyond Visual Line of Sight’ (‘BVLOS’) means a type of UAS operation which is not conducted in VLOS;</li>
<li>‘C2 link service’ means a communication service supplied by a third party, providing command and control between the unmanned aircraft and the CU;</li>
<li>C3 Link: The term “C3 link” encompasses: the Command and Control (C2) link, and any communication link required for the safety of the flight.&nbsp;</li>
<li>‘Contingency area’ means the projection of the contingency volume on the surface of the earth;&nbsp;</li>
<li>‘Contingency volume’ means the volume of airspace outside the flight<span>&nbsp;</span>geography where contingency procedures described in point (6)(d) of<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://www.easa.europa.eu/en/document-library/easy-access-rules/online-publications/easy-access-rules-unmanned-aircraft-systems?page=8#_DxCrossRefBm747354259"><span>Appendix 5</span></a><span>&nbsp;</span>to the Annex are applied;</li>
<li>‘Controlled Ground Area’ means the ground area where the UAS is operated and within which the UAS operator can ensure that only involved persons are present;</li>
<li>‘Dangerous goods’ means articles or substances, which are capable of posing a hazard to health, safety, property or the environment in the case of an incident or accident, that the unmanned aircraft is carrying as its payload, including in particular:&nbsp;
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type: none;">
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<li>explosives (mass explosion hazard, blast projection hazard, minor blast hazard, major fire hazard, blasting agents, extremely insensitive explosives);</li>
<li>gases (flammable gas, non-flammable gas, poisonous gas, oxygen, inhalation hazard);</li>
<li>flammable liquids (flammable liquids; combustible, fuel oil, gasoline);</li>
<li>flammable solids (flammable solids, spontaneously combustible solids, dangerous when wet);</li>
<li>oxidising agents and organic peroxides;</li>
<li>toxic and infectious substances (poison, biohazard);</li>
<li>radioactive substances;</li>
<li>corrosive substances;</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>‘Flight<span>&nbsp;</span>geography area’ means the projection of the flight<span>&nbsp;</span>geography on the surface of the earth;</li>
<li>‘Flight<span>&nbsp;</span>geography’ means the volume(s) of airspace defined spatially and temporally in which the UAS operator plans to conduct the operation under normal procedures described in point&nbsp;(6)(c) of<span>&nbsp;</span><span>Appendix&nbsp;5</span><span>&nbsp;</span>to the Annex (Easy Access Rules);</li>
<li>‘Geo-awareness’ means a function that, based on the data provided by Member States, detects a potential breach of airspace limitations and alerts the remote pilots so that they can take immediate and effective action to prevent that breach;</li>
<li>‘Geographical zone’ or 'Geo-Zone' means a portion of airspace established by the competent authority that facilitates, restricts or excludes UAS operations in order to address risks pertaining to safety, privacy, protection of personal data, security or the environment, arising from UAS operations;</li>
<li>‘Ground risk buffer’ is an area over the surface of the earth, which surrounds the operational volume and that is specified in order to minimise the risk to third parties on the surface in the event of the unmanned aircraft leaving the operational volume.</li>
<li>‘Light UAS Operator Certificate’ (‘LUC’) means a certificate issued to a UAS operator by a competent authority as set out in part C of the Annex (see Easy Access Rules);</li>
<li>‘Maximum Take-Off Mass’ (‘MTOM’) means the maximum Unmanned Aircraft mass, including payload and fuel, as defined by the manufacturer or the builder, at which the Unmanned Aircraft can be operated;</li>
<li>‘Night’ means the hours between the end of evening civil twilight and the beginning of morning civil twilight as defined in Implementing Regulation (EU) No 923/2012&nbsp;<span><span aria-describedby="ui-tooltip-8"><sup>8</sup></span>.</span></li>
<li>‘Operational volume’ is the combination of the flight<span>&nbsp;</span>geography and the contingency volume;</li>
<li>‘Payload’ means instrument, mechanism, equipment, part, apparatus, appurtenance, or accessory, including communications equipment, that is installed in or attached to the aircraft and is not used or intended to be used in operating or controlling an aircraft in flight, and is not part of an airframe, engine, or propeller;</li>
<li>‘Populated area’ should be understood as ‘congested area’, as defined in Regulation (EU) No 965/2012 (the ‘Air Operations Regulation’): ‘in relation to a city, town or settlement, any area which is substantially used for residential, commercial or recreational purposes’<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li>‘Robustness’ means the property of mitigation measures resulting from combining the safety gain provided by the mitigation measures and the level of assurance and integrity that the safety gain has been achieved;</li>
<li>‘Rural area’ is used in the context of the air risk and it means the volume outside a populated area and not within the aerodrome traffic zone (ATZ) of an aerodrome.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li>‘Standard Scenario’ means a type of UAS operation in the ‘specific’ category, as defined in<span>&nbsp;</span><a href="https://www.easa.europa.eu/document-library/easy-access-rules/online-publications/easy-access-rules-unmanned-aircraft-systems?page=8#_DxCrossRefBm1764556581"><span>Appendix&nbsp;1</span></a><span>&nbsp;</span>of the Annex in the Easy Access Rules, for which a precise list of mitigating measures has been identified in such a way that the competent authority can be satisfied with declarations in which operators declare that they will apply the mitigating measures when executing this type of operation;</li>
<li>‘Uninvolved persons’ means persons who are not participating in the UAS operation or who are not aware of the instructions and safety precautions given by the UAS operator;</li>
<li>‘Unmanned aircraft observer’ means a person, positioned alongside the remote pilot, who, by unaided visual observation of the unmanned aircraft, assists the remote pilot in keeping the unmanned aircraft in VLOS and safely conducting the flight;</li>
<li>‘Unmanned Aircraft System’ (‘UAS’) means an unmanned aircraft and the equipment to control it remotely;</li>
<li>‘Unmanned Aircraft System Operator’ (‘UAS operator’) means any legal or natural person operating or intending to operate one or more UAS;</li>
<li>‘Visual Line of Sight’ (‘VLOS’) means a type of UAS operation in which, the remote pilot is able to maintain continuous unaided visual contact with the unmanned aircraft, allowing the remote pilot to control the flight path of the unmanned aircraft in relation to other aircraft, people and obstacles for the purpose of avoiding collisions;</li>
</ol>
<p><strong><span style="font-size: 12pt;"></span></strong></p>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0qsj0v644">PART A: GENERAL</h1>
<p>This part contains regulations, general operational policies, company rules, instructions and procedures needed for a safe operation.</p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1eulg7o4775"><div class="page-break"></div>Chapter A1: ORGANISATION OVERVIEW <span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[OE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_GgYPgRxcp2NSKjE7sV4q" class="not_editable" data-id="GgYPgRxcp2NSKjE7sV4q">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="GgYPgRxcp2NSKjE7sV4q" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddh6"><span class="shortcode">[A1.0]</span> <span class="name">About [OPERATOR]</span></h2>
</article>
<p>At 2D Property Managemet B.V. we bring property management to a higher level with our service SkyInspect, which uses innovative technology for digital real estate mapping with the use of unmanned aircrafts. Our 3d solutions provide a realistic view of building, brick by brick, ensuring a more efficient working process and cost savings.</p>
<p>Additionally we make reports of our inspections which enable the customer to take decisions about maintenance and preventive repairs based on actual data.</p>
<p><br>Also [OPERATOR] offers mold and moisture inspections, heat loss observations and leakage detection.</p>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="EEzZFaYTAcK05TAImxp1" id="article_EEzZFaYTAcK05TAImxp1">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="EEzZFaYTAcK05TAImxp1" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7023b"><span class="shortcode">[A1.1A]</span> <span class="name">Organisation</span></h2>
<p>The organisation structure of [OPERATOR]:</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/dronestart-production.appspot.com/o/images%2Fgeneral%2FOrganisation%20zonder%20SM.png?alt=media&amp;token=2b1f8f08-e0d1-42e7-a54f-872d99c11d31" alt="" width="409"></p>
<p>&nbsp;All the nominated individuals or crew members will be listed in <a href="#article_DGaYAYQkBmuFlirHDROk">[APPENDIX A] CONTACT INFORMATION OF CREW MEMBER</a>.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="lsnjHF0bIU8lLHkcBjWF" id="article_lsnjHF0bIU8lLHkcBjWF">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="lsnjHF0bIU8lLHkcBjWF" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7023c"><span class="shortcode">[A1.2A]</span> <span class="name">Responsibilities and Duties</span></h2>
<p><strong><u>UAS Operator/ACCOUNTABLE MANAGER</u></strong></p>
<h4>Responsibilities</h4>
<ol>
<li>Ensure compliance with the conditions outlined in the operational authorisation issued by the competent authority.</li>
<li>Establish and maintain a safety management system to monitor, report, and mitigate risks associated with UAS operations.</li>
<li>Conduct comprehensive risk assessments for UAS operations and implement necessary mitigations.</li>
<li>Ensure that all remote UAS pilots are adequately trained and possess the required competencies.</li>
<li>Ensure adherence to all applicable regulations and operational procedures specific to the Specific Category.</li>
<li>Develop and implement procedures for reporting incidents, accidents, and safety-related issues to relevant authorities.</li>
<li>Ensure all UAS equipment is maintained according to the manufacturer's guidelines and operational requirements.</li>
<li>Maintain effective communication with relevant air traffic service units and stakeholders regarding operational plans and any changes during flights.</li>
<li>Manage personnel and operational resources effectively to support safe UAS operations.</li>
<li>Ensure the safety of the UAS operations of [OPERATOR].</li>
<li>Establish and maintain an effective management system.</li>
</ol>
<h4>Duties</h4>
<ol>
<li>Develop and implement operational procedures to ensure safe and efficient UAS operations.</li>
<li>Oversee UAS operations to ensure compliance with operational authorisations and safety protocols.</li>
<li>Maintain accurate records in UAS logbooks documenting all operational flights, incidents, and maintenance activities.</li>
<li>Ensure that operators are familiar with geographical and airspace restrictions applicable to their operations.</li>
<li>Allocate financial resources for the safe execution of operations and maintenance.</li>
<li>Update and communicate the operations manual and its appendices.</li>
<li>Inform crew members of the changes related to their position(s).</li>
<li>Ensure that every flight is carried out according to the procedures of the operations manual.</li>
<li>Provide UAS that is suitable and approved for the planned operations.</li>
<li>Provide sufficient and skilled manpower for the flights that are conducted.</li>
<li>Create a "just culture" in the organisation.</li>
<li>Be the contact person for the authorities and inform them of changes to the operations manual.</li>
<li>Appoint crew members and the commander of the mission.</li>
<li>Maintain the operations manual and, if necessary, suspend crew members who do not comply with the procedures.</li>
<li>Approve flights.</li>
<li>Manage the yearly inspection of the UAS equipment to ensure that it meets the legal requirements.</li>
<li>Supervise reports of incidents and/or accidents.</li>
<li>Purchase equipment for safe flight and/or maintenance.</li>
<li>Annually, the Accountable Manager checks the equipment for the UAS operations to ensure they meet the legally set requirements.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong></strong></p>
<p><strong><u>FLIGHT OPERATIONS MANAGER / REMOTE PILOT IN COMMAND</u></strong></p>
<p><strong>Responsibilities</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Ensuring the safe operation of the UAS system.</li>
<li>Ensuring the safety of all flight crew involved in UAS operations.</li>
<li>Having the appropriate remote pilot competency as defined in the operational authorisation.</li>
<li>Verifying compliance with geographical zones.</li>
<li>Ensuring direct remote identification is active and up-to-date, if applicable.</li>
<li>Avoid collision risks with other aircraft and discontinue the flight if necessary.</li>
<li>Familiarity with environmental and electromagnetic conditions that may impact safe operation.</li>
<li>Complying with specific operational limitations and conditions in the authorisation.</li>
<li>Verifying weather compatibility with operational and manufacturer requirements before and during the operation.</li>
<li>Reporting incidents and/or accidents to the Safety Manager and Accountable Manager.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Duties</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Being familiar with UAS manufacturer’s instructions.</li>
<li>Executing safe UAS flights according to the operations manual and pre-flight safety briefing.</li>
<li>Inspecting UAS construction and other operational equipment for safe use.</li>
<li>Considering specific field circumstances (e.g., terrain, obstacles, and environmental factors).</li>
<li>Conducting surveillance of the entire operation and all operational staff.</li>
<li>Keeping a personal logbook and UAS logbook up to date.</li>
<li>Checking the UAS on firmware updates or geo location updates before flight</li>
</ul>
<p><strong><u>VISUAL OBSERVER</u></strong></p>
<p><strong>Responsibilities</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Scanning the skies, the ground and the weather to identify potential hazards and notify the pilot of those hazards as they arise;</li>
<li>Communicating with the pilot about crucial information needed to ensure the safe operation of the drone.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Duties</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Keeping the UAS within sight;</li>
<li>Ensures that the maximum range of the radio connection is not exceeded between the pilot and the UAS during the operation;</li>
<li>Supporting the operation on location;</li>
<li>Performing emergency procedures if necessary.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong><u>MANAGER TRAINING</u></strong></p>
<p><strong>Responsibilities</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Training of the operational crew;</li>
<li>Ensuring that the training is carried out following the requirements of the aviation authority and the operations manual.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Duties</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Developing training programs;</li>
<li>Organising the training of new crew members;</li>
<li>Organising refresher courses if necessary;</li>
<li>Keeping a record of the training the crew members participated in.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong><u>MAINTENANCE MANAGER</u></strong></p>
<p><strong>Responsibilities</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Maintenance of the UAS;</li>
<li>Ensuring that the maintenance is carried out according to the requirements of the aviation authority and the operations manual.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Duties</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Developing a UAS maintenance program that complied with the requirements of the authority and the operations manual;&nbsp;</li>
<li>Implementing the maintenance program;</li>
<li>Testing the functioning of the UAS after the maintenance;</li>
<li>Updating maintenance logbook.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<ul style="margin-top: 0cm;" type="disc"></ul>
<p></p>
<h2 id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7023d">[A1.3] The role of the Safety Manager</h2>
<p>The role of the Safety Manager at&nbsp; [OPERATOR] is combined with the Accountable Manager.</p>
<p></p>
<article id="article_qjNIAh22LqCTaXsT7LBN" class="not_editable" data-id="qjNIAh22LqCTaXsT7LBN">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="qjNIAh22LqCTaXsT7LBN" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddh9"><span class="shortcode">[A1.4]</span> <span class="name">Crew Formation </span></h2>
<div class="page" title="Page 21">
<div class="section">
<div class="layoutArea">
<div class="column">
<p>Assignments can be categorised by their complexity. Depending on the complexity, an assignment can be performed alone or as a team. The complexity is linked to the flying situation and the type of operation.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Low-Complexity Open Category assignments</span></strong></p>
<p>[OPERATOR] flies within the restrictions of the Open Category, unless the specific operation with the specific UAS cannot be flown within these restrictions.&nbsp;</p>
<p>For Specific Category Flights, three categories apply; Low, Medium and High</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Low-complexity Specific Category assignments (solo operations)</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Low-complexity assignments are in circumstances where hardly any risks are recognized for machines, people and the surroundings. Examples of such situations are:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Flying rural areas/farms/fields without special objects/people within a radius of 100 meters from the start and landing area;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Objects where no people, who are not involved in the assignments, are present during the operation.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The operations that fall under low complexity are taking photos and video recordings and simple inspections. Such assignments often involve nothing more than just taking a few photos of an object. The following pre-conditions apply:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The horizontal distance between the pilot and the drone will not exceed 150 meters;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The maximum flight height may not exceed 80 meters AGL (Above Ground Level);</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">All scores of the risk analysis during flight preparation are lower than 12 (or 1A-1E, 2D, 2E, 3E) = green in risk analyses in Operational Plan in appendix C1);</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">No flying in a low-flying area that is active;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">There are no active NOTAMs for the flying area for that moment;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Wind force not higher than 5 (Beaufort);</span></span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In the case of a solo flight, the pilot is also responsible for completing the checklists.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">With a team of a pilot and an observer, it is possible to fly in all types of circumstances and all types of assignments where there are no non-mitigable risks for a machine, people and surroundings.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Average complexity of assignments (team)</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">These assignments have a relatively simple flight plan and the complexity, in this case, depends on the circumstances. Examples are as follows:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Flying &lt;25 meters other than the object to be inspected;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Flying in active low-flying areas and or CTRs (if allowed).</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">For assignments with an average complexity, the minimum crew formation for the flight operation is 2 people, namely a pilot and an observer. Conducting an operation without this minimum condition is not possible.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Depending on the situation, several observers and/or a payload operator can also be deployed. The requirement for the extra member(s) can be led from the risk analysis as a mitigating measure.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">High complexity assignments (team)</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">An assignment with high complexity is in a circumstance where there is a higher risk for machines, people and the surroundings and/or a complex flight plan. The following preconditions apply to these operations:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Accountable manager approval is required;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Several observers (ground) are needed.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In situations, where the safety of people who are not directly related to the flight operation, additional observers will be deployed. Think of flying at factory sites that are operational at that time or places where there is public access to the flying area via several places.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Several observers may be required in this type of assignment. The number is defined in the Operational Plan.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Factors considered in determining the number of observers include:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The complexity of the area. There are places where uninvolved people could come that should be kept at a distance during the flight. In that case, an observer is required, so that he/she could immediately alert the pilot.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">There are (multiple) objects in the flight area that need to be monitored by an observer.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Flying in a low-flying area or low-flying route.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The above list is by no means exhaustive; combinations of these examples require several observers. The rule is that every possible risk must be identified and addressed. Sometimes this is possible with two observers and in other cases more observers may be needed to mitigate the identified risks.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">A payload operator is only needed if the control of the payload must be separate from the flight movements and where this is not automated.</span></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Further Reading Section</span></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="#article_uqTYOzBs5H0TDKNaAl0f">[B2.2] External System</a></li>
<li><a href="#article_1H6NEQoeBlKjM7FSzLcq">[B2.5] Pre-flight Preparation and Checklists VLOS flights</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</article>

<article class="not_editable" data-id="yGwSrU9QzBdsDusoa9Eg" id="article_yGwSrU9QzBdsDusoa9Eg">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="yGwSrU9QzBdsDusoa9Eg" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7023e"><span class="shortcode">[A1.5]</span> <span class="name">Role of the Pilot in Command (PIC) </span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Calibri Light'; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">If there are two or more available remote pilots at the location, one pilot is designated as the remote pilot in command (RPIC). The RPIC<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<div class="page" title="Page 22">
<div class="section">
<div class="layoutArea">
<div class="column">
<ul>
<li>is directly responsible for and is the ultimate authority as to the operation of the UAS;</li>
<li>ensures that the UAS complies with all applicable regulations of the Operations manual.</li>
<li>has final authority during flight operations and cancels or postpones the flight if:
<ul>
<li>the safety of persons is endangered;</li>
<li>property on the ground is endangered;</li>
<li>other airspace users are endangered;</li>
<li>the terms of the operating permit are violated.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>is allowed to deviate from the regulations if the circumstances do not guarantee the safety of the operation. Deviations will be noted in the Operational Plan.</li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1eulg7o4775">Chapter A2: CONCEPT OF OPERATIONS<span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[CONEU]</span></h1>
<article id="article_Pd6qKVrwZFAkLLS2JU8k" class="not_editable" data-id="Pd6qKVrwZFAkLLS2JU8k">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="Pd6qKVrwZFAkLLS2JU8k" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddha"><span class="shortcode">[A2.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Concept of Operations (ConOps)</span></h2>
<p>In this chapter, a brief overview is given of the ConOps of [OPERATOR]. For the structure of the OM jump to <a href="#article_XXx29bCFtRlCP3APOTnr">Introduction</a>.</p>
</article>
<p class="MsoNormal">The main purpose of unmanned aircrafts for [OPERATOR] is to inspect properties in the Netherlands. Because inspections are generally commissioned by the owners or for example companies that are charged with maintaining buildings or making renovation plans the people in or nearby the property are part of the operation and can be easily instructed about possible risks.<o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Furthermore the main pilot of [OPERATOR], Danny Dijkshoorn, is an experienced, fully certified drone pilot. To make sure that operations are carried out safely [OPERATOR] uses this manual to make sure operations are carried out responsibly.<o:p></o:p></p>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1eulg7o4776">Chapter A3: STANDARD QUALIFICATIONS OF CREW&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[NIBE]</span><b></b></h1>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="BgcU6i63lZEhHfTHRnF2" id="article_BgcU6i63lZEhHfTHRnF2">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="BgcU6i63lZEhHfTHRnF2"><span class="shortcode">[A3.1P]</span> <span class="name">Crew Qualification</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">A pilot who conducts the flight operations according to PDRA-S01 for [OPERATOR] shall:<o:p></o:p></p>
<ul style="margin-top: 0cm;" type="disc">
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;">Be at least 18 years;</li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;">Have<o:p></o:p> A1-A3 and A2 certificates (OPEN);</li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;">Hold a certificate of remote pilot theoretical knowledge, in accordance with Attachment A to Chapter I of Appendix 1 to the Annex to the UAS Regulation, which is issued by the competent authority or by an entity that is designated by the competent authority of a Member State;&nbsp;</li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;">Hold an accreditation of completion of a practical-skills training course for this PDRA, in accordance with Attachment A to Chapter I of Appendix 1 to the Annex to the UAS Regulation, which is issued by:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type: none;">
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<li class="MsoNormal">an entity that has declared compliance with the requirements of Appendix 3 to the Annex to the UAS Regulation and is recognised by the competent authority of a Member State.<o:p></o:p></li>
</ol>
</li>
</ol>
<ul style="margin-top: 0cm;" type="disc">
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;">Have followed additional training for the specific procedures for the intended UAS operation.<o:p></o:p></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;">Use a (digital) flight logbook.<o:p></o:p></li>
</ul>
<p data-start="57" data-end="96"><strong data-start="57" data-end="96">Qualification of Other Crew Members</strong></p>
<p data-start="98" data-end="634">To take part in an operation, the remaining flight crew of [OPERATOR] must have the required basic knowledge to operate UAS and must be familiar with current procedures, laws and regulations, emergency procedures, and technical capabilities.<br data-start="339" data-end="342">In addition, the flight crew must be current at all times, meaning they must be able to provide proof of recent practical experience and/or successfully completed training modules.<br data-start="522" data-end="525">An initial training and/or briefing (the level of training depends on the role) is required; see also [D2.1].</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">A (visual) UAS-observer shall be at least 16 years old and must be able to see the UAS and scan its surroundings for potential collision hazards. Also, he or she must be able to readily communicate with the pilot.<o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><b>Remote Pilot additional requirements&nbsp;</b><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Before the first commercial operation, the pilot has at least 1 training session with an observer.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><strong>Recurrency</strong></p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal">At least 3 T/O's and landings in the last 3 months (90d).</li>
<li class="MsoNormal">At least 2 hrs flight-time in a year for a minimum of 6 flights on 6 different days. Record by pilot in aircraft and pilot log.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p><b></b></p>
<article id="article_U8QokLqkpaHSPBQWuvaK" class="not_editable" data-id="U8QokLqkpaHSPBQWuvaK">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="U8QokLqkpaHSPBQWuvaK"><span class="shortcode">[A3.2]</span> <span class="name">Currency Requirements for Flight Crew </span></h2>
<p class="p1">To stay current, the crew members of [OPERATOR] shall be trained annually:</p>
<p class="p1"><strong>Theoretical part </strong></p>
<p class="p1">For all operational crew members, it consists of theoretical knowledge of procedures, regulations and responsibilities regarding operations as described in this operations manual, at least once a year.</p>
<p class="p1"><strong>Safety part </strong></p>
<p class="p1">All operational crew members will attend a safety workshop. During this workshop, all safety procedures will be reviewed. This will take place at least once a year.</p>
<p class="p1"><strong>Practical part </strong></p>
<p>All operational crew members must participate in at least one training per year. Additionally, yearly recurrent training is required, covering the following subjects:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Emergency Response Plan</li>
<li>Multi-Crew Coordination, including communication with ATC</li>
<li>Testing abnormal and emergency procedures</li>
<li>Identification of critical environmental conditions</li>
<li>Human error recognition and management</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_N727TboG7bFioXjBJvBg" class="not_editable" data-id="N727TboG7bFioXjBJvBg">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fl6mjmj22d0b" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="N727TboG7bFioXjBJvBg"><span class="shortcode">[A3.3]</span> <span class="name">Alcohol Consumption </span></h2>
<p>The Dutch regulations prohibit drinking alcohol ten hours before duty or flying with a blood alcohol concentration greater than 0,2 mg of alcohol per millilitre of blood or a breath alcohol concentration of 90 μg per litre of exhaled air or higher.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_Y0NJJgh3i5zasBwfbQH4" class="not_editable" data-id="Y0NJJgh3i5zasBwfbQH4">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="Y0NJJgh3i5zasBwfbQH4" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7023h"><span class="shortcode">[A3.4]</span> <span class="name">Physiological aspects (IMSAFE)</span></h2>
<p>In the Dutch aviation law (<a href="https://wetten.overheid.nl/jci1.3:c:BWBR0005555&amp;hoofdstuk=2&amp;titeldeel=2.2&amp;artikel=2.11&amp;z=2021-01-01&amp;g=2021-01-01">Artikel 2.11 Wet Luchtvaart</a>) it is stated:</p>
<p>The holder of a license or certificate of equivalence is prohibited from performing activities for which that license entitles the holder to undertake due to their physical or mental condition, which endangers the safety of air traffic or could endanger it.</p>
<p><strong>General Aspect</strong></p>
<p>The good health of the flight crew is of great importance for the good process and flight safety.</p>
<p><strong>Good Airmanship</strong></p>
<p>Airmanship is defined as:</p>
<ul>
<li>A sound acquaintance with the principles of flight;</li>
<li>The ability to operate an aeroplane with competence and precision both on the ground and in the air;</li>
<li>The exercise of sound judgment that results in optimal operational safety and efficiency.</li>
</ul>
<p>The crew can use the&nbsp;<strong>IMSAFE</strong>&nbsp;checklist.&nbsp;<strong>IMSAFE&nbsp;</strong>stands for:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong><em>I</em></strong><em>llness: A</em>re you currently sick or have you been recently?</li>
<li><strong><em>M</em></strong><em>edication: A</em>re you taking prescription or over-the-counter medications?</li>
<li><strong><em>S</em></strong><em>tress: A</em>re you experiencing psychological pressure or anxiety?</li>
<li><strong><em>A</em></strong><em>lcohol: W</em>hen did you last consume alcohol, or are you hungover?</li>
<li><strong><em>F</em></strong><em>atigue: A</em>re you exhausted or overtired? When did you last eat?</li>
<li><strong><em>E</em></strong><em>motion: A</em>re you upset about anything?&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
<p>When one of the answers is yes, a pilot or a visual observer should not conduct a flight or start a series of flights. In addition, the crew should contact their Accountable Manager to request a substitute and/or reschedule the operation.</p>
<p><strong>Health</strong></p>
<p>Being free from illness or injury is crucial to executing safe flights. For the crew members, preparing or conducting any flight activities is prohibited:</p>
<ul></ul>
<ul>
<li>When under the influence of substances that influence his judgment and reactions.</li>
<li>When having consumed alcoholic beverages in the previous 10 hours.</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Wearing corrective glasses or lenses</span></p>
<p>A pilot whose medical record states that he needs corrective glasses or lenses should wear them during the entire flight operation or a series of flight operations.</p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Health Precautions</span></p>
<p>Utilising the following substances by the crew is strictly prohibited:</p>
<ul>
<li>Alcohol;</li>
<li>Drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Utilising the following substances by the crew is prohibited unless a doctor and the Accountable Manager approve this:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sleep aid supplements such as Melatonin;</li>
<li>Medicines that are both on prescription and not on a prescription that could influence his judgement or reaction time, such as:&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>Antibiotics</li>
<li>Painkiller</li>
<li>Antihistamine</li>
<li>Decongestant</li>
<li>Cough suppressants with antihistamines or decongestants</li>
<li>Stimulant</li>
<li>Any medicines or substances not stated above are prohibited if they influence his behaviour, ability of judgement, sight, hearing or balance. If you, as a crew, doubt your capability to conduct the activities due to the medicine you take, you should seek the advice of a qualified health professional.</li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p><span>The accountable manager has the final authority to decide if the operation can be conducted.</span></p>
<p>The Attitudes</p>
<p>Attitude affects the quality of aeronautical decision-making. Studies have identified five hazardous attitudes that can interfere with the ability to make sound decisions and exercise authority properly. These are <span style="text-decoration: underline;">five hazardous attitudes and antidotes</span>.&nbsp;</p>
<table border="1" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 99.6222%;">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="width: 65.3266%; text-align: center;"><strong>The Five Hazardous Attitudes</strong></td>
<td style="width: 31.0626%; text-align: center;"><strong>Antidote</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 65.3266%;"><strong>Anti-authority: “Don’t tell me.”</strong> This attitude is found in people who do not like anyone telling them what to do. In a sense, they are saying, “No one can tell me what to do.” They may resent having someone tell them what to do or regard rules, regulations, and procedures as silly or unnecessary. However, it is always your privilege to question authority if you feel it is in error.</td>
<td style="width: 31.0626%;">
<p>You are within your rights to question authority if you think it is incorrect. Talk to the Accountable Manager. No hearing? The second step is to let the Safety Manager know your doubts.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 65.3266%;"><strong>Impulsivity: “Do it quickly.” </strong>This is the attitude of people who frequently feel the need to do something, anything, immediately. They do not stop to think about what they are about to do, do not select the best alternative, and do the first thing that comes to mind.</td>
<td style="width: 31.0626%;">Create a timeout just before the start of the operation and use the checklists from the handbook.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 65.3266%;"><strong><strong>Invulnerability: “It won’t happen to me.” </strong></strong>Many people falsely believe that accidents happen to others, but never to them. They know accidents can happen and that anyone can be affected. However, they never really feel or believe they will be personally involved. Pilots who think this way are likelier to take chances and increase risk.</td>
<td style="width: 31.0626%;">Speak to the other person if he or she shows unsafe behaviour because you want to prove your point and report an incident to the Accountable Manager and the Safety Officer.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 65.3266%;"><strong>Macho: “I can do it.” </strong>Pilots are always trying to prove that they are better than anyone else thinks, “I can do it—I'll show them.” Pilots with this attitude will try to prove themselves by taking risks to impress others. While this pattern is considered a male characteristic, women are equally susceptible.</td>
<td style="width: 31.0626%;">Make a flight plan and agree to adhere to the limits and agreements in the plan. Speak to the other person if he or she shows unsafe behaviour because of the urge to prove. Report an incident to the Accountable Manager and the Safety Officer.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 65.3266%;"><strong><strong>Resignation: “What’s the use?” </strong></strong>Pilots who think, “What’s the use?” do not see themselves able to make a great deal of difference in what happens to them. When things go well, the pilot will likely think it is good luck. When things go badly, the pilot may feel that someone is out to get them or attribute it to bad luck. The pilot will leave the action to others, for better or worse. Sometimes, such pilots will even go along with unreasonable requests just to be a "nice guy."</td>
<td style="width: 31.0626%;">Could you talk to the pilot about maintaining the flight plan and keeping the goal in mind?</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>
<p></p>
