<h1 id="mcetoc_1ev2fe0te2hk"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1evf2a54ts0"><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Chapter A4: SAFETY MANAGEMENT SYSTEM<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[VMSE]</span></span></strong></h1>
<article id="article_tc84v11X3umExLF124lK" class="not_editable" data-id="tc84v11X3umExLF124lK">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="tc84v11X3umExLF124lK" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddhd"><span class="shortcode">[A4.1]</span> <span class="name">Safety Policy Objective</span></h2>
<p>[OPERATOR] pursues a policy aimed at preventing avoidable accidents.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_WrgfR3N4xpYazrRk50Px" class="not_editable" data-id="WrgfR3N4xpYazrRk50Px">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="WrgfR3N4xpYazrRk50Px" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddhe"><span class="shortcode">[A4.2]</span> <span class="name">Safety Culture</span></h2>
<p>[OPERATOR] strives for a corporate culture in which all crew members dare to be vulnerable. Making mistakes is human and more often than we are aware of. Structure and procedures notably overcome the consequences of these errors, but unfortunately, they are never perfect. Improving safety is a continuous process.</p>
<p>Information is required to implement improvements. The management of [OPERATOR] depends on its crew to obtain this information. They should feel free to report incidents without fear. Declaring “zero tolerance” (not allowed to make mistakes) applicable is not part of an open corporate culture and certainly not in aviation. It suggests that crew should not make mistakes and that procedures are always perfect for every thinkable situation. On the contrary, there are circumstances conceivable under which crew must deviate from the standard procedures.</p>
<p>It is important the crew feels free enough to share information. The accountable manager contributes to a "just culture" that will never punish the reporting of incidents. Of course, intentional violation of rules, other than for security reasons, is not included.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_ME8TopExIqtaPvt2Ywoj" class="not_editable" data-id="ME8TopExIqtaPvt2Ywoj">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhmla0m5q" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="ME8TopExIqtaPvt2Ywoj"><span class="shortcode">[A4.3]</span> <span class="name">Reporting Accident </span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Under European Regulation (EU) No. 376/2014, it is mandatory to report all accidents and serious incidents. This obligation also applies to pilots and organizations working with remotely piloted aircraft. See chapter </span><a href="#article_V28zgwoWrmKWuTmVRuFo">[A11.1] Reporting Procedures</a></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_tWu1PZ4euQPqbxdfyUmi" class="not_editable" data-id="tWu1PZ4euQPqbxdfyUmi">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="tWu1PZ4euQPqbxdfyUmi" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7123i"><span class="shortcode">[A4.4]</span> <span class="name">Safety Assurance</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">At least annually, incidents, accidents, occurrences, procedures and tasks and responsibilities are checked according to Deming's PDCA circle, Plan Do Check Act. The next steps are as follows:<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<ol style="margin-top: 0cm;" start="1" type="1">
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Schedule an annual appointment between the safety officer and the accountable manager.<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Planning training once a year with the flight crew, in which all possible incidents, accidents and the subsequent procedures and course of action are taken into account.<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Reporting of both activities.<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Annual evaluation between the safety officer and the accountable manager (can be combined with point 1 in small organisations). As soon as more than 100 flight hours are made per year, this frequency is increased to every two years.<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Implementing points for improvement in the organisation: safeguarding agreements, manuals and other internal procedures.<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Distribute the feedback for improvement and agreements within the organisation of [OPERATOR].<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">If necessary, adjustments to procedures in the manual will be processed and communicated internally. Then, they should be presented to ILT.<o:p></o:p></span></li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0g9fsrk20">Chapter A5: CREW COMMUNICATION <span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[CCE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_3rSPRcOG8DrY1ZdvT3O4" class="not_editable" data-id="3rSPRcOG8DrY1ZdvT3O4">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="3rSPRcOG8DrY1ZdvT3O4" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddhg"><span class="shortcode">[A5.1]</span> <span class="name">Cooperation in General</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Making mistakes is human and we make mistakes. Making mistakes happens more often than we think. Sometimes we make mistakes that we are immediately aware of, but the worst are the mistakes that we are not (yet) aware of. Effective communication plays an important role in this. 100% effective communication is when communication is complete and not filtered by emotions. By translating emotion into words of the compiler, mistakes arise. Errors also arise during the transmission and subsequent translation of words into emotion by the receiver. Choosing words is always from a (limited) perspective that is never the same as that of the receiver.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Crew members of [OPERATOR] should make the following task distributions and arrangements of communication during the flight.</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Pilot: The person designated by the UAS operator who operates the UAS during a flight.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Airspace Observer: The person who assists the pilot by performing unaided visual scanning of the airspace in whcih the UA is operating for any potential hazard in the air.</span></li>
<li>Unmanned Aircraft Observer: The person who is positioned alongside the pilot. This person, by unaided visual observation of the UA, assists the pilot in keeping the UA in VLOS and safely conducting the flight. The UA observer handles all matters around the operation (dealing with viewers, traffic, etc.).</li>
<li>Payload Operator: Operates the payload of the UAS and ensures the correct settings.</li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Depending on the scale of the assignment, several observers are assigned to coordinate traffic or maintain communication.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">To limit errors as much as possible, it is important to agree on how [OPERATOR] flight crew work together. Who does what, how and when? How do we speak clearly to each other? And how do we ensure that troublesome elements have as little effect as possible on our cooperation?</span></p>
<p>For the next two sections, general directions of cooperation between the pilot and the observer are described.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_tP6Z8NeZDRzP1K5m42J6" class="not_editable" data-id="tP6Z8NeZDRzP1K5m42J6">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="tP6Z8NeZDRzP1K5m42J6" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddhh"><span class="shortcode">[A5.2.1]</span> <span class="name">Cooperation Pilot/Observer</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">During the cooperation between a pilot and the observer(s) on location, communication must be mutually efficient and goal-oriented. We apply the following rules to streamline communication:</span></p>
<ul>
<li>The pilot is flying and in charge of UAS-related matters, all other tasks during the flight are assigned to the observer(s).</li>
<li>We speak of left / right from the pilot's point of view.</li>
<li>There is an appropriate response to risks to avoid a possible shock reaction.</li>
<li>The pilot and observer remain within speaking distance of each other unless additional communication technology can be used.</li>
</ul>
<p>During the flight phases, [OPERATOR] uses the following phraseology:</p>
<p><em>Prior to take-off:</em></p>
<ul>
<li>UAS pilot: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “READY FOR TAKE-OFF”</li>
<li>observer:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;“CHECK, FLY ZONE IS CLEAR”</li>
<li>UAS pilot:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “TAKING OFF”</li>
</ul>
<p><em>Or when the flight cannot be started:&nbsp;</em></p>
<ul>
<li>UAS pilot: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “READY FOR TAKE-OFF”</li>
<li>observer:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; “CHECK, FLY ZONE IS NOT CLEAR”</li>
<li>UAS pilot:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “ABORT MISSION”</li>
</ul>
<p><em>Landing</em></p>
<ul>
<li>UAS pilot: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “observer READY FOR LANDING?”</li>
<li>observer:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; “LANDING CONFIRMED”</li>
</ul>
<p>If all crew members agree, the UAS pilot initiates the landing and lands the UAS on the landing zone (LZ).</p>
<p><em>Or when it is not possible to land:</em></p>
<ul>
<li>UAS pilot: &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “observer, READY FOR LANDING?”</li>
<li>observer:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;“STANDBY, LANDING ZONE NOT CLEAR”</li>
<li>UAS pilot:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “STANDING BY"&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
<p><em>Crash</em></p>
<p>In case of a crash:</p>
<ul>
<li>Crew:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;“CRASH, CRASH, CRASH</li>
</ul>
<p>Emergency procedure unexpected low battery</p>
<ul>
<li>UAS pilot:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;“EMERGENCY, LOW BATTERY”</li>
<li>observer:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; “EMERGENCY, CLEARING LANDING AREA or “EMERGENCY, LANDING AREA IS CLEAR”</li>
</ul>
<p>Other air traffic</p>
<ul>
<li>observer:&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;“INTRUDER, AIRCRAFT (HELICOPTER) AT NORTH/SOUTH/WEST/EAST</li>
<li>UAS pilot:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; “TRAFFIC INSIGHT"</li>
</ul>
<p>See <a href="#article_47consH3pQ76mhQ7I0Q6">OM C4.5</a> for avoiding conflicts with other airspace users (deconfliction scheme).</p>
</article>
<p><br><span data-preserver-spaces="true"></span></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="j4oW3RnofrKkPMzGnpJC" id="article_j4oW3RnofrKkPMzGnpJC">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="j4oW3RnofrKkPMzGnpJC" id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiincr"><span class="shortcode">[A5.2.3]</span> <span class="name">Communication systems</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Communication beyond speaking distance between a pilot and one observer will take place via a mobile telephone connection with an earpiece or two-way radio with headsets. With these equipment </span><span data-preserver-spaces="true">the UAS pilot does not have to detach his hands from the controls and can open the connection automatically by speaking.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">More observers</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">If there are more observers, two-way radio or walkie talkies are used. So that one person communicates with multiple people at the same time.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><strong>Deterioration of external systems</strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true"></span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">If the cell phone network goes down and cell phones are not working, two-way radios are used as a means of communication.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">If one or more walkie-talkies fail, cell phones will be used. The communications plan includes all phone numbers of those involved.&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="3JXUgShgeEqCZaDAp1zd" id="article_3JXUgShgeEqCZaDAp1zd">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="3JXUgShgeEqCZaDAp1zd" id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiincs"><span class="shortcode">[A5.3]</span> <span class="name">Loss of communication between Pilot/Observer</span></h2>
<p>In the event of a loss of communication between the pilot and the observer(s):</p>
<table border="1" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; height: 63.1718px; border-width: 1px;"><colgroup><col style="width: 20.2356%;"><col style="width: 64.9973%;"><col style="width: 14.8067%;"></colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 18.3906px;">
<td style="height: 18.3906px;"><strong>Issue /event</strong></td>
<td style="height: 18.3906px;"><strong>Mitigation(s)</strong></td>
<td style="height: 18.3906px;"><strong>Actor(s)</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 22.3906px;">
<td style="height: 22.3906px;">Loss of communication between the pilot and the observer(s)</td>
<td style="height: 22.3906px;">
<ul>
<li>Pause operation immediately</li>
<li>If possible, hover UA in position until communication can be resumed</li>
<li>If not successful within 10 to 15 seconds, fly the UA to the landing area to restore communication and/or start the landing procedure from here</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="height: 22.3906px;">Pilot</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0r59arqcf4">Chapter A6: NORMAL OPERATION STRATEGY<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[SE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_5kbos0KjYadZ16O5q8bI" class="not_editable" data-id="5kbos0KjYadZ16O5q8bI">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="5kbos0KjYadZ16O5q8bI" id="mcetoc_1h4is3ulm108"><span class="shortcode">[A6.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Operation Strategy</span></h2>
<p>Standard procedures contribute to a safe flight process. Above all, these should make clear what is expected of whom; when, how and why? Understanding leads to acceptance.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_RgIn7oZnXihQmxzmmfdi" class="not_editable" data-id="RgIn7oZnXihQmxzmmfdi">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="RgIn7oZnXihQmxzmmfdi"><span class="shortcode">[A6.1]</span> <span class="name">Understanding Normal Operation Strategy</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">In manned aviation, SOPs (Standard Operating Procedures) are used to rule out errors in the operation as much as possible. They are written work instructions that describe in detail how a certain action must be performed to create uniformity in the action and therefore also its result. Aviation is all about safety during the execution of the flight. In principle, this Operations Manual is full of "standard working methods”. <o:p></o:p></span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">The standard working method of [OPERATOR] distinguishes three phases for flight preparation:<o:p></o:p></span><span data-preserver-spaces="true"></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><b><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">Phase 1: Quick Scan Regulations<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">In this step a check is performed to determine whether the flight can take place within the legal possibilities:<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 36.0pt; text-indent: -18.0pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Calibri Light'; mso-fareast-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">The flight takes place during the daylight period, unless [OPERATOR] has CAA-NL exemption for flying outside UDP hours (Uniform Daylight Period (UDP).<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 36.0pt; text-indent: -18.0pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Calibri Light'; mso-fareast-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">The flight takes place at a maximum height of 120 meters (400ft) above the ground or water. N.B.: this does not apply to CTR, low-flying areas and/or (temporary) restricted areas (NOTAM).<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 36.0pt; text-indent: -18.0pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Calibri Light'; mso-fareast-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">The flight takes place in uncontrolled airspace (Classification G) or (C/D when [OPERATOR] has an exemption in the OA.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 36.0pt; text-indent: -18.0pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: 'Calibri Light'; mso-fareast-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">The flight takes place (partly) in the open or specific category. If it is possible to fly the operation entirely in the Open category, that is preferable.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<ul></ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The result of the quick scan is recorded in the first version of the operational plan, see the section&nbsp;<a href="#article_tMIIplfArp05A2EmoKqV">[A7.21] Operational Plan (OP)</a>. This also includes an assignment description.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Phase 2: Assessment of Location and (airspace) Restrictions</span></strong></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">In this step, it is examined whether the Operational Volume at the flight location is suitable for operations. [OPERATOR] determines the Flight Geography, Operational Volume, Contingency Volume and Ground Risk buffer and completes the Flight Plan and Check Lists.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">Among other things, the location concerning obstacles, roads, adjoining buildings, railways, etc. is examined. [OPERATOR] uses the information source from the OM. Additionally, the operator, if possible, will visit the location to assess its current condition.<o:p></o:p></span><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;"><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">[OPERATOR] also checks whether the airspace in which the flight takes place has restrictions that are important for the execution of the flight.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">[OPERATOR] evaluates the area of operations by means of on-site inspections or appropriate appraisals to lower the density of the people at risk (SORA, M1 low). Two possible mitigations:</p>
<ol start="1" type="1">
<li class="MsoListParagraph">Change the time of flight to a quiet time (off-hour).</li>
<li class="MsoListParagraph">Add an observer to keep uninvolved people at a distance.</li>
</ol>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">Furthermore, the adjacent area is reviewed for any known events. [OPERATOR] coordinates with local authorities or event organisers to determine if there are any scheduled public gatherings, events, or activities within the adjacent area. If available, [OPERATOR] consults local event calendars to stay informed.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-ascii-theme-font: major-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: major-latin; mso-bidi-theme-font: major-latin;">In case the adjacent area is expected to have gatherings, [OPERATOR] identifies and plans alternative zones that are free from people, ensuring the flight can proceed safely without encountering crowds.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Phase 3: Flight Preparation on the day of execution</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Before [OPERATOR] leaves for the location, the following items are checked:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The expected horizontal view. In uncontrolled airspace, this must be at least 1500 meters, in CTRs (controlled airspace) at least 5km.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The wind strength. It must be within the limits of the UAS used. See chapter B1 for details.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The temperature. It must be within the limits of the UAS used. See chapter B1 for details.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Is there precipitation (expected)?</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The Kp index. Is it within the limit of less than 5?</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Check for temporary airspace closures at <a href="https://www.lvnl.nl/diensten">https://www.lvnl.nl/diensten</a>.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">A final check of the location takes place at the location itself. These are:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Checking horizontal visibility.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Measuring the wind strength and direction</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Assess the location. Are there any risks that have not yet been included?</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">For this, [OPERATOR] uses the checklist <a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a>.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">When the flight preparation has been completed, the UAS pilot agrees to take off. Before, during and after the flight, the procedures must be followed as described in the section 'Normal Procedures' in this operations manual. Flight data is recorded in the appropriate logs.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Types of Operations</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">If the operation requires additional actions, these are described from 'Peculiar to Single Operation' in the section 'Normal Procedures' in this operational manual. We speak of an increased risk in these special operations. This should be considered during flight preparation.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Emergency procedures</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">To minimize risks, a communication protocol is used during the operation. This means that it is discussed with the entire crew how to act in an emergency. Besides, there is an overview of procedures available at the flight location and available for inspection in the event of an emergency. The procedures are described in 'Contingency Procedures' and 'Emergency Procedures' in this Operations Manual.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Checklists</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Because a flight can only be conducted safely after proper flight preparation, checklists are used for each intended flight or series of flights. The UAS pilot fills in the results of the checklist in the operational plan that is made for each project, see&nbsp;<a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a>.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">These checklists must be completed on location by the pilot to ensure the quality and safety of the operation. The packing checklist must take place before transportation and upon return to the [OPERATOR] location. The other checklists must be completed on-site before the UAS is found to be airworthy. The checklists must be available in hard copy and must be available for every crew member before, during and after the operation.</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_r7UVMhiMEkyV652657SU" class="not_editable" data-id="r7UVMhiMEkyV652657SU">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="r7UVMhiMEkyV652657SU" id="mcetoc_1in3piiddhj"><span class="shortcode">[A6.2]</span> <span class="name">Deviation from the "Normal Operation Strategy"</span></h2>
<p>Sometimes a normal procedure is not available such as <span>sudden wind or bird attack, distraction of outside the OV (like an incident, or sound)</span> In this case, the crew has the freedom to deviate and/or to improvise it.</p>
<p>The crew may deviate from these procedures. [OPERATOR] then appeals to the common sense of and good cooperation between its crew members.</p>
<p>If, during an operation, it is necessary to deviate from the standard working method, it is always the Pilot in Command who makes this decision based on "good airmanship".</p>
<p>Deliberate violation of rules, other than in the interest of safety, is not permitted.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_G6z0hp1Xf5sRhknLCZGO" class="not_editable" data-id="G6z0hp1Xf5sRhknLCZGO">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="G6z0hp1Xf5sRhknLCZGO" id="mcetoc_1h4is3ulm10b"><span class="shortcode">[A6.3]</span> <span class="name">VLOS</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">VLOS stands for Visual Line Of Sight. Flying under VLOS means that the pilot has direct visual contact with UAS without any support.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Sight distance</span></strong></p>
<p>The EU regulation 2019/947 assumes for VLOS operations that the observer is not able to detect other air traffic further than 2 NM. The distance of 2 NM (rounded off to 3700 metres) is not considered a fixed value and will depend to a large extent on atmospheric conditions, dimensions of the UA and other air traffic, speed of approach, altitude etc. The operator must therefore adjust his operations and/or procedures accordingly. <span id="tgtAlignment_0" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">This</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_1" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">can</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_3" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">differ</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_4" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">per</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_5" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">type</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_6" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">(format)</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_7" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">of</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_8" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">UAS.</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_9" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">A</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_10" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">Mavic</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_11" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">can</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_12" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">stay</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_13" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">in</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_14" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">VLOS</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_15" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">for</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_16" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">less</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_17" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">time</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_18" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">than,</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_19" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">for</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_20" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">example,</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_21" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">an</span> <span id="tgtAlignment_22" class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">M300.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The distance between the pilot and the UAS is not limited to a distance, although the UAS should always remain visible to the pilot. There may be circumstances where visibility or communication with the UAS is restricted, such as:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Bright sun</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Objects</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">EM fields</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Size and Type of the UAS</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Dark sky (grey clouds so that the UAS no longer stands out)</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In these circumstances, the maximum distance is equal to the distance at which the UAS is sufficiently visible.</span></p>
<p>The table below "maximum VLOS distances in relation to sight distances" shows the weather conditions under which the operations can be performed:</p>
<table style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100.039%; height: 67.1778px;" border="1">
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 22.3926px;">
<td style="width: 25.041%; text-align: center; height: 22.3926px;">VLOS distance (m)</td>
<td style="width: 25.041%; text-align: center; height: 22.3926px;">Sight distance (m)</td>
<td style="width: 23.3996%; text-align: center; height: 22.3926px;">Cloud base (m)</td>
<td style="width: 26.5559%; text-align: center; height: 22.3926px;">Precipitation (m)</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 22.3926px;">
<td class="td1" style="width: 25.041%; text-align: center;" valign="top">
<p class="p1">≤ 1000</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 25.041%; height: 22.3926px; text-align: center;">5000</td>
<td class="td1" style="width: 23.3996%; text-align: center;" valign="top">
<p class="p1">≥ 1000</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 26.5559%; height: 22.3926px; text-align: center;">No Precipitation</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 22.3926px;">
<td class="td1" style="width: 25.041%; text-align: center;" valign="top">
<p class="p1">&gt; 1000 ≤ 3500</p>
</td>
<td class="td1" style="width: 25.041%; text-align: center;" valign="top">
<p class="p1">10.000</p>
</td>
<td class="td1" style="width: 23.3996%; text-align: center;" valign="top">
<p class="p1">≥ 1500</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 26.5559%; height: 22.3926px; text-align: center;">No chance of precipitation</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Priority rules applied</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Remotely piloted aircraft give way to aeroplanes, helicopters, gliders, free balloons and airships by descending as quickly as possible.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In the case where two aircraft are encountering at or about the same flight level and lowering is not an option anymore, keep right (in the flying direction).</span></p>
</article>
<p><span style="background-color: #e67e23;"></span></p>
<article id="article_iBubAHcFLAEsZrxb2cnZ" class="not_editable" data-id="iBubAHcFLAEsZrxb2cnZ">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="iBubAHcFLAEsZrxb2cnZ" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7123k"><span class="shortcode">[A6.4P]</span> <span class="name">Determination of the Operational Volume PDRA-S01</span></h2>
<p>Part of the flight preparation is determining the Operational Volume (OV). The Operational Volume consists of a 'Flight Geography' and a 'Contingency Volume'. In addition to these two areas, the Ground Risk Buffer and the Air Risk Buffer must also be determined during flight preparation. The required volume is examined and described in the Operational Plan.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FGround%20Risk%20Model%20and%20Operational%20Volume.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=d1c85637-790e-4427-a629-f6b925bc91a8" alt="" width="365"></p>
<p>When determining the Operational Volume according to PDRA-S01, specific accounts must be taken of:</p>
<ol>
<li>The extent to which the UA can hold its position (accuracy)</li>
<li>The technical inaccuracies regarding the flight path (map errors on the HMI)</li>
<li>Latency</li>
</ol>
<p><span>[OPERATOR] uses the Hovering Accuracy Range and Latency specifications in the manual of the UA.</span></p>
<h4><strong>A6.4P.1 Flight Geography</strong></h4>
<p>An area of ​​flight geography is the projection of a flight area onto the Earth's surface and the spatially and temporally defined airspace volume(s) in which the pilot intends to operate by the normal procedures described in this Operations Manual. The following points should be considered while determining the flight geography:</p>
<ol>
<li>The required maximum height for the operation. Depending on the zones in which the flight or series of flights are operated, [OPERATOR] verifies the geozone in order not to invade controlled airspace or regulated airspace (defined via a geozone).&nbsp;</li>
<li>The UA shall not exceed the maximum flight altitude specified. The maximum height for PDRA-S01 is 150 meters (Flight geography is 120 m, and contingency volume is 30 m. This results in a 150 m flight volume).</li>
<li>The maximum distance between pilot, observer and UAS shall be as short as possible and always comply with the legal requirements described in the chapter air traffic rules, insofar as they have not been modified by law.</li>
<li>The required volume is examined and described in the operational flight plan: see <a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[Appendix C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a>.</li>
</ol>
<h4><strong>A6.4P.2 Contingency volume</strong></h4>
<p>The contingency volume is the zone for unforeseen circumstances. During flight preparation, [OPERATOR] shall consider a contingency volume. The size of the contingency volume depends on several factors, including the speed of the drone, GNSS accuracy error, map error, and others.</p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Calculation of the contingency volume</span></p>
<p>Contingency Volume Lateral</p>
<p>The parameters are shown below.</p>
<ul>
<li>GPS Inaccuracy (S<sub>GPS</sub>): 3 meters</li>
<li>Position Holding Error (S<sub>POS</sub>): 3 meters</li>
<li>Map Error (S<sub>M</sub>): 1 meter</li>
<li>Maximum speed of Drone: V<sub>0</sub></li>
<li>Reaction Distance (S<sub>RD</sub>)
<ul>
<li>Manual Initiation of measures: Reponse time (t) = 1s then S<sub>RD</sub> = V<sub>0</sub> x 1</li>
<li>Fully automatic systems: It can be smaller than the above value</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Contingency Manoeuvres (S<sub>CM</sub>)
<ul>
<li>The minimum distance for stopping to hovering mode: S<sub>CM</sub> = 1/2 x V<sub>0</sub><sup>2</sup>/ g x tan (theta). A maximum pitch angle of less than 45 degrees.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Lateral extension contingency volume (S<sub>CV</sub>): S<sub>CV</sub> = S<sub>GPS</sub> + S<sub>POS</sub> + S<sub>M</sub>+ S<sub>RD</sub>+S<sub>CM</sub></li>
</ul>
<p>Contingency Volume Vertical</p>
<ul>
<li>Height of Flight Geography (H<sub>FG</sub>)</li>
<li>Altitude measurement error (H<sub>baro</sub>): H<sub>baro</sub> = 1 meter for barometric altitude measurement or 4 meters for GPS-based altitude measurement.</li>
<li>Response Height (H<sub>RH</sub>):&nbsp;
<ul>
<li>Manual Initiation of measures: Responce time (t) = 1s with 45 degrees pitch angle. Then H<sub>RH </sub>= V0 x 0.7 x 1s</li>
<li>H<sub>RH</sub> can be smaller than in fully automatic systems</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Contingency Manoeuvres (H<sub>CM</sub>): For multirotor, the forward kinetic energy is completely converted into potential energy. Then = 1/2 x V<sub>0</sub><sup>2</sup>/g</li>
</ul>
<p>Continvency Volume (H<sub>CV</sub>): H<sub>CV</sub> = H<sub>FG</sub>+ H<sub>baro</sub>+ H<sub>RH</sub>+ H<sub>CM</sub></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;">Reference: Guidance for Dimensioning of Flight Geography, Contingency Volume and Ground Risk Buffer, Version 1.6, LBA (German CAA)</span></p>
<p>The contingency volume is the zone for unforeseen circumstances. During flight preparation, [OPERATOR] shall take into account a Contingency Volume of at least 10 m in addition to the limit(s) of the flight geography (not tethered UA).</p>
<table style="width: 94.1092%; height: 107px; border-collapse: collapse; border-style: solid;" border="1">
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 67px;">
<td width="307" style="width: 49.8077%; height: 29px;">
<p><span>i) procedures in case the unmanned aircraft leaves the designated flight geography</span></p>
</td>
<td width="307" style="width: 45.7504%; height: 29px;">
<div><span lang="EN-US">Fly Away. This procedure is described in C4.1 <a href="#article_9lW5NbSuYFIc7JWn1brq">Unmanned Aircraft leaves the Flight Geography</a></span></div>

</table>
<p>The required volume is examined and described in the operational flight plan.<strong></strong></p>
<h4>A6.4P.3. Ground Risk Buffer</h4>
<p>The ground risk buffer is an area above the earth's surface that encloses the operational volume and is specified to minimise the risk to third parties on the surface in the event the unmanned aircraft leaves the operational volume. The following picture shows that the ground risk buffer serves as a safety margin in case a drone is out of control.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FGRbuffer.png?alt=media&amp;token=e9fdf311-6a65-4fbd-8bae-69134fe7cd27" alt="" width="256"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>3D model Operational Volume and Risk buffer</em></p>
<p>The buffer applies to the territory with a higher risk than where the operation takes place.</p>
<p><strong>A.6.4P.3.1 Determining the Ground Risk Buffer</strong></p>
<p>Under PDRA-S01, any territory outside the controlled territory is at higher risk and therefore a ground risk buffer is required for each operation. The size of the buffer is determined as follows:</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/dronestart-production.appspot.com/o/images%2Fgeneral%2FPDRA-S01%20ver1.2.png?alt=media&amp;token=f7dc907d-4204-41f1-bd95-2a7ce4d075e2" alt="" width="300"></p>
<p>Use the 1:3 rule as a basis, see the table above.</p>
<h4>Air Risk Buffer<strong></strong></h4>
<ul>
<li>There is no formal buffer for air risk unless otherwise determined by the geozone.</li>
<li>However, the adjacent flight area with a higher risk must be taken into account, for example, if flying close to a CTR area.</li>
<li>The pilot avoids possible collisions at all times and immediately takes the necessary distance from other UAS, aircraft or birds.</li>
</ul>
<h4><strong>A6.4P.4 Adjacent Volume</strong></h4>
<p>The adjacent volume begins at the outer limit of the contingency volume. Its width results from a two-minute flight of the UA at its operating speed 𝑉<sub>0</sub>:</p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Adjacent volume horizontal</span></p>
<p>Width of the adjacent volume (<em>𝑆<sub>AV</sub></em>): <em>𝑆<sub>AV</sub></em> = 120 𝑠 x 𝑉<sub>0</sub></p>
<p>The height of the adjacent volume is at least 500 feet (150 m) above the operational volume.</p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Adjacent volume vertical </span></p>
<p>Hight of the adjacent volume (<em>𝐻<sub>AV</sub></em>): <em>𝐻<sub>AV&nbsp;</sub></em>= <em>H<sub>CV</sub></em> + 150 m</p>
<p><em>H<sub>CV</sub></em> is contingency volume (See A6.4.2 Contingency volume).</p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;">Reference: Guidance for Dimensioning of Flight Geography, Contingency Volume and Ground Risk Buffer, Version 1.6, LBA (German CAA)</span></p>
<h4><strong>A6.4P.5 Adjacent Area</strong></h4>
<div>
<p paraeid="{adae9a50-cad7-4bed-b46c-a26128c13b17}{83}" paraid="1054398924"><span xml:lang="EN-GB" data-contrast="auto">The adjacent area does not include a populated area or an assembly of people and </span><span xml:lang="EN-GB" data-contrast="auto">the adjacent airspace is classified as ARC-a or ARC-b.</span></p>
</div>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">The lateral outer limit of the adjacent area is calculated from the boundary of the operational volume as the distance flown in 3 minutes at the UA's maximum speed, with a minimum of 5 km and a maximum of 35 km.</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_bSb4QTeQ5r9CSQL6lvrQ" class="not_editable" data-id="bSb4QTeQ5r9CSQL6lvrQ">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="bSb4QTeQ5r9CSQL6lvrQ"><span class="shortcode">[A6.5P]</span> <span class="name">Controlled Ground Area PDRA-S01</span></h2>
<p>The controlled ground area is the area on the ground in which the UAS is operated and in which [OPERATOR] can guarantee that only involved persons are present.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Flying according to PDRA-S01 always requires a controlled territory: uninvolved persons must <u>not be present</u> within the operational volume and ground risk buffer. [OPERATOR] will designate the zone and close it if necessary. If that is not possible, additional observers and other crew members are added to the operation to deny access to these non-involved parties.</p>
<p>A physical barrier can consist of lashing tape, fences or cones with signage. The controlled territory is surveyed and described in the operational flight plan.</p>
<p>Before commencing the drone operation, [OPERATOR] must ensure that all persons located in the controlled area:</p>
<ol>
<li>have been informed of the risks of the operation<span data-contrast="auto" xml:lang="EN-GB" lang="EN-GB" class="TextRun Highlight SCXW176647967 BCX4"><span class="NormalTextRun SCXW176647967 BCX4"> by written and/or verbally by pilot(s) and/or observer(s).</span></span><span class="EOP SCXW176647967 BCX4" data-ccp-props="{}">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li>have been informed or trained in, where appropriate, the safety measures and measures adopted by [OPERATOR] to protect them; and</li>
<li>have expressly consented to participation in the operation;</li>
</ol>
<p>For this purpose, all involved persons sign the form from Annex C5.</p>
<p>Source: PDRA-S01, paragraph 4. UAS operator and UAS operational conditions.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_MXrj51Qv8mloDSKXdDAl" class="not_editable" data-id="MXrj51Qv8mloDSKXdDAl">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="MXrj51Qv8mloDSKXdDAl" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7123l"><span class="shortcode">[A6.6]</span> <span class="name">Involved and uninvolved persons</span></h2>
<p>Persons considered <strong>uninvolved</strong> by [OPERATOR]:</p>
<p>Persons that do not take part in the UAS operation, either directly or indirectly, and that could be potentially affected by the UAS operation.</p>
<p>Persons protected by a shelter (e.g. a roof) are not considered to be affected by the UAS operation nor exposed to direct risks if the MTOM of the UA is below 25 kg or if the UA complies with the conditions defined in criterion #2 of mitigation M1 of the SORA.</p>
<p>People that sit at a beach or in a park, or walk on a street or a road, are considered uninvolved persons.</p>
<p><strong>Involved persons</strong></p>
<p>A person may be considered to be ‘involved’ in the UAS operation when the following conditions are met.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Before the flight, the person:</p>
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<li>has given explicit consent (it may be verbal) to the UAS operator or to the remote pilot to be part of the UAS operation (even indirectly as a spectator or just accepting to be overflown by the UAS); and</li>
<li>has received from the UAS operator or from the remote pilot clear instructions and safety precautions to follow in case the UAS exhibits any unexpected behaviour.</li>
</ol>
<p>[OPERATOR] is responsible for ensuring that all persons involved can follow promptly the emergency procedures. In principle, to be considered a ‘person involved’, one:</p>
<p>(a) is able to decide whether or not to participate in the UAS operation;</p>
<p>(b) broadly understands the risks involved;</p>
<p>(c) has reasonable safeguards during the UAS operations, introduced by the site manager and the aircraft operator; and</p>
<p>(d) is not restricted from taking part in the event or activity if they decide not to participate in the UAS operation.</p>
<p>The person involved is expected to follow the directions and safety precautions provided by the UAS operator or the remote pilot, and the UAS operator or the remote pilot should check by asking simple questions to make sure that the directions and safety precautions have been properly understood.</p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;"><em>Source:&nbsp;AMC to Annex I to ED 2022/002/R</em></span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_xztG7DstLijADEy0btTp" class="not_editable" data-id="xztG7DstLijADEy0btTp">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="xztG7DstLijADEy0btTp"><span class="shortcode">[A6.7]</span> <span class="name">Population Density of an Area</span></h2>
<p>The EU regulations distinguish three levels:</p>
<ol>
<li>Controlled Ground Area</li>
<li>Sparsely Populated Area</li>
<li>Populated Area</li>
</ol>
<p>When an area cannot be seen as a Controlled Ground Area (1) and not as a Populated Area (3), it is automatically Sparsely Populated.<br>The basic principle is that a densely populated area corresponds to the areas within the built-up area of ​​towns and villages.</p>
<p>To research the statistical human density in an area during flight preparation, the following sources can be used:</p>
<ol>
<li><a href="https://ec.europa.eu/regional_policy/information-sources/maps/degree-urbanisation_en">https://ec.europa.eu/regional_policy/information-sources/maps/degree-urbanisation_en</a>: green area = sparsely populated</li>
<li><a href="https://ec.europa.eu/regional_policy/information-sources/maps/degree-urbanisation_en">https://ec.europa.eu/regional_policy/information-sources/maps/degree-urbanisation_en</a> : yellow or red area = densely populated</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: Population density figures can determine the type of environment, but not the number of people on-site and/or the potential risk for the UAS operation. It is therefore important that the pilot estimates the number of persons who are not involved and sees whether the operational volume is densely or sparsely populated at that specific moment. This estimate must be noted on the Operational Flight Plan for flights outside the controlled ground area.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_0UF336ZJXnCdRaeOpG4z" class="not_editable" data-id="0UF336ZJXnCdRaeOpG4z">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="0UF336ZJXnCdRaeOpG4z"><span class="shortcode">[A6.8]</span> <span class="name">Take-off and landing locations within the Operational Volume</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The site(s) of operation must allow the take-off and landing of the UA in complete safety and the safety of persons and property on the ground must never be compromised.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">A main and at least one alternative take-off and landing location must be established at the flying location. Besides, it must be acknowledged at which landing site the UAS will perform the emergency landing, if applicable.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Depending on the risk analysis, the flight location is cordoned off and set up following the provisions of the Regulations on airports and other sites.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The take-off and landing site meets the following requirements:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">For landing and take-off, a surface area should be available with at least 5 times the diameter of the UAS, unless other means of safety around the zone are in place (e.g. forest, trees, walls);</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The ground conditions, in terms of flatness and bearing capacity, such that the relevant UAS can take off and land safely;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">There are no obstacles on the surface. The crop height on the surface is a maximum of 15 centimetres, insofar as it does not endanger a safe flight operation;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">If necessary, a landing pad is used for the UAS;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The obstacle-free zone is at least 20 m<sup>2</sup>.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><span style="font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif; mso-fareast-font-family: Aptos; mso-fareast-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-ansi-language: NL; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: AR-SA;">The (ground under) the take-off site should be as free as possible from (electro)magnetic sources, such as metal and antennas, that may interfere with the compass and other parts of the drone.</span></span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The site should be cordoned off and marked with cones and/or restricted tapes to keep uninvolved persons away, for example by posting warning signs.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">When designing and choosing, also consider access and availability to the following items:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Fire extinguisher;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">A shovel;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">First aid kit;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Accessibility for emergency services.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Procedure to keep bystanders away</strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The observer is responsible for keeping bystanders at a safe distance so that the pilot can maintain focus on the operation. The procedure is as follows:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The observer addresses bystanders threatening to enter the flying area and kindly asks them to keep their distance.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The observer tries to act de-escalating so that the pilot can remain focused on the operation.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The observer will remain between the pilot and the bystander in case of aggression.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">If the situation escalates further, the observer will contact the police.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The pilot retrieves the UAS, lands and follows the shutdown procedure.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The pre-flight check is performed at the starting location. The procedure for shutting down UAS immediately after the flight is described in <a href="#article_xlWWAijWlxABHl6YEFPd">[B2.8] Post-flight Procedures</a>.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">After the flight, the takeoff and landing locations should be checked for debris. Each crew member is responsible for returning all materials.</span></p>
<p><em><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Alternative take-off and landing location</span></em></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">An alternative take-off and landing place must meet the same requirements as stated above. The alternative take-off and landing locations must be chosen strategically. The following criteria are used for this:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In line with the UAS flight path;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Not in line with the UAS to the pilot. In an emergency, the intention is to fly off the pilot and crew;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In a place visible to the pilot;</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">An open area with no waste, obstructions or combustible objects.</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="Dyjmr17EqG65QJpoBZdI" id="article_Dyjmr17EqG65QJpoBZdI">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="Dyjmr17EqG65QJpoBZdI"><span class="shortcode">[A6.10A]</span> <span class="name">Basic Containment and AltMoc Triggers for Enhanced Containment</span></h2>
<p><strong>Basic Containment</strong></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;">Basic Containment refers to the level of containment required for UAS operations in the specific category as per SORA standards. The key objective of basic containment is to ensure that no probable failure of the unmanned aircraft system (UAS) or any external system will lead to the aircraft operating outside the designated operational volume.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><strong></strong></p>
<p><strong>Procedure for Determining Basic Containment Requirements</strong></p>
<p>This procedure outlines the steps to determine the level of containment:</p>
<p><strong>1. Assessment of UAS Characteristics:</strong></p>
<p><em>Characteristic dimensions of the UA (in metres)</em>: the width of the UA in the direction transversal to the direction of flight.</p>
<ul>
<li>for fixed wing UA including hybrid configurations, the UA characteristic dimension is the wingspan;</li>
<li>for conventional or coaxial helicopters UA, the UA characteristic dimension is the diameter of the main rotor;</li>
<li>for multirotor (e.g. hexacopter) UA, the UA characteristic dimension is defined by the maximum distance (i.e. the diagonal distance) between blade tips.</li>
</ul>
<p><em>Maximum speed of the UA: </em>the maximum speed is conservatively defined as the maximum possible&nbsp;airspeed of the UA, as defined by the designer. This is not the mission specific maximum airspeed of the UA as reducing the mission airspeed may not necessarily reduce the impact area.</p>
<p><em>MTOM (Maximum Take of Mass): </em>the maximum UA mass, including payload and fuel, as defined by the manufacturer, design organisation or the builder, at which the UA can be operated.</p>
<p><strong>2. </strong><strong>Choose the right table/column in the table A6.10A for containment based on UA size and speed</strong></p>
<p><strong><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light', sans-serif;">3. UA between &gt;1m and &lt; 3 m? Is sheltering applicable?</span></strong></p>
<p>Expected protection of people from the UA in case of a crash into a building or structure. If the operator claims a sheltered operational environment, the operator:<br>(a) uses a UA of less than 25 kg and a maximum speed of less than 35 m/s and,<br>(b) must verify that although the operation is conducted in a populated environment, it is reasonable to consider that most of the non-involved persons will be located within a building</p>
<p>If this is not the case, use the containment table/column without sheltering.</p>
<p><strong style="font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;">4. Adjacent Area Calculation:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Calculate the size of the adjacent area based on the distance flown at maximum speed for three minutes. If this distance is less than 5 km, a minimum distance of 5 km will be used; if it exceeds 35 km, a maximum of 35 km will apply.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>5. Population Density Evaluation:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;">Calculate the average population density in the calculated adjacent area to the operational volume using publicly available data, such as Statistics Netherlands (<a href="https://app.pdok.nl/viewer" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CBS/PDOK</a>).<o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"></span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;">6. Outdoor assemblies of people within 1km from the Operational Volume?&nbsp;</span></strong></p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;">Assess whether there are any outdoor assemblies of people of more than 40.000 people within one (1) km from the operational volume. Events with more than 40.000 people nearby are not allowed with basic containment.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong></strong></p>
<p><strong>7. Basic Containment Determination (see DIA declaration):</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Basic containment is required for all UAS operations in the specific category. This means that no probable failure of the UAS or any supporting external system shall lead to operation outside the operational volume.</li>
<li>The allowed probability of single failures that could lead to a fly-away must be set at a remote level (less than 10<sup>-3</sup> per flight hour).</li>
<li>Check if UA has been declared (DIA declaration).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>8. Final Decision:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>If the calculated population density and the assessment of outdoor assemblies do not indicate a need for enhanced containment, the operator can proceed with basic containment.</li>
<li>All operational procedures and risk assessments are aligned with the basic containment requirements.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<table class="MsoNormalTable" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" width="604" style="width: 453.3pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 260.775px; border-spacing: 0px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 22.125px;">
<td width="384" nowrap="nowrap" colspan="3" valign="bottom" style="width: 288.1pt; padding: 0cm 3.5pt;">
