<article id="article_F3QfXC1bWUfO0Yxuw7w4" class="not_editable" data-id="F3QfXC1bWUfO0Yxuw7w4">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="F3QfXC1bWUfO0Yxuw7w4" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja71242"><span class="shortcode">[A7.22]</span> <span class="name">Mandatory documents on flight location</span></h2>
<p>The following documents must be present at the flight location:</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;">Operational Authorisation<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;">A (digital) copy of the Operations Manual&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light', sans-serif; color: black; background-image: initial; background-position: initial; background-size: initial; background-repeat: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial;">Proof of competence (pilots)</span><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></li>
<li class="MsoNormal" style="mso-margin-top-alt: auto; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 36.0pt;"><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light', sans-serif; color: black; background-image: initial; background-position: initial; background-size: initial; background-repeat: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial;">Operational plan</span><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"><o:p></o:p></span></li>
</ul>
<p>Other documents are not required but are strongly recommended to take with you to the flight location. For this, refer to section [APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_a8orMQERZVhgQKhQgkoE" class="not_editable" data-id="a8orMQERZVhgQKhQgkoE">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="a8orMQERZVhgQKhQgkoE" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei0"><span class="shortcode">[A7.23]</span> <span class="name">Declaration procedure for new pilots and/or UAS </span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">For some operations, the use of a different type of drone is desirable. In other operations additional drone pilots are needed. This procedure describes the declaration process. Declaration means that the accountable manager (the applicant) declares that the pilot/UAS is safe for the intended operation (ConOps).</span></p>
<p><strong>Pilot declaration</strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true"></span>For each pilot, [OPERATOR] states that the pilot has a theoretical and practical training that is sufficient for the intended operation and includes the following elements:</p>
<ol>
<li>knowledge of European UAS regulations (EU- 2019/947) and other relevant European and national regulations</li>
<li>rules related to the type of airspace (SERA &amp; SORA)</li>
<li>airmanship and airspace safety</li>
<li>human performance limits</li>
<li>meteorology</li>
<li>navigation &amp; maps</li>
<li>the UAS</li>
<li>operational procedures</li>
</ol>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The declaration for the new pilot (name, date of birth and certificate) is send to ILT: vergunningverlening.drones@ILenT.nl</span></p>
<p><strong>UAS declaration</strong><br><strong></strong></p>
<p>For each UAS, [OPERATOR] verifies and states that:</p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The RDW 'exploitantnummer' of [OPERATOR] NLDxxx is placed visible on each UAS which is operated.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The UAS is insured and is covered by the covering conditions of the policy of [OPERATOR];</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The UAS complies with the same category and class as that for which the pilot is authorized and as described in this Operations Manual and the operating license.</span></li>
<li>Characteristics and limitations of the C3 links, RF spectrum and environmental factors are sufficient for safe intended operation.</li>
<li>For the type and model in question, the desired information is displayed on the display of the GCS, including the alarm.&nbsp;</li>
<li>The UAS supplier has published a EU <em>declaration of conformity*</em></li>
</ul>
<p><sub>*If no declaration of conformity is available, contact CAA-NL.</sub></p>
<p>The declaration for the new UAS is send to ILT: vergunningverlening.drones@ILenT.nl</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_rvoEnzE3Xl8fZ7piImKF" class="not_editable" data-id="rvoEnzE3Xl8fZ7piImKF">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="rvoEnzE3Xl8fZ7piImKF" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei1"><span class="shortcode">[A7.24]</span> <span class="name">Cross-border Operations</span></h2>
<p>Cross-border operations or operations according to Article 13 - Regulation (EU) 2020/639):</p>
<p>Send an application to the competent authority of the Member State with the following information:</p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type: none;">
<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<li>a copy of the operating licence granted to the UAS operator in accordance with Article 12; and</li>
<li>the location(s) of the proposed operation, including the updated mitigation measures, where necessary, to address the risks identified in accordance with point (b) of Article 11(2) that are specific to local airspace, terrain and population characteristics and climatic conditions. According to OSO #23, environmental factors for a safe flight, an evaluation of the environmental factors in that particular EU country is necessary. Think, for example, of flying in a mountainous environment. For this, a specific addition to the handbook is necessary. These measures are added to the handbook in section C3.13 (if applicable).</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Upon receipt of the application, the competent authority shall assess the intended operation and shall provide confirmation to the competent authority of the Member State of registry (CAA-NL = ILT) and the [OPERATOR] that the updated mitigating measures referred to in point (b) of paragraph 1 are satisfactory for the operation at the intended site.</p>
<p>Upon receipt of that confirmation, [OPERATOR] may commence the intended operation and ILT shall record the updated mitigation measures to be applied by the UAS operator in the operating licence issued in accordance with Article 12.</p>
<p>Check the EASA website for information of flying in other member states: <a href="https://www.easa.europa.eu/en/domains/civil-drones/naa" contenteditable="false" title="https://www.easa.europa.eu/en/domains/civil-drones/naa">https://www.easa.europa.eu/en/domains/civil-drones/naa</a></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1evfl8v7s1e3">Chapter A8: GENERAL MAINTENANCE<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[OAE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_vThipL9VVFJ8Zz0hWwEy" class="not_editable" data-id="vThipL9VVFJ8Zz0hWwEy">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="vThipL9VVFJ8Zz0hWwEy"><span class="shortcode">[A8.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Maintenance</span></h2>
<p>Under EU regulations, requirements are set for maintenance and for the people who carry out the maintenance. In OSO #03 it is stated that:</p>
<ul>
<li>UAS maintenance instructions are prepared and, where applicable, contain the relevant instructions and conditions of the manufacturer.</li>
<li>The maintenance personnel will carry out maintenance by the maintenance instructions.</li>
</ul>
<p>[OPERATOR] distinguishes between minor routine maintenance and major non-routine maintenance.</p>
<p><em>1. Routine minor Maintenance</em><br>At [OPERATOR], the Maintenance Manager and pilot will perform routine maintenance, as described in the UAS manual. In all cases, the maintenance log must be updated with all work completed and a flight test performed (in which all functions are tested).</p>
<p><br><em>2. Non-routine major maintenance</em><br>Non-routine major maintenance involves addressing unexpected issues like component failures, structural damage. Skilled technicians must diagnose and repair the problem, often replacing key parts and recalibrating systems. After repairs, thorough testing ensures airworthiness and compliance with safety standards. This maintenance will performed by the supplier.</p>
</article>
<p class="MsoNormal">Minor maintenance is performed by the maintenance manager at the office address of [OPERATOR] at Hazenkoog 29E, Alkmaar. Non-routine major maintenance will be performed by an authorized DJI dealer.<o:p></o:p></p>
<article id="article_ZBXTbZWKc2h4jmVsNaKk" class="not_editable" data-id="ZBXTbZWKc2h4jmVsNaKk">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="ZBXTbZWKc2h4jmVsNaKk" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei3"><span class="shortcode">[A8.1]</span> <span class="name">Maintenance Manager</span></h2>
<p>Maintenance is essential for safe operation with a UAS. To be able to guarantee this responsibility, one person responsible is appointed within [OPERATOR] for the maintenance of the UAS. The maintenance manager is responsible for the optimal condition of the UAS. For this, the maintenance manager uses the maintenance documentation supplied by the producer of the UAS.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_8KYUVACqqEUvJirJLbxa" class="not_editable" data-id="8KYUVACqqEUvJirJLbxa">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="8KYUVACqqEUvJirJLbxa"><span class="shortcode">[A8.2]</span> <span class="name">General Maintenance Program</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">To be able to guarantee safety and reliability when using the UAS, it is necessary to carry out maintenance on the UAS at a fixed interval or after incidents.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Two parameters have been defined for regular maintenance:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">After a certain number of flying hours;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">After a certain number of flights.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Both parameters are UAS-dependent and are determined by the Maintenance manager. These parameters are also registered in the log of the relevant UAS. Maintenance activities are performed in accordance with the manufacturer's official maintenance guidelines and the specifications outlined in Part B of this Operations Manual.</span></p>
</article>
<table style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%;" border="1">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="width: 19.1667%; text-align: center;">UAS</td>
<td style="width: 37.6234%; text-align: center;">Flight hours for small maintenance</td>
<td style="width: 43.1306%; text-align: center;">Flight hours for major maintenance</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 19.1667%;">DJI Mavic 3</td>
<td style="width: 37.6234%;">20&nbsp;</td>
<td style="width: 43.1306%;">100&nbsp;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 19.1667%;">DJI Mavic 3 thermal</td>
<td style="width: 37.6234%;">20</td>
<td style="width: 43.1306%;">100</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<article id="article_wWfHn5FellXSJxsiqyfa" class="not_editable" data-id="wWfHn5FellXSJxsiqyfa">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="wWfHn5FellXSJxsiqyfa" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei5"><span class="shortcode">[A8.3]</span> <span class="name">Performing Maintenance</span></h2>
<p>Minor maintenance is carried out at the maintenance location of the UAS in the head office or a business location of [OPERATOR]. In order to perform the maintenance, specific tools are available at this location. See APPENDIX A for the name(s) of authorized service personnel.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Major maintenance is carried out with competent and authorized maintenance personnel.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_lEZ1haq3V9P4nKcKcmKH" class="not_editable" data-id="lEZ1haq3V9P4nKcKcmKH">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="lEZ1haq3V9P4nKcKcmKH" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln110"><span class="shortcode">[A8.4]</span> <span class="name">Firmware Updates</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Software and firmware are part of this configuration. Some important points are described below.</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The Maintenance manager knows the purpose of the update and which systems this update will affect before the software or firmware is executed.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The Maintenance manager conducts further research through the internet into possible reports about the reliability of the update. There are some forums available for doing that.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Only if there are no indications from which the Maintenance manager can conclude that an unsafe situation will arise due to the update, he performs the update.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Before the Maintenance manager releases the UAS operationally after a software or firmware update, he ensures that the control over the UAS is functioning properly using a Functional Check Flight (FCF) as described in chapter A8.5.<br></span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The Maintenance manager processes the update and execution of the FCF including the successful outcome of the FCF in the technical administration and the logbook.</span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<ul>
<li><span style="background-color: #fbeeb8;">As part of firmware updates also information about the geo-awareness function is updated when this is supported by the UAS. The Maintenance manager does an extra check after the firmware update to check if GNSS functions properly.</span></li>
</ul>
<article id="article_vGBI4Lr4Cen4lAFgbFSs" class="not_editable" data-id="vGBI4Lr4Cen4lAFgbFSs">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="vGBI4Lr4Cen4lAFgbFSs" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln111"><span class="shortcode">[A8.5]</span> <span class="name">Conduct Test Flight After Maintenance</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In case of major maintenance and/or damage, the UAS will have to undergo several tests showing that airworthiness is assured. By performing the tests below, the UAS can be declared airworthy and troubleshooting:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">All functions in the system must be thoroughly tested;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">A test flight of at least 10 minutes is to be made to rule out any particularities. Any details must be recorded in the operation log;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">When the Maintenance Manager considers the UAS suitable to be used for operations, he/she will release the UAS and write it down in the logbook.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">During that test flight, the following systems must be checked:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">GNSS functionalities;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Connectivity of the UAS with the ground station;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The operating system of the UAS;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Flight characteristics of the UAS;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The functioning of the propulsion system;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Fail-safe and emergency procedures should be checked </span><span data-preserver-spaces="true">as described in <a href="https://www.nlr.nl/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/20200710-NL-AS-RPAS2-Final.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">AS-RPAS2</a> </span><span data-preserver-spaces="true">at the Dutch Civil Aviation Authority (NLR);</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The functioning of the batteries and power supply.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The location where the test flight is performed meets the following conditions:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Obstacles, buildings, vehicles, vessels, roads, railway lines, people, animals, electricity pylons, etc. at least &gt; 25 meters from the take-off and landing site;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Airspace class G;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Quiet, preferably in a rural location (few people).</span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<p>If a test flight is required this will be carried out at the Kleimeer, Koedijk which is a rural area without obstacles nearby where a test flight can be carried out safely.</p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="XsuxKV78Z3FEJCpfXu9i" id="article_XsuxKV78Z3FEJCpfXu9i">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="XsuxKV78Z3FEJCpfXu9i" id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiindi"><span class="shortcode">[A8.6]</span> <span class="name">Administration Maintenance</span></h2>
<p>All maintenance work performed is immediately updated in the technical logbook available per UAS. See for an example in APPENDIX D. Detailed maintenance records must be stored. See chapter <a href="#article_nzYDthIRZdtfpWJxAJlr">[A12.1] Record-Keeping Procedures</a> for more information.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_wpmjTWkJdt7S2LPqFbGx" class="not_editable" data-id="wpmjTWkJdt7S2LPqFbGx">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1flbi8a7i2hj" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="wpmjTWkJdt7S2LPqFbGx"><span class="shortcode">[A8.7]</span> <span class="name">Investigation and Reporting of Defects and Losses</span></h2>
<p>If technical defects and losses are found, the Accountable Manager should be contacted. The detection of the defect must be recorded in the technical log available per UAS. In consultation with the Accountable Manager, it is decided what action should be taken to make the UAS operational again.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_CiAjCDNRinptNNCRv5go" class="not_editable" data-id="CiAjCDNRinptNNCRv5go">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="CiAjCDNRinptNNCRv5go" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja71243"><span class="shortcode">[A8.8]</span> <span class="name">Battery Management</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The batteries used in the UA are usually of the type LiPo (Li-Polymer) or Li-ion. These high-capacity batteries are a fire hazard when overloaded (This phenomenon is not yet identified regarding Li-Metal).</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The batteries come with instructions for handling and it is important to follow these carefully to prevent fire on the UAS or in the storage area.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Follow the instructions regarding:</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Storage</span></strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">LiPos are safely stored in a fireproof bag (LIPO bag) or suitable suitcase;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Check the best temperature for storage;</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Transport</span></strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Transport the batteries in the appropriate suitcase or bag;&nbsp;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Make sure the batteries are not damaged during transport or use. This can cause an internal short circuit (and fire);</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Usage</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Follow the specifications of the batteries carefully. Most batteries are automatically charged and discharged correctly;</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The batteries should not be used if they are swelling or are already warm;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In case of damage or bulging during use, the battery must be handed in as soon as possible as small chemical waste (KCA). Caution in case of fire: <span style="text-decoration: underline;">Do not inhale the toxic smoke</span> and let the battery burn out for at least 20 minutes</span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fki0aip31q19">Chapter A9:&nbsp;SECURITY<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[VS]<br></span></h1>
<article id="article_4fBc1DUNlL4TzGq5cGjV" class="not_editable" data-id="4fBc1DUNlL4TzGq5cGjV">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="4fBc1DUNlL4TzGq5cGjV" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei6"><span class="shortcode">[A9.0]</span> <span class="name">Security</span></h2>
<p class="p1">In this chapter, the security requirements are described. This is a broad concept that broadly covers the following topics:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li2">Security of data and documents;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li1">Security of the area where the operation takes place.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p3"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The [OPERATOR] ensures that security requirements applicable to the area of operations comply with the intended operation.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p1">Section 9.1 deals with the security of data and documents. Paragraph 9.2 deals with the security of the area where the operation takes place.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_odkI1iZYHNftzjaRkkaE" class="not_editable" data-id="odkI1iZYHNftzjaRkkaE">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="odkI1iZYHNftzjaRkkaE" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln114"><span class="shortcode">[A9.1]</span> <span class="name">Security of data and documents</span></h2>
<p class="p1">Data and documents of both involved and uninvolved persons must be protected against unauthorized access and/or interference. The following topics have been cited:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li2">Security of personal data;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Security of the UAS and the online working environment;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Security of confidential documents;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li1">Protection against fraud and embezzlement.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p1"><strong>[A9.1.1] Security of personal data<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></strong></p>
<p class="p1">Since 25 May 2018, the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) applies. Since then, the same rules apply throughout Europe for the processing of personal data. Personal data is any information about an identified or identifiable natural person.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p1">There is a good chance that personal data will be processed during flights in inhabited areas where images are taken. These can be images and/or sound recordings of persons, license plates or address details.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p1">There are several bases that justify the processing of personal data:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li2">Consent of the person in question;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Necessary for the execution of an agreement;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Necessary because this results from a legal obligation;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Necessary for the protection of vital interests;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Necessary for the performance of a task carried out in the public interest or the public authority;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li1">Necessary to represent one's legitimate interest.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p1">Typically, consent or necessity for the performance of an agreement with a customer will be the applicable basis.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p1">Personal data of third parties that are processed during the flight must be handled with the utmost care:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li4">Every personal data is made unrecognizable using a blurring tool;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li4">Images and/or recordings that are not (or no longer) used must be deleted immediately;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li1">Images are stored at all times in a secure environment.<span class="Apple-converted-space"> See [A9.1.3] Security of confidential documents.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p2"><strong>[A9.1.2] Security of the UAS and the online work environment<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></strong></p>
<p class="p2">Measures must be taken to protect the UA system and the online working environment against unauthorized modification and/or unlawful access to data streams.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p2"><em>9.1.2.1 Modification<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></em></p>
<p class="p2">UAS are stored in an enclosed area, to which only authorized personnel have access. It is strictly forbidden to make modifications to the hardware and software of the UAS. Only the Maintenance Manager and the maintenance staff are authorised to do so.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p2">When an update needs to take place, the Maintenance Manager will be notified. It will also perform the update if necessary.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p2">After each use of a UAS, the type of use and the user are recorded in the UAS journal of the relevant UAS. In this way, any (unwanted) modification or damage can be traced.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p2"><em>9.1.2.2 Data streams<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></em></p>
<p class="p2">UAS and the online working environment are protected against unlawful access to data (flows). Some measures are taken that contribute to security:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li3">Use of strong passwords (possibly two-factor authentication);<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li3">Regularly updating firmware/software/computer programs;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li3">Only use official/original systems;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li3">Set a limit on the number of devices that connect to the GCS;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Functioning RTH mode.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p2"><strong>[A9.1.3] Security of confidential documents<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></strong></p>
<ul>
<li class="p2">Both digital and paper versions of confidential documents should be stored securely.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="p2">Paper versions of confidential documents should be kept in a locked room, to which only authorized personnel have access.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="p2">Digital versions of confidential documents should be stored in a secure folder, to which only authorized personnel have access.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="p2"><span class="Apple-converted-space">Images and recordings that could not be deleted immediately should be stored on an external hard disk, to which only autorized personnel has access.</span></li>
<li class="p2"><span class="Apple-converted-space">The accountable manager is responsible of guarding, changing, updating and protecting and only authorized persons have access.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="p2"><strong>[A9.1.4] Fraud and embezzlement protection<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></strong></p>
<p class="p2">To prevent (parts of) UAS or confidential documents from being unlawfully removed, all UAS, the online working environment and the confidential documents must be secured by the measures in the previous paragraphs.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_sFdpv67I0VL4KyaHLamT" class="not_editable" data-id="sFdpv67I0VL4KyaHLamT">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="sFdpv67I0VL4KyaHLamT" id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiindj"><span class="shortcode">[A9.2]</span> <span class="name">Implementing Area Security</span></h2>
<p>Unlawful interference with drones poses significant risks to both operators and the public, including privacy violations, safety hazards, and potential legal consequences. As drone operators, it's crucial to be aware of these threats and take proactive measures to mitigate them.</p>
<p><strong>Mitigations</strong><br><br>1. Security Measures<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Store drones securely to prevent unauthorized access.<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Use strong passwords and keep firmware updated.<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Conduct regular pre-flight checks to ensure integrity.<br><br>2. Operational Practices<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Plan flight routes to avoid restricted areas.<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Maintain situational awareness during operations.<br><br>3. Data Protection<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Encrypt sensitive data to protect privacy.<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Use secure communication protocols for data transmission.<br><br>4. Compliance and Education<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Stay informed about local regulations and airspace restrictions.<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Adhere to ethical guidelines and principles.<br><br>5. Training and Emergency Response<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Undergo comprehensive training for safe and secure drone operation.<br>&nbsp; &nbsp;- Establish emergency response protocols for interference incidents.<br><br>By implementing these mitigations, the risks of unlawful interference can be minimized, ensuring responsible and compliant operation of drones.</p>
</article>
<p><span style="background-color: #fbeeb8;">Hoofdstuk A9.3 toegevoegd</span></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="xF4q4NPtcPDgRM2uI65G" id="article_xF4q4NPtcPDgRM2uI65G">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="xF4q4NPtcPDgRM2uI65G" id="mcetoc_1ib4kg3vdm"><span class="shortcode">[A9.3]</span> <span class="name">Optimizing Radio Spectrum Usage for Safe Operations</span></h2>
<p>UAS operations are conducted in a manner that:</p>
<ul>
<li>Efficiently utilizes available radio spectrum resources.</li>
<li>Support the optimal functioning of other communication systems by avoiding interference.</li>
</ul>
<p>This can involve various strategies such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Using frequency bands allocated specifically for UAS communication.</li>
<li>Employing technologies and protocols that minimize the risk of interference with other systems.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<ul>
<li><span style="background-color: #fbeeb8;">Various ways to avoid interference of the radio spectrum are implemented in de specific operations such as keeping distance to power lines and a pre flight check of obstacles in the environment that can disturb radio spectrum usage.</span></li>
<li><span style="background-color: #fbeeb8;">Additionally for both the UAS and the radio communication equipment (if applicable) pre flight is checked if both the UAS signal and the radio communication equipment is good.</span><span style="background-color: #fbeeb8;"></span></li>
</ul>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdd543d11963"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f01g8iqts6"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0r59arqcfo"></h1>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdf7ngrq1rcd"><div class="page-break"></div>Chapter A10:&nbsp; ENVIRONMENT<span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[GU]</span></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1euu04s2027f"></h1>
<article id="article_9195UBNiPKqvRZB73nFx" class="not_editable" data-id="9195UBNiPKqvRZB73nFx">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="9195UBNiPKqvRZB73nFx" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei7"><span class="shortcode">[A10.1]</span> <span class="name">Guidelines Nuisance</span></h2>
<p>All UAS operations are to be carried out in line with applicable environmental and nature protection obligations as outlined in national and EU law.</p>
<p>As outlined in the ConOps, it is allowed to fly above sparsely populated areas, in the vicinity of homes and other buildings.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>There are a number of factors that can cause nuisance, such as invasion of privacy (UA with camera flies close to homes / gardens, etc.) and the sound of the propellers.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Therefore the following guidelines are followed by [OPERATOR].</span></p>
<p class="p1"><b>Privacy Guidelines<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></b></p>
<p class="p1">To ensure the privacy of third parties, the following guidelines are used during operations within or nearby populated areas:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li2">Choosing time brackets for the operation when its normally quiet in the area (e.g. outside peak hours in residential areas and at night in industrial areas);<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">If required by the ConOps, distribute flyers or letters to residents and businesses in the affected area beforehand, detailing the time, purpose, nature of the operations and the contact information of the operator. The operator will ensure it is provided with ample notice, allowing adequate time to prepare. In the flyer, it can be also explained that privacy is respected and that closing curtains can be contributed to this, for example.</li>
<li class="li2">Place signs at noticeable spot around the area of operation, informing people about the drone activity.</li>
<li class="li1">Deploy personnel on the ground to interact with residents, provide information, and address immediate concerns.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p1"><b>Noise guidelines<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></b></p>
<p class="p1">The noise of the propellers of the UA can cause nuisance if flying near people. The sound can also trigger startle reactions in animals.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Persons living near the operation are advised to close the windows and doors during the operation to minimize noise.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p1">Flights that take place in the vicinity of/above Natura 2000 sites must always be coordinated with the manager of that site. In some cases, guidelines regarding drones have been included in the management plan of the area in question. This indicates whether it is permitted to fly a drone in that area and, if so, how permission can be obtained. If this is not laid down in the management plan, the "lead" of the area must always be contacted in advance. Often this is the province in question.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p class="p1">For a list of Natura 2000 sites, see <a href="#article_41xHw3CDpzrLzISeLUB4">[A7.8] Natura2000</a></p>
<p class="p1"><a href="https://www.bij12.nl/onderwerpen/natuur-en-landschap/natura-2000-beheerplannen/">https://www.bij12.nl/onderwerpen/natuur-en-landschap/natura-2000-beheerplannen/</a></p>
<p class="p1">Of course, in all other cases, the natural habitat of animals must be respected.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_DMq8yrm4hbVouZHtmAPT" class="not_editable" data-id="DMq8yrm4hbVouZHtmAPT">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="DMq8yrm4hbVouZHtmAPT" id="mcetoc_1in3piidei8"><span class="shortcode">[A10.2]</span> <span class="name">Environmental Guidelines</span></h2>
<p class="p1">[OPERATOR] contributes to the maintenance of a healthy and safe (living) environment. Therefore, the following guidelines are used:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ul class="ul1">
<li class="li2">Flight documents shall, if possible, be consulted and stored digitally as much as possible;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">The area where the operation takes place is cleaned up afterwards. Waste such as food and drink packaging or broken parts of the UA are thrown away/taken away by the UAS team;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">Defective LiPo batteries are not thrown in the bulky waste. These are periodically brought to the waste disposal;<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
<li class="li2">The environment of people and animals is respected at all times.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<p>[OPERATOR] has completed a DPIA analysis . The conclusion of this analysis is: No DPIA required.</p>
<p>See the attached DPIA Analyse 1.0.</p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdf7ngrq1rcf"><div class="page-break"></div>Chapter A11:&nbsp; OCCURRENCE REPORTING PROCEDURES<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[RP]</span></h1>
<article id="article_V28zgwoWrmKWuTmVRuFo" class="not_editable" data-id="V28zgwoWrmKWuTmVRuFo">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="V28zgwoWrmKWuTmVRuFo"><span class="shortcode">[A11.1]</span> <span class="name">Reporting Procedures</span></h2>
<p>The European Union and its Member States are committed to ensuring a high level of aviation safety and to protect European citizens by better-preventing aircraft accidents (Regulation (EU) No 376/2014). The regulation deals with the reporting, analysis and follow-up of occurrences in civil aviation.</p>
<p>This chapter describes how to act in the event of an incident with the UAS or system parts of the UAS. The aim is to improve aviation safety by ensuring that relevant safety information related to the UAS operation is reported, collected, stored, protected, exchanged, disseminated and analysed.</p>
<p>On the basis of Regulation (EU) 376/2014, occurrences in civil aviation are subject to a reporting obligation. This also includes events with a UA. A report shall be made if:</p>
<ul>
<li>an aircraft endangers, or could endanger, its occupants or other persons;</li>
<li>concerns an accident or a serious incident.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Accident</strong></p>
<p>An accident is an event related to the use of a UAS and occurs between the time when the UAS operator intends to perform a flight and the time when the flight is (un)intended to end, where:</p>
<ul>
<li>A person is fatally or seriously injured as a result of direct contact with (a part of) the UAS, including parts that have become detached from the UAS;</li>
<li>The UAS is missing or completely unreachable;</li>
<li>The UAS suffers damage or a structural defect, causing:
<ul>
<li>Its solidity, performance or flight characteristics are impaired; and</li>
<li>Which would normally require major repairs or replacement of the affected component;</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Serious incident</strong></p>
<p>A serious incident is an incident that occurs under circumstances that indicate that an accident has almost occurred.</p>
<p><strong>Incident&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p>An incident is an event related to the functioning of a UAS that impairs or could impair safe operation, with the exception of an accident.</p>
<p><strong></strong></p>
<h2>[A11.2] Occurrence Registration and Reporting</h2>
<p>All events are registered in the Occurrence Register. [OPERATOR] maintains this register to manage occurrences and risk mitigation measures.</p>
<p>All incidents are internally reported. The purpose of reporting incidents is to prevent accidents and (serious) incidents and not to establish guilt or liability.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Mandatory reporting</strong><br>As stated in Regulation (EU) 2015/1018 Annex V, a number of elements must be reported specifically<a href="https://eur-lex.europa.eu/eli/reg_impl/2015/1018/oj">.</a> See the overview below.</p>

</td>

</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>Anyone within the UAS organization can report incidents. When several people are involved in an incident, it may be useful to make mutual agreements about who will report it. However, this is not a requirement.</p>
<p>The reporter must in any case provide the following elements about the event:</p>
<ul>
<li>Brief description of the incident;</li>
<li>Injury and/or damage (if applicable);</li>
<li>The location of the incident;</li>
<li>The date and time of the occurrence;</li>
<li>The measures that have already been taken;</li>
<li>How to reach the reporter.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Notification form</strong></p>
<p>The forms for reporting occurrences can be found on the ECCAIRS 2 website: <a href="https://e2.aviationreporting.eu/reporting">https://e2.aviationreporting.eu/reporting</a>. For events with UAS, this can be done via the menu "Report an Occurrence" &gt; "I report on behalf of my Organisation" &gt; "Netherlands ILT" &gt; "Report an occurrence without registration" &gt; "General Aviation".</p>
<p>&nbsp;Always make a (digital) copy and send it to the responsible person of [OPERATOR].</p>
<p><strong>Procedure after receipt of the report</strong></p>
<p>After the Pilot has reported the incident to the Accountable Manager or Safety Manager (if available) and has sent the form, if applicable, to the external authorities, the [OPERATOR] will investigate the incident, answering at least the following questions:&nbsp;</p>
<ul>
<li>What happened?</li>
<li>How could this happen or what is the source cause of the incident?</li>
<li>How can the incident be prevented in the future?</li>
</ul>
<p>The Accountable Manager ensures the implementation of the established corrective measures.&nbsp;</p>
<p>[OPERATOR] always gives feedback to the person who made the report and informs about the actions taken in response to the report.</p>
<p><strong>External reporting and notification:</strong></p>
<table width="100%" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; border-style: solid;" border="1">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td width="48%">
<p><em>Aviation Incident Analysis Bureau (ABL)</em></p>
</td>
<td width="48%">
<p>The ABL is informed by [OPERATOR] of each incident. This can be done via the following site: <a href="https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/voorvallen-luchtvaart/documenten/formulieren/2023/06/12/melden-voorval-met-een-drone-uas">Melden voorval met een drone</a>.&nbsp; [OPERATOR] will provide as much relevant information as possible to the ABL.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="48%">
<p><em>Dutch Safety Board (OVV)</em></p>
</td>
<td width="48%">
<p>Serious incidents and accidents with injury or death of a person must, after medical assistance has been provided and/or the emergency services have been alerted, be reported directly to the OVV by or on behalf of the AM. This can be done on the following telephone number: 0800-6353688.</p>
<p>Or this webpage: <a href="https://www.onderzoeksraad.nl/nl/report-incident">https://www.onderzoeksraad.nl/nl/report-incident</a></p>
</td>
</tr>

<td width="48%">

</td>

</td>
</tr>

<td width="48%">

</td>

</td>

<td width="48%">

</td>

</td>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0945he014s"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1itg4ja71246"><div class="page-break"></div></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiindn">Chapter A12: RECORD KEEPING PROCEDURES<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[RPE]<br></span></h1>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="nzYDthIRZdtfpWJxAJlr" id="article_nzYDthIRZdtfpWJxAJlr">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="nzYDthIRZdtfpWJxAJlr"><span class="shortcode">[A12.1]</span> <span class="name">Record-Keeping Procedures and logs</span></h2>
<p>Qualifications, certificates, flight information and other logs must be kept according to the retention periods mentioned in EU Regulation 2019/947.</p>
<p>UAS. SPEC.050 (1) (g) (i), (ii) and (iii) Responsibilities of the<strong> UAS Operator</strong> requires a retention period of at least 3 years for:</p>
<ul>
<li>qualifications and training courses for crew members and maintenance personnel after these persons have terminated their employment with the organisation or changed positions in the organisation;</li>
<li>The maintenance activities carried out on the UAS;</li>
<li>The information about UAS activities, including unusual technical or operational events and other data as required by the operating licence (OA), such as pilot logs and flight logs.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Logging flight information according to AMC1 UAS. SPEC.050 (1)(g) point c</strong></p>
<p>The <strong>UAS pilot</strong> records all his flights in a Pilot logbook and records the following points according to AMC1 UAS. SPEC.050(1)(g):</p>
<table width="100%" border="1" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 93.1931%;">

</td>
<td style="width: 6.08021%;">
<p><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Date</span></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 8.66753%;">
<p><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Flight location</span></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 6.08021%;">
<p><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Start time</span></p>
</td>

</td>
<td style="width: 7.50323%;">

</td>

<p>This flight information must be kept for at least 2 years in a way that protects against unauthorized access, damage, alteration and theft.</p>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0r6kj7tda6">PART B: UAS OPERATING INFORMATION</h1>
<p>This part contains all type-related instructions and procedures needed for a safe operation. It takes account of any differences between types, variants or individual UAS used by the operator.</p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0945he014u"><div class="page-break"></div>Chapter B1: TECHNICAL DESCRIPTION UAS<span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[AUA]</span></h1>

<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="LtMsCvybopsUNREMC55K" id="mcetoc_1in3piideib"><span class="shortcode">[B1.0]</span> <span class="name">INTRODUCTION SPECIFIC INFORMATION UAS</span></h2>
<p>This chapter contains specific information on the UASs used by [OPERATOR] and classified by [OPERATOR] for this UAS operation authorisation.</p>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1f1cnrnpr2g8"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f1cnrnpr2g9">Chapter B2: NORMAL PROCEDURES (UAS RELATED)<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[NPE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_JWKD8VnvBudCEph9rvgK" class="not_editable" data-id="JWKD8VnvBudCEph9rvgK">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="JWKD8VnvBudCEph9rvgK" id="mcetoc_1in3piideic"><span class="shortcode">[B2.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Normal Procedures</span></h2>
<p>Normal operational procedures are the guideline for planning safe UAS operations. In this chapter, [OPERATOR]'s normal operations are described. For the specific operations, see Chapter C3: Specific Flight Procedures. For both these cases, the operations are considered ‘under control’ of the pilot.</p>
<p>The contingency and emergency procedures are described respectively in Chapters C4 and C5.</p>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FNormal%20procedures.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=47f4ac24-77e1-4717-addb-e6cc7a25e50c" alt=""></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_kDfKRfTypQ01dorQHJEV" class="not_editable" data-id="kDfKRfTypQ01dorQHJEV">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1flbi8a7i2hr" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="kDfKRfTypQ01dorQHJEV"><span class="shortcode">[B2.1]</span> <span class="name">Assignment of Duties and its Distribution</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">To minimize human errors, a clear distribution and assignment of tasks are required.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Distribution and Assignment of Duties</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">See <a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a> and <a href="#article_ei5BA8TEGx9USGEJos5I">[A1.2] Responsibilities and Duties</a>.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Internal checklists</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">For an internal checklist to control that crew members are properly performing their assigned tasks, the checklist can be conducted. See <a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a>.</span></p>
</article>

<article id="article_uqTYOzBs5H0TDKNaAl0f" class="not_editable" data-id="uqTYOzBs5H0TDKNaAl0f">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="uqTYOzBs5H0TDKNaAl0f"><span class="shortcode">[B2.2]</span> <span class="name">External services and systems</span></h2>
<p><strong>External services (OSO#13)</strong></p>
<p><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light', sans-serif;"><span lang="EN-US">External services should be understood as any service provided to the UAS operator that is necessary to ensure the safety of a UAS operation and is provided by a service provider other than the UAS operator.</span></span></p>
<p><em><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"><span lang="EN-US">Declaration</span></span></em></p>
<p><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light', sans-serif;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;">[OPERATOR] ensures that the level of performance for any externally provided service that is necessary for the safety of the flight is adequate for the intended operation. [OPERATOR] declares that this level of performance is adequately achieved.&nbsp;</span></span></span></p>
<p><em>Role and responsibilities between [OPERATOR] and external providers</em></p>
<p><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;">Next table shows the external services in use for [OPERATOR]. </span>The roles and responsibilities of both parties are clearly defined per service.&nbsp;</span><strong></strong><strong></strong><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"></span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-family: 'Calibri Light',sans-serif;"><span style="font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;">*Processing the pre-flight checklist [appendix C4], [OPERATOR] ensures the level of performance. If any of the criteria are not met, the flight cannot be executed.</span></span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;">Preventing Degradation of C2/C3 Link</strong></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;">The C2/C3 link (Wifi/4G/5G), which is not an external system or service, is crucial for controlling the UA. During flight preparation, attention must be given to maintaining the quality of this link. The quality of the C2/C3 link can be compromised by:</span></p>
<ul>
<li>Reflection off water, buildings, obstacles, or large trees;</li>
<li>Electromagnetic (EM) radiation or strong radio signals from nearby high-voltage power lines, large substations, radio/TV transmission towers, or mobile phone towers;</li>
<li>Other nearby wireless equipment such as wifi or Bluetooth devices.</li>
</ul>
<p>Each Remote Controller of the UA from [OPERATOR] is equipped with the capability to monitor the degradation of the C2/C3 link.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_umb8e6lKU2zkzm2dMUdC" class="not_editable" data-id="umb8e6lKU2zkzm2dMUdC">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1flbi8a7i2hs" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="umb8e6lKU2zkzm2dMUdC"><span class="shortcode">[B2.3]</span> <span class="name">Coordination between the remote pilot and other personnel</span></h2>
<p>See the following chapter:&nbsp;<a href="#article_qjNIAh22LqCTaXsT7LBN">[A1.4] Crew Formation</a></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_jCmy2V0GKub17nU8yplv" class="not_editable" data-id="jCmy2V0GKub17nU8yplv">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="jCmy2V0GKub17nU8yplv" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11c"><span class="shortcode">[B2.4]</span> <span class="name">Methods to Exercise Operational Control</span></h2>
<p>There is simulator software available on the market. The crew member could utilise this to exercise operational control. Furthermore, see Chapter D2: TRAINING.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_1H6NEQoeBlKjM7FSzLcq" class="not_editable" data-id="1H6NEQoeBlKjM7FSzLcq">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="1H6NEQoeBlKjM7FSzLcq" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja71247"><span class="shortcode">[B2.5]</span> <span class="name">Pre-flight Preparation and Checklists VLOS flights</span></h2>
<p>(1) The site of the operation</p>
<p>The following points should be thoroughly considered when the flight operation is planned:</p>
<ul>
<li>The assessment of the area of operation and the surrounding area.</li>
<li>The assessment of the geographical zone (The operational volume should be located outside of any geographical zone identified as a flight restriction area for a protected aerodrome or any other designated zone, as specified by the responsible authority, unless the UAS operator has been granted appropriate permission).</li>
<li>Map potential electromagnetic fields (EM fields) in the vicinity, such as high-voltage power lines/boxes and communication towers, which could interfere with the Wi-Fi C2/C3 signal between the drone and the controller.</li>
<li>The compliance between visibility and planned range when the (Visual) Observer is used for the flight operation.</li>
<li>The class of airspace and other aircraft operations such as local aerodromes or operating sites.</li>
<li>The type of UA, including any details regarding inaccuracies, speed and range.</li>
</ul>
<p>See Chapter A7: FLIGHT PREPARATION for further details to include those points. For the checklists for the flight preparation, see <a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a>.</p>
<p>(2) Environmental and Weather Conditions</p>
<p>The crew member studies the adequate environmental and weather conditions to conduct the UAS operations. The remote pilot must always ensure that the UA stays clear of clouds.</p>
<p>Please refer to the sections in Chapter D1: GENERAL INSTRUCTION OF FLIGHT OPERATIONS for background information. <a href="#article_Kte1lesJaUhNRVu4fUVo"></a>To obtain the weather forecasts or conditions, please refer to the sections in Chapter A7: FLIGHT PREPARATION.<a href="#article_4fvWGKdg1PFBRY8suDm3"></a></p>
<p>(3) Coordination with third parties if applicable</p>
<p>(4) Crew Formation</p>
<p>Assignments can be categorised by their complexity. Depending on the complexity, an assignment can be performed alone or as a team. The complexity is linked to the flying situation and the type of operation. See section <a href="#article_qjNIAh22LqCTaXsT7LBN">[A1.4] Crew Formation</a> for further details.</p>
<p>Their responsibilities are described in section <a href="#article_ei5BA8TEGx9USGEJos5I">[A1.2] Responsibilities and Duties</a>.</p>
<p>(5) Crew Communication</p>
<p>The required communication procedures between the personnel in charge of duties essential to the UAS operation are described in Chapter A5: Crew Communication.<a href="#article_3rSPRcOG8DrY1ZdvT3O4"></a></p>
<p>(6) Compliance with any Specific requirement from the authority</p>
<p>See the section <a href="#article_QZuY26xOr1hkhFaKs0ue">[D1.1.1] Regulations in EU and the Netherlands</a>.&nbsp;</p>

<p>For the risk mitigations for the general procedures, see below.</p>

<p>(8) Pre-flight Preparation</p>
<p>Procedures to verify that the UAS can safely conduct the intended operations are described below.</p>
<p><strong>Preparation UAS</strong></p>
<p>The UAS is prepared before departure for the flight location.&nbsp;</p>
<ul>
<li>The configuration of the UAS is controlled in the logbook;</li>
<li>The structural integrity of the UAS is checked and, where necessary, repaired and/or prepared before departure to the operation site.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Flight Preparation</strong></p>
<p>The flight preparation also consists of the</p>
<ul>
<li>Check and prepare chargers/power supplies for the batteries.&nbsp;</li>
<li>Compile the correct configuration of the sensor and UAS combination.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Pre-flight Procedures</strong></p>
<p>The pre-flight check takes place near the take-off location. For the pre-flight checklist, see Appendix C.</p>
<p><br>Before the flight can commence, it is ensured that all persons on site (involved in the operation)<br>a. are informed about the risks of the operation;<br>b. are aware of the safety measures for the crew members;<br>c. have explicitly agreed to participate in the operation.</p>
<p>The person who performs the pre-flight check brings the UAS to the take-off location, thereby ensuring its validity. The UAS check should follow the manufacturer's manual. When all items on the checklist have been approved, the take-off procedure can be started.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_yF3gf10yZwvEIFXYtrwQ" class="not_editable" data-id="yF3gf10yZwvEIFXYtrwQ">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="yF3gf10yZwvEIFXYtrwQ" id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiindr"><span class="shortcode">[B2.6]</span> <span class="name">Launch and Recovery Procedures</span></h2>
<p>Those procedures are described below.</p>
<p><strong>Before Take-off Procedures</strong></p>
<p>The starting procedure is carried out by the pilot, (possibly in consultation with the payload operator).</p>
<ul>
<li>Place the UAS on the designated landing pad</li>
<li>The crew keeps a minimum safety distance of 5 meters from the UAS;</li>
<li>The pilot places the batteries in the UAS;</li>
<li>The pilot checks the functions of the control sticks, trim, switches, throttle neutral, etc.</li>
<li>The pilot activates the UAS's transmitter(s);</li>
<li>The pilot checks the functions and settings of the sensor in consultation with the payload operator;</li>
<li>The pilot verifies that the remote identification system is operational;</li>
<li>The pilot (in consultation with the payload operator) activates the sensor transmitter;</li>
<li>The pilot turns on the UAS and connects the transmitters;</li>
<li>Monitor the LED indicators and audio alerts;</li>
<li>Checking GNSS reception;</li>
<li>Set and check home point and altitude for automatic return;</li>
<li>Checking that the take-off area is still free and unoccupied;</li>
<li>In case of observers at the operation, checking that the communication latency is less than 15 seconds.</li>
</ul>
<p>Communicate "platform free"</p>
<ul>
<li>Start engines and check for detectable vibrations and/or noises.</li>
<li>The pilot verifies that the means to terminate the operation (FTS) is operational;</li>
</ul>
<p>Gradually increase engine speed and be alert to any abnormal noises or irregularities.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_HAzr4ciPm7wbl2Nl4FQG" class="not_editable" data-id="HAzr4ciPm7wbl2Nl4FQG">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhmla0m6b" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="HAzr4ciPm7wbl2Nl4FQG"><span class="shortcode">[B2.7]</span> <span class="name">In-flight Procedures</span></h2>
<p>Those procedures are described below.</p>
<p><strong>After Take-off Procedures</strong></p>
<p>The take-off procedure is performed by the pilot.</p>
<ul>
<li>Check that the take-off area is clear;</li>
<li>Test the flight controls: left, right, forward, backwards;</li>
<li>Take off and bring the UAS into the holding area for 20 to 30 seconds at a height of 2-3 meters to check for unusual vibrations or noises;</li>
<li>Centre all "sticks" to control GNSS "position hold" functionality;</li>
<li>Check battery voltage;</li>
<li>The landing gear is being retrieved.</li>
</ul>
<p>Communicate "ready for flight" to the crew.</p>
<p>The pilot flies the UAS to flight altitude and communicates with the observer to which direction the UAS is moving.</p>
<ul>
<li>The pilot keeps an eye on both the instruments and the UAS.</li>
<li>The observer monitors the environment of the operation, both on the ground and in the air.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Points of Attention During the Flight Operation</strong></p>
<p>At any time after take-off of the UAS and throughout the flight, the pilot of a UAS must comply with the following minimum instructions. The pilot:</p>
<ul>
<li>Indicates verbally in which direction he will manoeuvre the UAS;</li>
<li>Always keep the transmitter and the operation of the UAS in your own hands;</li>
<li>Do not lose sight of the UAS;</li>
<li>Manoeuvre the UAS in such a way that there is an opportunity to respond quickly to unexpected situations;</li>
<li>Position the UAS at a sufficiently safe distance from persons and goods on the ground.</li>
<li>To be able to send the UAS away from other (manned) air traffic.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Before Landing Procedures</strong></p>
<p>Descending procedure</p>
<ul>
<li>The pilot verbally indicates that he wants to start the descent and to what height;</li>
<li>Observer keeps an overview of the situation in the air and indicates whether the descent is possible;</li>
<li>The pilot manoeuvres the UAS to the indicated altitude and acknowledges when it has been reached.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pre-landing check procedure</p>
<ul>
<li>The UAS is positioned in the holding area;</li>
<li>The pilot verbally indicates that he wishes to initiate the landing;</li>
<li>Observer monitors the situation of the landing area and landing pad;</li>
<li>Observer indicates that the landing is possible;</li>
<li>The pilot verbally confirms the start of the landing procedure.</li>
</ul>
<p>Landing procedure</p>
<ul>
<li>The landing procedure is confirmed verbally by the pilot;</li>
<li>The landing gear is deployed;</li>
<li>The UAS is landed by the pilot at the appropriate landing location;</li>
<li>After a stable landing, the engines of the UAS are switched off;</li>
<li>After switching off the UAS, the transmitter sticks are placed on "neutral";</li>
<li>The landing is confirmed verbally by the pilot;</li>
<li>The flight is logged.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_xlWWAijWlxABHl6YEFPd" class="not_editable" data-id="xlWWAijWlxABHl6YEFPd">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1flbi8a7i2i0" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="xlWWAijWlxABHl6YEFPd"><span class="shortcode">[B2.8]</span> <span class="name">Post-flight Procedures</span></h2>
<p>The procedures are described below including the inspections to verify the conditions of the UAS.</p>
<p><strong>After landing procedure</strong></p>
<p>After landing, the pilot of a UAS must perform the following minimum actions:</p>
<ul>
<li>The pilot turns off the power to the UAS;</li>
<li>The pilot switches off the power supply to the transmitter and possibly the payload transmitter;</li>
<li>The pilot switches off the power to the payload in consultation with the payload operator;</li>
<li>The pilot visually checks the UAS for deviations and/or damage;</li>
<li>The pilot removes the batteries from the UAS.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Removal procedure UAS</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Do the UAS post-flight check according to the post-flight checklist (link);</li>
<li>The post-flight check is signed off in the logbook;</li>
<li>The UAS is stored in the designated flight case.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>UA motor shutdown</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The propellers are removed, folded and/or covered.</li>
<li>The UAS is stored in a flight case</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Post-flight</strong></p>
<p>The flight is logged;</p>
<p>After the flight, a debriefing is held with all crew involved.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_nUDZs5eFJyYqKjTxITRc" class="not_editable" data-id="nUDZs5eFJyYqKjTxITRc">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="nUDZs5eFJyYqKjTxITRc" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11e"><span class="shortcode">[B2.9]</span> <span class="name">Procedures for the Detection of Potentially Conflicting Aircraft</span></h2>
<p>The procedures are described below.</p>
<p><u>Aborting the Flight Operation</u></p>
<p>If it appears that the flight has to be cancelled due to an unforeseen circumstance, the observer checks whether the predetermined alternative landing location is still free of obstacles, people and animals. If necessary, the observer clears the site or - if that is not possible - looks for an alternative.</p>
<p><strong>Procedure for other air traffic in the area</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The observer identifies the air traffic and transmits information to the pilot;</li>
<li>The observer informs the pilot from which direction and, if possible, what height the other air traffic is coming from;</li>
<li>Let the UAS drop quickly, preferably to the holding area and/or on the landing pad;</li>
<li>If on the same course and no possibility of going down; swerve to the right;</li>
<li>Pause or stop the operation until other air traffic has passed.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="R21sfSgvjt5Vp6fctYHg" id="article_R21sfSgvjt5Vp6fctYHg">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="R21sfSgvjt5Vp6fctYHg" id="mcetoc_1in3piideif"><span class="shortcode">[B2.10]</span> <span class="name">Dangerous Goods</span></h2>
<p>For this [OPERATOR], flight operation with dangerous goods is not permitted.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="ghJ598wRFWZ4wVP4N4mx" id="article_ghJ598wRFWZ4wVP4N4mx">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="ghJ598wRFWZ4wVP4N4mx" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja71248"><span class="shortcode">[B2.11]</span> <span class="name">Equipment and Parts Safety Assurance</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">This chapter explains the process of ensuring the safety of equipment and parts used in various applications for the UAs.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">1. OEM Equipment/Parts<o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">"OEM" stands for Original Equipment Manufacturer. OEM equipment or parts are those that are made by the original manufacturer of a product. Using OEM equipment or parts means using components specifically designed and produced by the same company that originally manufactured the product. This is often preferred because OEM parts are typically guaranteed to fit and function properly.<br><br>2. Verification of Comparable Safety Standards<o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">This refers to demonstrating that non-OEM (non-original) equipment or parts can provide the same level of safety as the OEM ones. This involves a process of testing, analysis, or certification to ensure that the substitute parts meet the same safety standards and performance requirements as the original ones.<br><br>OEM components are preferred when replacing parts or equipment due to their seamless fit and function. Nevertheless, if non-OEM parts are chosen, it is essential to verify that they adhere to identical safety standards and performance benchmarks as the originals, necessitating a validation or substantiation procedure.<o:p></o:p></p>
</article>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdf7ngrq1rcn"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdd543d1196k"><div class="page-break"></div>PART C: SPECIFIC OPERATING PROCEDURES</h1>
<p>This part contains all instructions and information needed for the area of operation.</p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdd543d1196l"><div class="page-break"></div>Chapter C1: PDRA<span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[PD]</span></h1>
<article id="article_VWvmuKQV559kh1IfgNlI" class="not_editable" data-id="VWvmuKQV559kh1IfgNlI">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="VWvmuKQV559kh1IfgNlI" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11f"><span class="shortcode">[C1.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction PDRA</span></h2>
<p>A Pre-Defined Risk Assessment (PDRA) assists operators when applying for operational authorisation in a specific category. Even though the CAA (ILT in the Netherlands) will still need to validate the risk assessment and mitigating measures, significant time savings are achieved by providing these documents in a standardised format.</p>
<p>CAA applies the SORA methodology to define “Pre-Defined Risk Assessments” for a growing number of identified types of ConOps with known threats and acceptable risk mitigations. Pre-Defined Risk Assessments limit the administrative burden for both UAS operators and the authorities and stimulate innovation by lowering the entry level for certain types of operation.</p>
<p>Drone operators in de Specific category declare the PDRAs in combinations with a ConOps and an Operations Manual.&nbsp;</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_xTfLes7Ac3XyIdq7Cyij" class="not_editable" data-id="xTfLes7Ac3XyIdq7Cyij">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="xTfLes7Ac3XyIdq7Cyij" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja71249"><span class="shortcode">[C1.1]</span> <span class="name">PDRA-S01 </span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">See the table below for the overview of PDRA-S01.</span></p>
<table border="1" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100.039%;">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="width: 10.244%;">PDRA #</td>
<td style="width: 13.9117%;">Version/date</td>
<td style="width: 14.9234%;">UAS characteristics</td>
<td style="width: 7.85189%;">BVLOS/VLOS</td>
<td style="width: 22.2479%;">Overflown area</td>
<td style="width: 10.244%;">Max. range from remote pilot</td>
<td style="width: 9.99111%;">Max. height</td>
<td style="width: 10.6235%;">Airspace</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width: 10.244%;">PDRA-S01</td>
<td style="width: 13.9117%;">1.2/Sept 2023</td>
<td style="width: 14.9234%;">The maximum characteristic dimension of up to 3 m</td>
<td style="width: 7.85189%;">VLOS</td>
<td style="width: 22.2479%;">
<p>A controlled ground area that might be located in a populated area</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 10.244%;">VLOS</td>
<td style="width: 9.99111%;">150 m (120 m in the Netherlands)</td>
<td style="width: 10.6235%;">Controlled or uncontrolled, with a low risk of an encounter with manned aircraft</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p><strong>Final GRC: 3, FInal ARC: b, SAIL II</strong></p>
<p><strong>Operational characteristics (scope and limitations) summary</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>VLOS at all times</li>
<li>No autonomous operations</li>
<li>Maximum span width 3 meter</li>
<li>Maximum flight speed 5 m/s</li>
<li>Controlled Ground Area</li>
<li>Maximum 150 meter height (N.B. 120 meter height in the Netherlands)</li>
</ul>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy.appspot.com/o/images%2FDronewize%20PDRA-SO1%20above%20105m.png?alt=media&amp;token=0ce53268-563f-4c72-8ffb-afc033c9796a" alt="" width="350"></p>
<ul>
<li>When flying nearby an artificial obstacle that is taller than 105 meter, maximum height = obstacle height + 15 meter</li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Refer for details to section <a href="https://www.easa.europa.eu/document-library/easy-access-rules/online-publications/easy-access-rules-unmanned-aircraft-systems?kw=PDRA-S01">PDRA-S01</a></span></p>
<p></p>
<p><strong>Operational Mitigations</strong></p>
<p><u><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Operational Volume</span></u></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The UAS operator should define the operational volume for the intended operation, including:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">the flight geography; and</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">the contingency volume, with its external limit(s) at least 10 m beyond the limit(s) of the flight geography if the operation is conducted with untethered UA.</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">To determine the operational volume, the UAS operator should consider the position-keeping capabilities of the UAS in 4D space (latitude, longitude, height, and time)</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The procedure for defining the Operational Volume is described in <a href="#article_NiCKFeVZ0akFej1WJJki">Chapter</a> A6.</span></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Ground Risk</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy.appspot.com/o/images%2FGrondbuffer%20PDRA-S01.png?alt=media&amp;token=d3224c3c-3236-430b-a874-35113fd1bfc8" alt="" width="432"></span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">When determining the operational volume, the accuracy of the navigation solution, the UAS's flight technical error, the flight path definition error, and latencies should be considered.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The UAS pilot should apply emergency procedures immediately if there is an indication that the UA may exceed the limits of the operational volume. See the following sections;</span></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="#article_YW1f57Pvi7KomxoTjURa">[C4.4.1] Loss of Link (to fly away)</a></li>
<li><a href="#article_kFiTrz1kTuXUmN3QaR09">[C4.4.2] Autopilot Failure</a></li>
<li><a href="#article_geIRWVO3hq4bd5MpWKY4">[C4.4.4] Navigation Failure</a></li>
<li><a href="#article_l1IeW8Gu76Znc0rBWoSH">[C5.4] Fatal Error</a></li>
</ul>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The operator should establish a ground risk buffer to protect third parties on the ground outside the operational volume.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">For the operation of untethered UA, the ground risk buffer should cover a distance beyond the external limit(s) of the contingency area. The distance should be at least as defined below:</span></p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/dronestart-production.appspot.com/o/images%2Fgeneral%2FPDRA-S01%20ver1.2.png?alt=media&amp;token=f7dc907d-4204-41f1-bd95-2a7ce4d075e2" alt="" width="352"></p>
<p></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Air Risk</span><span data-preserver-spaces="true"></span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The operational volume should be outside any geographical zone corresponding to a flight restriction zone unless the operator has been granted the appropriate permission.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Before the flight operation, the operator should assess the proximity of the planned operation to manned aircraft activity.</span></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Observers</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Airspace observers are not necessary. UA observers might be useful for some types of operations.</span></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">UAS Operations</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">dedicated flight tests</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">simulations provided that the representativeness of the simulation means is proven for the intended purpose with positive results</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">upload updated information into the geo-awareness function</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">ensure that the controlled ground area is in place, effective and compliant with the above-mentioned mitigated measures at Ground Risk</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">VLOS</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">at a ground speed of less than 5 m/s in case of untethered UA</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">UAS Maintenance</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">See chapter A8: GENERAL MAINTENANCE.</span></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">External Services</span></p>
<p>See <a href="#article_uqTYOzBs5H0TDKNaAl0f">[B2.2] External System</a></p>
<p><strong>Provisions for the personnel in charge of duties essential to the UAS operation&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p><span style="text-decoration: underline;">UAS pilot</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">In addition to his responsibilities and duties (<a href="#article_ei5BA8TEGx9USGEJos5I">[A1.2] Responsibilities and Duties</a>), the UAS pilot, who is engaged in operations under this PDRA-S01 should;</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">hold a certificate of remote-pilot theoretical knowledge </span></li>
<li>hold an accreditation of completion of a practical-skill training course for this PDRA</li>
<li>before starting the UAS operation, verify that the means to terminate the flight of the UA, as well as the remote identification system, are operational and during the flight:&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">(a) keep the UA in VLOS and maintain a thorough visual scan of the airspace that is surrounding the UA to avoid any risk of collision with manned aircraft; the remote pilot should discontinue the flight if the operation poses a risk to other aircraft, people, animals, environment or property;&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">(b) for point (a) above, be possibly assisted by a UA observer; clear and effective communication should be established between the remote pilot and the UA observer (see also section <a href="#article_tP6Z8NeZDRzP1K5m42J6">[A5.2.1] Cooperation Pilot/Observer under VLOS</a>;&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">(c) use the contingency procedures that are defined by the UAS operator for abnormal situations, including situations where the remote pilot indicates that the UA may exceed the limits of the flight geography; and&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><span data-preserver-spaces="true">(d) use the emergency procedures that are defined by the UAS operator for emergencies, including triggering the means to terminate the flight when the remote pilot indicates that the UA may exceed the limits of the operational volume; the means to terminate the flight should be triggered at least 10 m before the UA reaches the limits of the operational volume (See section <a href="#article_YW1f57Pvi7KomxoTjURa">[C4.4.1] Loss of link</a>) or <a href="#article_VSe5v9SmcaGsdm7U7Mpy">[C4.4.4] Navigation Failure</a> or <a href="#article_l1IeW8Gu76Znc0rBWoSH">[C5.4] Fatal Error</a>).</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="i2QNRZ69JpFEuP5jbrte" id="article_i2QNRZ69JpFEuP5jbrte">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="i2QNRZ69JpFEuP5jbrte" id="mcetoc_1i2bqufuna"><span class="shortcode">[C1.1.1]</span> <span class="name">PDRA S01 Conditions</span></h2>
