The measurement of the distances should be adapted according to the geographical characteristics of the terrain, such as plains, hills, and mountains.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 89.6023px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 89.6023px;">
<p class="p1"></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 89.6023px;">
<p class="p1">1.10 When flying a UA within a horizontal distance of 50 m from an artificial obstacle that is taller than 105 m, the maximum height of the UAS operation may be increased up to 15 m above the height of the obstacle, at the request of the entity responsible for the obstacle.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 67.2017px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1"></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1">1.11 When UAS operators intend to operate at a height above 120 m, up to 150 m,</p>
<p class="p1">they should define a risk buffer according to point 3.8 below. (N.B. The maximum height is 120 m in the Netherlands)</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 67.2017px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1">Air space</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1">1.12 The UA should be operated:</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 67.2017px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1"></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1">1.12.1 in uncontrolled airspace, unless different limitations are provided for by the Member</p>
<p class="p1">States for their UAS geographical zones in areas where the probability of encountering manned aircraft is not low; or</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 112.003px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 112.003px;">
<p class="p1"></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 112.003px;">
<p class="p1">1.12.2 in controlled airspace after coordination and flight authorisation in accordance with the published procedures for the&nbsp; area of operation, to ensure that the probability of encountering manned aircraft is low.</p>
<p class="p1"><em>Note: Airspace with an air risk that is classified as not higher than ARC-b can be considered having a low probability of encountering manned aircraft.</em></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 22.4006px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 22.4006px;">
<p class="p1">Visibility</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 22.4006px;">
<p class="p1">1.13 The flight visibility should allow the remote pilot to conduct the entire flight in VLOS.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 67.2017px;">
<td style="width: 15.8087%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1">Others</p>
</td>
<td style="width: 84.2288%; height: 67.2017px;">
<p class="p1">1.14 The UA should not be used to carry dangerous goods, except for dropping items in connection with agricultural, horticultural or forestry activities where the carriage of such items does not contravene any other applicable regulations.</p>
<p class="p1"><span style="font-size: 12pt;"><em><span style="font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; color: black;">Note: </span><span style="font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;">The operator shall comply with applicable national or international regulations on the use of plant protection products, chemicals, dangerous substances, and preparations as appropriate. This includes Directive 2009/128/EC establishing a framework for Community action to achieve the sustainable use of pesticides, if applicable.</span></em></span></p>
</td>

<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f6k76vm36vj">Chapter C3: SPECIFIC OPERATIONAL PROCEDURES<span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[NPES]</span></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f6k76vm36vk"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1evpoli6mcv"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0g9fsrk22"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f0iq1lig3o4"></h1>
<article id="article_wpYy40eQxfJxQXBBK9C0" class="not_editable" data-id="wpYy40eQxfJxQXBBK9C0">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757ak5" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="wpYy40eQxfJxQXBBK9C0"><span class="shortcode">[C3.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Specific Flight Procedures</span></h2>
<p>In this section, specific procedures for a single operation are described.&nbsp;</p>
</article>
<p>The normal procedures and standard working methods from this manual apply to all types of operations. There is an increased risk in some operations of [OPERATOR]. These meet the conditions of the ConOps.<br>Additional conditions are set for these specific missions. These conditions are described by [OPERATOR] in the following procedures of this chapter.</p>
<p></p>
<article id="article_xq7um1ufXtn1bGyXrqOQ" class="not_editable" data-id="xq7um1ufXtn1bGyXrqOQ">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="xq7um1ufXtn1bGyXrqOQ" id="mcetoc_1in3piideih"><span class="shortcode">[C3.1A]</span> <span class="name">Procedure for flying in sparsely populated area over controlled ground area</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FLandschap%20inspecties.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=e008abc3-73dd-436e-80eb-75791bd56b7d" alt="" width="73"> UAS can be used for various applications in agriculture, for inspections and security in and around industrial sites and in other areas where in sparsely populated areas, but where uninvolved people are or may be present.</p>
<p>This procedure concerns flying in Sparsely Populated Area, for example within built-up areas where a Controlled Ground Area can be created. The condition for this procedure is that no uninvolved people are present within the Operational Volume. Uninvolved persons have not agreed with the risks associated with drone operations and should therefore be kept out of the Operational Volume. Examples of this are people in cars, trams, buildings, train etc.</p>
<p><strong>The risks to these operations</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Injuries to people and animals</li>
<li>Collision with other air traffic</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Mitigating measures</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Mapping the obstacles (and distances) and other risks in the terrain during flight preparation;</li>
<li>[OPERATOR] shall use additional observers and deposits (barriers) to ensure that no uninvolved persons can enter the Operational Volume;</li>
<li>The deposits and observers shall be recorded in the Operational Plan;</li>
<li>Use a flat terrain or platform for the take-off and landing area (or choose a UAS with landing gear);</li>
<li>Before the flight starts, the RTH function is tested, so that if the direct view is lost, the UAS pilot can give the RTH command so that the UA returns to the take-off area;</li>
<li>During the flight, consider animals/birds that can make an unexpected entrance within the Operational Volume. If there is 'interaction', shorten flight duration and abort operation;</li>
<li>Configure Geofence with a max radius and height.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_qWsCePreX8MnryWdUEPl" class="not_editable" data-id="qWsCePreX8MnryWdUEPl">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="qWsCePreX8MnryWdUEPl" id="mcetoc_1in3piideii"><span class="shortcode">[C3.2]</span> <span class="name">Procedure &gt; 120 meters AGL Flying Around Object</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2F400ft.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=7dbeb098-843c-4381-a89d-1891a2ad1adc" alt="" width="74"> [OPERATOR] wants to perform operations higher than 120 meters (400ft) AGL under certain circumstances. These flights are possible if the object that is part of the aerial work is higher than 120 meters (400ft) AGL within Atypical Airspace. If [OPERATOR] flies a maximum of 30 meters from a building or object today, that is called Atypical Airspace.</p>
<p><em>Risks during this operation</em></p>
<ol>
<li>Collision with other air traffic</li>
<li>Uncontrollability due to gusts of wind at height</li>
</ol>
<p><em>Measures</em></p>
<ol>
<li>Permission of the owner of the object to operate the flight;</li>
<li>Check whether the object and its height are displayed on the ICAO map 1:500,000;</li>
<li>Calculate the exact height of the AGL object.</li>
<li>Even with 1000 ft (≈300 meters) separation between manned aviation and the object, the crew must be alert and monitor the airspace;</li>
<li>Calculate the wind speed at altitude, see the section[D1.7] Gusts.</li>
<li>An additional risk assessment must be carried out for the site, which is recorded in the flight plan (and is part of it).</li>
<li>The maximum height of the UAS is never higher than 30 meters above the object to be inspected;</li>
<li>Flying above 120 meters (400ft) AGL should be done within 30 meters horizontally of the object to be inspected.</li>
<li>The pilot shall be in such a position that he always maintains visual contact with the UAS and that visibility is not obstructed by sunlight or the object;</li>
<li>The observer shall be in such a position that he stands between the object and the UAS and has a view of the surroundings and whether the UAS maintains sufficient distance from the object.</li>
<li>The pilot must take special account of the RTH function. This function ensures that the UAS can return to the home-point (often - but not always - the starting position). There must be no obstacle in the flight path when RTH is activated, whereby the pilot is cleared that when activating RTH, the UAS is first flown to the preset RTH altitude. The RTH height must therefore be at least 10 meters (30ft) above the highest point of the object that is part of the inspection. There should also be no obstacles in the RTH flight path. The pilot ensures that the landing site is free of obstacles and safe to land.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_LbBlRNOEmzddT9EiEeGd" class="not_editable" data-id="LbBlRNOEmzddT9EiEeGd">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="LbBlRNOEmzddT9EiEeGd"><span class="shortcode">[C3.3]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying in Civil CTRs</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FCiviel%20CTR.png?alt=media&amp;token=49c8a6a5-41fc-47bb-bd96-e8a47de7269f" alt="" width="69" height="31"></p>
<p>This specific procedure describes operations in civil-operated CTRs as part of the ConOps privileges. Most civil-operated CTRs are Class C airspace. Class C is controlled airspace where IFR and VFR flights are permitted.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Conditions for UAS flights</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>For the most up-to-date information, see <a href="https://www.lvnl.nl/ohd/bijzondere-vluchten/drones">https://www.lvnl.nl/ohd/bijzondere-vluchten/drones</a>.</li>
<li>For this specific scenario, it has been assumed that the flight will not take place over a populated area or assemblies of people, unless [OPERATOR] also has a procedure for this in the OM and this is part of the operating authorisation.</li>
<li>An exception is made for flying over industrial and port areas in the CTR. These industrial and port areas are mostly sparsely populated. [OPERATOR] also flies over industrial and port areas, so may, under the conditions of this scenario, also fly within the CTR.</li>
<li>This section describes the elements of the manual that according to SORA should be included with regard to flying within civil CTRs (Aerodromes) without the UA having a transponder.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Conditions for flights in civil CTRs</strong></p>
<p>Flights with a UA may operate in civil CTRs:</p>
<ul></ul>
<ul>
<li>Not above 120 meters AGL above the ground or water, unless nearby an obstacle or object within 30 meters horizontal and maximum of 30 meters above the object (A-typical airspace);</li>
<li>Within visual line of sight (VLOS);</li>
<li>Within the Uniform daylight period (UDP)(see AIP GEN 2.7). Note: An exemption is required to operate outside the UDP;</li>
<li>Flights are conducted under Visual Flight Rules (VFR), which means that there must be a minimum horizontal visibility of 5000 meters, a horizontal distance to cloud cover of at least 1500 meters and a vertical distance of at least 300 meters to cloud cover;</li>
<li>Special VFR is only possible if a specific clearance from the air traffic control responsible in the relevant CTR has been received for this. Special VFR: minimum 800 m horizontal view and ground view, cloud base at minimum 600 ft;</li>
<li>The flight remains within the area authorised by the LVNL operational helpdesk.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Separation in airspace class C and D</strong></p>
<p>In the CTRs of class C airspace (Schiphol, Rotterdam, Eelde, Lelystad, Maastricht), the following responsibilities regarding separation apply.</p>
<ul>
<li>IFR flights are separated by air traffic control from other IFR flights and VFR flights, including UA;</li>
<li>VFR flights are also separated from IFR flights;</li>
<li>VFR flights (including UA) receive information about other VFR traffic and 'traffic avoidance' advice upon request;</li>
<li>VFR traffic (including UA) is responsible for separation from other VFR traffic (both manned and unmanned).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Team composition for flights in civil CTRs</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Flights within civil CTRs are operated with:</p>
<ul>
<li>At least 1 pilot who has a valid EU pilot license A1/A2/A3 and/or additional training for the Specific category and;</li>
<li>At least 1 observer and;</li>
<li>Pilot and/or observer has a valid radiotelephony rating. [OPERATOR]'s R/T carries proof of the theory, practical and LPE (Language) exams with him.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Required equipment</strong></p>
<p>To establish two-way radio contact during a flight in the CTR, use is made of:</p>
<ul>
<li>An approved (Telecom) radio transmitting and receiving station with channel spacing 8.33 kHz;</li>
<li><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: Aptos, sans-serif;">A valid permit for frequency use issued by the Rijksinspectie Digitale Infrastructuur (RDI)</span>.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Required pre-flight actions</strong></p>
<p>Before a flight is executed, the following actions are performed:</p>
<ul>
<li>No later than 24 hours prior to the flight, [OPERATOR] requests permission (PPR = Prior Permission Required) from the Operational Helpdesk (OHD) via Godrone;</li>
<li>The UAS Operator submits a flight plan for each series of consecutive flights in one flight area (for multiple flight areas: one request and flight plan per flight area);</li>
<li>Within one clearance, all take-offs and landings that take place within the allocated time block and flight area can be made. These do not have to be individually registered and logged off with traffic control over the radio.</li>
<li>The flight cannot start until clearance from air traffic control has been obtained via the R/T;</li>
<li>If the flight is cancelled, [OPERATOR] will inform the operational helpdesk.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Submit flight plan (FPL)</strong></p>
<p>[OPERATOR] submits a flight plan via <a href="http://www.godrone.nl">www.godrone.nl</a>.&nbsp;</p>
<p>For assistance in completing the flight plan, the FSC can be reached by telephone at the number below. If the flight is cancelled, the flight plan must be canceled by telephone with the FSC of LVNL: 020 – 406 2315.</p>
<p><strong>VFR and special VFR rules in class C and D airspace</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>The following VFR rules apply in this class of airspace:</p>
<ul>
<li>Minimum horizontal visibility of 5000 meters.</li>
<li>Horizontal distance to clouds of at least 1500 meters.</li>
<li>Vertical distance of at least 300 meters to cloud cover.</li>
<li>Special VFR is only possible if a specific clearance has been received for this from the air traffic control responsible in the relevant CTR.&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
<p>Special VFR: minimum 800 m horizontal view and ground view, cloud base at minimum 600 ft.</p>
<p><strong>Units and Conversion</strong></p>
<p>In communication with ATC, the units used in aviation for flight direction (heading), altitude (altitude in feet, AMSL), speed in knots must be used.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Flight direction (heading)</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>To indicate the heading of the UA, the cardinal points or compass points are used, such as north, northeast, south, southwest, etc.</p>
<p>[OPERATOR] uses compass headings for this. The UA heading must be readily available during the flight. Working with compass headings is regularly trained, see chapter D2.</p>
<p><strong>Altitude</strong></p>
<p>Height is always indicated in relation to what is being measured. In communication with ATC, state:</p>
<ul>
<li>UA's altitude in relation to the mean sea level, calculated in feet.&nbsp;</li>
<li>UA's height in relation to local height (start/landing location)</li>
</ul>
<p>If the ground station does not provide this information but does provide the height in meters from the ground, convert this to the height in feet above the ground using the rule of thumb “meters to feet = number in meters times 3 plus 10%.”</p>
<p><strong>Speed</strong> &nbsp;</p>
<p>In aviation, speed is usually expressed in knots. For a UA, the speed used is usually in meters/second. The speed in knots can be obtained by multiplying the speed in meters/sec by the number 1.9438. This will be the number 2 for convenience.</p>
<p>When the speed is given in communication with air traffic control, the following formula is used: speed in m/s x 2 = speed in knots</p>
<p><strong>Contingency procedures</strong></p>
<p>See chapter C4 Abnormal or Contingency Procedures.</p>
<p><strong>Emergency Procedures</strong></p>
<p>A CTR is a piece of airspace established around a controlled airport. The purpose of the CTR is to protect air traffic to and from the airport against other air traffic. In the CTR there is a real chance of lower air traffic. One of the risks with UA is a fly away. The chance of a fly away must therefore be reduced as much as possible.</p>
<p>[OPERATOR] takes operational and technical mitigating measures for this. It is important here that a 'single point of failure' should never be the cause of a fly away.</p>
<p><strong>Flight area</strong></p>
<p>When determining the flight area, in addition to the standard procedure, the location of the flight area in relation to the airport area must be taken into account. [OPERATOR] makes every effort to prevent the flight from flying into the airport in the event of a small deviation in the flight profile or a fly away. This can be achieved by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Choosing a flight direction, for example, parallel to or downstream of the CTR (See figure 1);</li>
<li>Turns directed down the CTR (See figure 2);</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/dronestart-production.appspot.com/o/images%2Fgeneral%2FCTR%20parallel.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=721d0386-0242-4965-9689-6c8fb3194cd3" alt="" width="408" height="265" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 1: Flying Parallel to the runway</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/dronestart-production.appspot.com/o/images%2Fgeneral%2FCTR%20downstream.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=f9d49345-4bf3-4007-babb-fef05f19afde" alt="" width="433" height="276"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure 2: Turns directed down the runway</p>
<p>N.B. This is only meant to sketch the flying directions. The distances between the runway and the operational volume is not the actual.</p>
<p><strong>Emergency response plan (ERP)</strong></p>
<p>See Chapter C6 EMERGENCY RESPONSE PLAN.</p>
<p><strong>Training (internal)</strong></p>
<p>See for this <a href="#article_Amg1RhPJCEGzwnk6E53X">[D2.1] Training General</a>. Additional training is provided for this specific R/T procedure.</p>
<p><strong>Flight Process</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The person who conducts radio communication with air traffic control (provided a valid R/T) does a radio check on the relevant Delivery frequency just before the UAS activity at the relevant flight location.</li>
<li>After the radio check, Delivery refers the observer to the relevant Tower frequency. At this frequency, the observer makes a clearance request for the flight.</li>
<li>The tower controller provides the clearance based on the current situation in the control zone (CTR). A clearance authorizes the pilot to perform the UAS activity with the UA in accordance with the flight plan and any additional conditions of the air traffic controller. The UA does not start from an airport where local air traffic control is provided. As a result, no take-off and/or landing clearance is provided, but only clearance for the flight.</li>
<li>Within the same clearance, all take-offs and landings that occur within the allocated time block and flight area can be made. These do not have to be registered and deregistered individually over the radio with traffic control. During the flight, the RT'er monitors the frequency and specified telephone for any indications or adjustments or cancellation of clearance.</li>
<li>The flight is canceled by the RT operator via radiotelephony to the air traffic controller as soon as the entire UAS activity within the relevant flight area has ended and no more flights will be made in the time block that was reserved for this.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Radiotelephony (RT)</strong><br>Communication by radiotelephony takes place according to strict rules. This is to keep communication short and clear. The RT'er calls the traffic control within the reserved time block, and is referred to the TWR traffic control if the signal is good. [OPERATOR] creates its own call-sign (PH number is not valid) and uses this in the communication/request with LVNL. For example: UNMANNED-BBW.</p>
<p><strong>Radio Check</strong></p>

<p><strong>Ending the flight</strong></p>
<p>When the flight is completed, the RT member reports the flight to the TWR controller. If the entire UAS activity has to be terminated due to an uncontrolled landing (crash) of the UAS, the same radiotelephony is used as at the conclusion of the flight. It is also possible that the flight has to be temporarily interrupted or terminated entirely on the instructions of air traffic control.</p>

<p><strong>Loss of control over the UAS</strong><br>If control over the UAS is lost, air traffic control should be informed as soon as possible.</p>
<table border="1" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 99.9132%;">

<p><strong>Loss of communication</strong><br>In the event of loss of communication with the tower during the flight, the pilot lands the UA as soon as possible and immediately informs the TWR unit by telephone.</p>
<p><strong>After the flight</strong><br>Completing flight plan at OHD. It is not necessary to conclude a flight plan with the FSC.</p>
</article>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<article id="article_THzTyJt2ijxpuwGSR0Kl" class="not_editable" data-id="THzTyJt2ijxpuwGSR0Kl">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1gf5tglhd7c" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="THzTyJt2ijxpuwGSR0Kl"><span class="shortcode">[C3.3.1]</span> <span class="name">CTR Niederrhein Weeze</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FCiviel%20CTR.png?alt=media&amp;token=49c8a6a5-41fc-47bb-bd96-e8a47de7269f" alt="" width="69"> This sub-procedure is specific to the CTR managed by ATC Niederrhein Weeze.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy.appspot.com/o/images%2FNiederrhein%20CTR%20ASWV6.1.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=3ea33fca-0a07-47c4-939d-7f69d1abbe0d" alt="" width="440"></p>
<p>For flights in Niederrhein CTR, a separate procedure applies with regard to authorisation. These must be coordinated with German air traffic control. At least 2 weeks before the start of the UAS operation, an e-mail is sent to the German air traffic controller: bnl@dfs-as.aero.</p>
<p>The request shall specify the following elements:</p>
<ul>
<li>Type fly operation;</li>
<li>Location of the flight operation;</li>
<li>Date of flight operation;</li>
<li>Time of the flight operation;</li>
<li>Contact details of the UAS team.</li>
</ul>
<p>On the basis of art. 2.2.2 of the "Nachrichten Für Luftfahrer" clearance will be issued if the following conditions are met:</p>
<ul>
<li>The permitted MTOM of the UA is 25 kilograms or less;</li>
<li>The flight is performed in the pilot's VLOS;</li>
<li>The minimum distance to the border of the airport is 1.5 km;</li>
<li>Priority shall always be given to manned aircraft;</li>
<li>The flight is operated under VMC VFR minimums.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_2ZnRXuX7wIyblWFGZP8U" class="not_editable" data-id="2ZnRXuX7wIyblWFGZP8U">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="2ZnRXuX7wIyblWFGZP8U" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7124b"><span class="shortcode">[C3.4]</span> <span class="name">Procedure Flying within Military CTRs</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FMil%20CTR.png?alt=media&amp;token=fee83d55-ccd0-4000-a343-62cace547e3e" alt=""> The airspace of the military CTR is class D. If relevant, other traffic is informed about the drone operation by military air traffic control.</p>
<p>To fly missions within a military CTR, [OPERATOR] takes the following mitigating measures:</p>
<ol>
<li>Obtain military air traffic control contact and clearance prior to the operation;</li>
<li>Submit by email from:
<ul>
<li>Flight Location (GNSS)</li>
<li>Flight altitude</li>
<li>Flight duration</li>
<li>Flight starting time and finishing time</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Be aware of the current local weather information of the relevant CTR;</li>
<li>Maintained line of communication with CTR military air traffic control during operation;</li>
<li>Telephone registration and deregistration of an operation to military air traffic control CTR.</li>
</ol>
<p>The most current application form is requested by [OPERATOR] from the relevant air base. The application must be submitted to this air base at least 24 hours prior to the flight. Mail is not read on weekends.<br>When determining the operational volume, the location of the flight area in relation to the CTR must be taken into account in addition to the standard procedure. This can be achieved by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Choosing a flight direction, for example, parallel to or downstream of the CTR;</li>
<li>Turns down the CTR.</li>
</ul>
<p>So if permission is required for operations on weekends or on Mondays, these must be submitted before 12:00 on Friday. On the day of the flight, military traffic control must be contacted (by telephone) at least 15 minutes before the start.</p>
<p>If you coordinate a NOTAM by yourself, then via <a href="mailto:ais@mindef.nl">ais@mindef.nl</a><br>In a civil CTR or in/under civil airspace <a href="mailto:ops_helpdesk@lvnl.nl">ops_helpdesk@lvnl.nl</a><br>Outside the military CTR in/under military airspace <a href="mailto:aocs.amc@mindef.nl">aocs.amc@mindef.nl</a></p>
<p><strong>Emergency procedure</strong><br>In the event of a fly-away and/or crash, contact military traffic control immediately. Below is an overview of contact details:</p>

<article id="article_42TYweoi9EeILUU1St0L" class="not_editable" data-id="42TYweoi9EeILUU1St0L">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="42TYweoi9EeILUU1St0L" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11k"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5]</span> <span class="name">Procedures flying close to Objects, Roads, Buildings</span></h2>
<p>Flying closer to buildings, roads, railways, etc. are subject to EU regulations in principle under the procedure flying outside adjacent buildings. Depending on around which object/road/building the drone operation would be conducted, the additional conditions are added. Therefore the procedures are separately mentioned in this section.&nbsp;</p>
</article>
<p>C3.5.1 Flying close to/within an industrial area and port area<br>C3.5.2 Flying close to vessels<br>C3.5.3 Flying close to vehicles<br>C3.5.4 Flying close to objects/infra structures<br>C3.5.5. Fly near (not-above) railways<br>C3.5.6 Flying close to adjacent buildings<br>C3.5.8 Flying close to roads up to 80km/h<br>C3.5.9 Flying close to ≥ 80 km/h (highway) roads<br>C.3.5.10 Flying over road/water</p>
<p></p>
<article id="article_5l1R5p6SakJ8JgbLY4pV" class="not_editable" data-id="5l1R5p6SakJ8JgbLY4pV">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="5l1R5p6SakJ8JgbLY4pV" id="mcetoc_1in3piideil"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.1]</span> <span class="name">Procedure for flying near/within Industrial area and Port area</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FIndustrie%20inspecties.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=b28d2a01-da28-4cb5-8908-46ecc813af62" alt="" width="68"> [OPERATOR] wrote this procedure for conducting a safe drone operation in an industrial area or in a port area.</p>
<p><strong>Specific risks in industrial and port areas</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Explosion hazard and fire hazard.</li>
<li>Flying against people and objects, vehicles and vessels, see also [C3.5.2] Procedure flying near vessels and [C3.5.3] Procedure flying near vehicles.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Additional mitigating measures</strong><br>In addition to the normal procedures, the following measures apply:</p>
<ol>
<li>During the flight preparation, information is requested about the risks of explosion and fire.</li>
<li>Flight planning takes into account possible EM sources, buildings and wetlands for correct GNSS reception.</li>
<li>Flights are carried out when risky activities around the flight location are minimal.</li>
<li>Landowner permission has been obtained where the operation is to be performed (for take-off and landing).</li>
<li>No uninvolved people may be present in the flight area. The flight crew is aware of the risks of the operation.</li>
<li>Position the flight crew in such a way that a clear view can be kept of the distance to the object, in particular the positioning of the observer;</li>
<li>Analysis of wind current and probability of turbulence around object by analyzing the environment for indicators of the wind direction on location. See also the section on the venturi effect in [D1.6] Turbulence. If the wind force is greater than 3, choose to fly controlled slow in manual mode.</li>
<li>Flight crew has (if necessary) VCA certification (Dutch certificate for Safety, Health and Environment ) and/or a responsible person from the client with knowledge about potential risks and measures.</li>
<li>Drivers of the vehicles or captains of the vessels, part of the flight operations are briefed about the safety risks (what can be expected, what can go wrong and what are the do's and don'ts);</li>
<li>If an operation has to take place in the vicinity or in a port, [OPERATOR] must obtain permission from the security officer of the port facility (Port Security Officer);</li>
</ol>
<p>In addition, it can be decided in consultation with the manager of the area/building to take additional mitigating measures.<br><br></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_VyUtzs1SLGCk6kuvuBb0" class="not_editable" data-id="VyUtzs1SLGCk6kuvuBb0">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="VyUtzs1SLGCk6kuvuBb0"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.2]</span> <span class="name">Procedure for flying close to Vessels</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2F25%20meter%20schip%3Avoertuig.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=cb7daa77-392d-466a-a685-f5c53dce8773" alt="" width="68" height="30"> [OPERATOR] photographs, films or inspects specific construction objects around or in (industrial) construction areas, harbour areas and waterways. The most significant risk is damage to a vessel and/or injury to the crew. Therefore, the following mitigating measures apply:</p>
<ol>
<li>The pilot flies no closer than 10 meters or more, depending on the required ground risk buffer horizontally in the vicinity of a vessel;</li>
<li>Advice maximum wind speed &lt; 19 km/h (wind force up to 3). Higher than wind force 3: wind direction away from the object.</li>
<li>Position the flight crew in such a way that a clear view can be kept of the actual distance to the object, in particular, the positioning of the observer;</li>
<li>The return to Home function is set in such a way that there is no risk of collision with the object, an explicit consideration is made to choose dynamic or static home position;</li>
<li>Analysis of wind currents and probability of turbulence around objects by analysing the environment for indicators of the wind direction at the location. See also the section on the Venturi effect in&nbsp;<a href="#article_u6S19kJ8tnIBziluhJoS">[D1.6] Turbulence</a>.</li>
<li>Informing people in the immediate vicinity of the flight location.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_uvNifYE19dME5OkxqAg8" class="not_editable" data-id="uvNifYE19dME5OkxqAg8">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="uvNifYE19dME5OkxqAg8" id="mcetoc_1in3piidein"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.3]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying close to Vehicles</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FPictogram%20Droneconsultancy%20operaties%20nabij%20voertuigen.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=d87446f6-99cb-41c7-ad6f-6d640cfa6ac5" alt="" width="84"> The greatest risk of this operation is damage to a vehicle or injury to people getting in/out/walking. [OPERATOR] takes the following measures to fly near vehicles:</p>
<ol>
<li>Vehicles are stationary during the mission and no people are getting in/out of the vehicles.</li>
<li>Position the flight crew in such a way that a clear view can be kept of the distance to the object, especially the positioning of the observer.</li>
<li>Taking into account the required ground risk buffer as noted in the Operational Plan.</li>
<li>Analysis of wind flows and probability of turbulence around object by analyzing the environment for indicators of the wind direction on location. See also the section on the venturi effect in<br>[D1.6] Turbulence.</li>
<li>Informing people who are present in the immediate vicinity of the flight location.</li>
<li>Observer(s) with experience flying on high-risk experience and briefed with all possible specific risks on site.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_mAEKphUvk1bjHNolAnZj" class="not_editable" data-id="mAEKphUvk1bjHNolAnZj">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="mAEKphUvk1bjHNolAnZj" id="mcetoc_1in3piideio"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.4]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying close to objects/civil engineering structures</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2F25%20meter%20object.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=b910ca74-0c34-46fc-8f4a-58269e54ebd8" alt="" width="81"> [OPERATOR] inspects, photographs or films objects/civil engineering structures.</p>
<p>Risks for this type of operation are;</p>
<ul>
<li>Collision with object or artwork;</li>
<li>Sudden wind turbulence effects around the artwork or object.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mitigating measures</p>
<ol>
<li>Position the flight crew in such a way that a clear view can be kept of the distance to the object, especially the positioning of the observer.</li>
<li>There should be no objects between the UAS and the flight crew.</li>
<li>In situations where there is a high probability of external influences, we use an additional observer. This can, for example, monitor traffic, people or vessels.</li>
<li>Return to Home function set in such a way that there is no risk of collision with the object, a clear consideration is made to choose dynamic or static home position. This also takes into account any overhanging parts of the object or civil engineering structures that could affect the return to home function.</li>
<li>Take into account the influence of the object on the operation of the compass. [OPERATOR] therefore flies a short distance from the pilot.</li>
<li>Keep a minimum distance to the object of more than 10 meters.</li>
<li>When flying over an object or start from or land on the object, the owner should have given permission.</li>
<li>Analysis of wind currents and probability of turbulence around object by analyzing the environment for indicators of the wind direction on location.</li>
<li>Influence of radiation from antennas on the object, electricity pylon etc. Flying close to this type of EMC-causing equipment is not allowed with [OPERATOR]. If necessary, equipment that causes the radiation can be turned off temporarily.</li>
<li>Informing persons who are present in the immediate vicinity of the operational volume.</li>
<li>Turn off operational volume and always keep the area under UAS clear of persons and/or vehicles, remove them immediately from operational volume if present.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_hrErLMUCnmrU4eAfzWp0" class="not_editable" data-id="hrErLMUCnmrU4eAfzWp0">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="hrErLMUCnmrU4eAfzWp0" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7124d"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.5]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying close to railways</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fvlakbij%20sporen.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=df32caab-73f7-4fa6-9935-2d394e3ed676" alt="" width="74"></p>
<p>[OPERATOR] regularly records near railways. Many client's buildings are located right next to it. For the majority of these shots, it is not required to get closer than 10 meters (= outside the danger zone). [OPERATOR] must also take into account the ground risk buffer associated with the ConOps. This procedure concerns flying up to a maximum of 10 meters on railways, where, in principle, no coordination with Prorail is necessary.</p>
<p><strong>Risks</strong></p>
<p>Safety when working near railways is determined by two risks:</p>
<ol>
<li>The risk of collision with people and/or equipment by track-bound equipment (e.g. trains, work trains, maintenance equipment etc.);</li>
<li>The risk of electrocution due to contact with the UAS with electrically charged parts of the power supply installation or train protection installation.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Risk of collision</strong><br>The danger zone (A) is the zone where there is a risk of collision. In this scenario, [OPERATOR] stays well outside of zones A,B and C.</p>
<p>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FGevarenzones%20rondom%20spoor.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=b2ae6b7a-8c66-48ea-b875-c2573e56f1a1" alt="" width="359"></p>
<p>The dimensions of this zone depend on the speed of the train or other track-related equipment. Outside the danger zone, there are two zones (B and C) which, due to their proximity to danger zone A, are exposed to side effects from passing track-bound equipment.</p>
<p><strong>Dimensions</strong></p>
<p>The boundary of danger zone A depends on the maximum permitted speed on the track. The table below defines the dimensions that apply to the different travel speeds.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20Tabel%20met%20afmetingen%20nabij%20spoor.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=3823119c-d4b6-4812-8db0-3ae9e7de35ee" alt="" width="554"></p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fc.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=db08eae8-96de-4903-9c59-7973d95e3387" alt=""></p>
<p class="p2">Danger Zone B has a default size of 1 meter and starts at the boundary of Danger Zone A. Proximity Zone C has a default size of 1.75 meters and starts at the boundary of Proximity Zone B.</p>
<p class="p2"><strong>Risk of electrocution</strong></p>
<p class="p2">[OPERATOR] flies no closer than 10 meters from the track in this scenario, so the chance of electrocution is nil.</p>
<p class="p2"><strong>Mitigating measures</strong></p>
<p class="p2">The following measures are taken to mitigate the risks mentioned:</p>
<ul>
<li class="p2">Keep at least 10 meters (or more = depending on ground risk buffer) horizontal distance from the center from the track. That is well beyond the minimum safe distance of 5.75 m.</li>
<li class="p2">If a safety fence is present, it is always flown from outside the fence and the drone remains outside the fence.</li>
<li class="p2">To prevent electrocution of the UAS on contact with the track or cutting edge equipment, the flight planning takes into account as much as possible a flight plan in which the aircraft is flown off the track.</li>
<li class="p2">When a train passes, the flight should be interrupted. This is possible in 3 ways:
<ul>
<li class="p2">The UAS is retrieved to the take-off and landing location and can idle there</li>
<li class="p2">The UAS will hover at a safe location at a height of 3 meters. These locations are marked as 'hover locations' in the operational</li>
<li class="p2">The UAS will land and idle at designated take-off and landing locations</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="p2">A minimum distance of 25 meters will be kept from passing trains.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="f0G3wFsTIuX5BZnzWWvH" id="article_f0G3wFsTIuX5BZnzWWvH">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="f0G3wFsTIuX5BZnzWWvH"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.6A]</span> <span class="name">Flying nearby populated areas under Basic Containment</span></h2>
<p><img height="36" width="81" alt="" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fnabij%20boven%20bebouwing%20en%20steden.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=018e9455-24f1-4494-943d-60ea332f395d"> This operation concerns flying closer to populated and urban areas. It covers UAS operations nearby villages and cities, but not for flying within these cities.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Guidelines for flights near populated areas under Basic Containment, aligned with the additional conditions specified in the Alt/24/0064 Triggers for Enhanced Containment.</p>
<p><strong>Assumptions for flights closer to adjacent buildings</strong></p>
<p>Flights may take place near (not above) buildings under the following conditions/mitigating measures:</p>
<ul>
<li>flights are conducted under Visual Flight Rules (VFR), which means that there must be a minimum horizontal visibility of 5000 meters, a horizontal distance to cloud cover of at least 1500 meters and a vertical distance of at least 300 meters to cloud cover;</li>
<li>at a low airspeed such that the UA cannot crash outside the control area in the event of an engine failure;</li>
<li>with a maximum flight altitude above ground/water determined in the flight plan;</li>
<li>without infringing on the privacy of people on the ground or in buildings;</li>
<li>with an adequate ERP, should something go wrong. The standard emergency procedures of [OPERATOR] are used for this, see Chapter C5: Emergency procedures.</li>
<li><span style="text-decoration: underline;">UA smaller than 1 meter and max speed &lt;25m/s</span>: the average population density between the outer limit of the ground risk buffer and the adjacent area (5 km) is less than 50,000 people per square kilometre, and the number of people within 1 km of the operational volume is less than 40,000.</li>
<li><span style="text-decoration: underline;">UA smaller than 3 meter and max speed &lt;35 m/s</span>: the average population density between the outer limit of the ground risk buffer and the adjacent area (5 km) is less than 5,000 people per square kilometre, and the number of people within 1 km of the operational volume is less than 40,000. (sheltering is applicable).</li>
</ul>
<p><br>When selecting and organizing this ground area, the following must be taken into account (and be stated in the flight plan):</p>
<ul>
<li>Minimum and maximum height above the object.</li>
<li>The set height of the RTH function</li>
<li>Maximum height above ground/water.</li>
<li>The horizontal speed (low speed).</li>
<li>Wind speed and wind direction.</li>
<li>Turbulence around the object and the 'venturi effect'.</li>
<li>The proximity and number of “uninvolved” people to be expected.</li>
<li>The number of inhabitants in the adjacent area.</li>
<li>Events with more than 40.000 people in the adjacent area.&nbsp;</li>
<li>Number of required observers and any traffic controllers.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Reliable connection with C3 link</strong><br>A malfunction must not lead to an incident. [OPERATOR] selects and tests the quality of the connection between the transmitter and the UA, paying attention to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Appropriate radio frequency (RF) for the local conditions</li>
<li>Data security, spoofing and hacking</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Design of the UAS and emergency measures</strong></p>
<p>[OPERATOR] selects the following mitigating measures to prevent risks of collision with people and/or buildings.</p>
<p>The UAS that has been found to be airworthy and maintained according to established procedures must meet a number of minimum technical requirements, including loss of link procedures, return to home procedures, geofencing, and the possibility of manual flight in case of GNSS problems. The basic principle is that a single failure may not immediately lead to an incident.</p>
<p>If the connection fails, the UA automatically enters the Return to home procedure.</p>
<p><strong>Use of external data sources, such as weather, air traffic</strong><br>[OPERATOR] must verify during flight preparation and prior to flight whether the information presented on drone apps and flight management systems corresponds to government information such as KNMI and LVNL (notes, no-fly zones).</p>
<p><br><strong>Emergency Response Plan (ERP) - Emergency Plan</strong></p>
<p>In addition to the standard emergency procedures in this manual, see chapter C5: Emergency procedures, an ERP is required for this type of operation. This ERP should limit crash-escalating effects. [OPERATOR] reviews this ERP with all relevant third parties identified in the ERP.</p>
<ul>
<li>The ERP is validated through a representative tabletop exercise (e.g. chronological discussion of steps during a possible incident or accident).</li>
<li>The ERP must be consistent with the ERP training syllabus, see&nbsp;<a href="#article_9MmFXZjgMkLvw5Be70Gy">[D2.5] Practical Training for Emergency Procedures.&nbsp;</a></li>
<li>An ERP training program (see&nbsp;<a href="#article_9MmFXZjgMkLvw5Be70Gy">[D2.5] Practical Training Emergency Procedures</a>) is available. An administration of the ERP training followed by the relevant crew is prepared and updated. In addition, the competences of the relevant crew are verified by an authorized third party (ILT) through the approval of this manual, see&nbsp;<a href="#article_ei5BA8TEGx9USGEJos5I">[A1.2] Responsibilities and Duties</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Emergency services are called in the event of a crash, see Chapter C6: ERP (Emergency Response Plan).</p>
<p><strong>VLOS Deconfliction Scheme – phraseology</strong></p>
<p>During the operation, the phraseology from this manual is used, see Chapter A5: Crew Communication.</p>
<p><strong>Maintenance UAS</strong></p>
<p>The maintenance procedures in this manual are followed and the maintenance performed is recorded, see<br><a href="#article_vThipL9VVFJ8Zz0hWwEy">[A8.0] Introduction Maintenance</a>.</p>
<p><strong>Operational procedures, contingency and emergency procedures</strong></p>
<p>Specific to this scenario, the contingency and emergency procedures are important, mitigating the greatest risks for flying within urban areas. Include the following points of attention in the Emergency Response Plan and in the flight plan:</p>
<ul>
<li>Wind turbulence, in particular, is a concern with the risk of loss of control and a crash.</li>
<li>During flight preparation, conduct research into wind speeds and venturi effects in the flight area.</li>
<li>In addition, there is the risk of injury due to uncontrollability. That is why the operational volume in which the aircraft is flown is secured with temporary barriers and/or traffic controllers.</li>
<li>Information boards will be placed.</li>
<li>An observer must be present in addition to the pilot. This observer has the task to communicate well to those involved in the environment and to keep people away.</li>
<li>The aircraft is flown at a low speed to minimize the effects of a crash.</li>
<li>The ERP/flight plan contains the current numbers of the emergency services in the vicinity of the flight operation. The ERP is present at the flight location.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Training</strong></p>
<p>Until now, this scenario has not been flown in the Netherlands. Therefore, for this specific scenario, a so-called 'self-declaration' is required for training containing the following additional components:</p>
<ul>
<li>Application and training of operational procedures</li>
<li>Communication</li>
<li>UA flight route planning</li>
<li>Leadership, teamwork and self-direction</li>
<li>Problem solving and decision making</li>
<li>Situational Awareness</li>
<li>Managing work</li>
<li>Coordination and transfer of tasks.</li>
</ul>
<p>These aspects have been added to the basic training program of [OPERATOR] in&nbsp;<a href="#article_awO2ILwDydA9jQ69xrHr">[D2.1] Training General</a>. Self-declaration means that the operator can prove that the pilot has been trained in the above aspects.</p>
<p><strong>Privacy aspects</strong></p>
<p>If recordings are made of homes or business premises (for example, for inspections), the residents will have to be informed in advance about the operation. According to the GDPR, the operator must, among other things, make it clear for what purpose the recordings are made, how the data is processed, and who has access to the data. See also <a href="#article_9195UBNiPKqvRZB73nFx">[A10.1] Guideline Nuisance</a>.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_XRFsVkxOHo83tQqJ6uQV" class="not_editable" data-id="XRFsVkxOHo83tQqJ6uQV">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="XRFsVkxOHo83tQqJ6uQV" id="mcetoc_1in3piideir"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.8]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying close to motorways (the speed limit is up to 80km/h)</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fautoweg.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=46324b27-3fa0-4c88-8e4f-10662eea7d96" alt="" width="79"> Due to their good accessibility, many clients have office and business premises built and managed near roads with a maximum speed of up to 80 km/h and have these inspected regularly.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Risks for this operation</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Traffic collision and/or traffic distraction with the risk of an accident. This operation, therefore, requires more of the flight crew present.</span></p>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Mitigation Measures</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">The following mitigating measures are in force for this operation:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Observer specifically monitoring the ground situation:&nbsp;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">To have a shortest possible time of exposure, and thus cross at right angles. Do not hover above the road;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Restrict off the flight location (pylons and/or restrict tapes) and keep the area under UA clear of persons. If they are present, immediately remove them from the flight location;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Flying during quiet hours and outside rush hours;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Return to Home function is set in such a way that there is no risk of collision with the object, a clear consideration is made to choose a dynamic or static home position;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Maintain a minimum horizontal distance from the road of wider than 5 meters;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Analysis of current wind and the possibility of turbulence around the object by analyzing the environment for indicators of the wind direction on location;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Informing persons near the flight location;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Fly for the shortest period possible over the road, i.e., cross it at a right angle.</span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_7STAvjtC7QOP4VO3kCcY" class="not_editable" data-id="7STAvjtC7QOP4VO3kCcY">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="7STAvjtC7QOP4VO3kCcY" id="mcetoc_1in3piideis"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.9]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying close to motorways (Speed limit is ≥ 80 km/hour)</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fsnelweg.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=40bf9d7f-304c-4413-8633-d423856621d8" alt="" width="83"> [OPERATOR] performs the drone operation for various purposes for flying in the vicinity of ≥ 80 km/h motorways (i.e. motorways and highways).</p>
<ul>
<li>To carry out inspections of bridges, viaducts and tunnels to develop 3D models and/or take high-quality inspection photos without hindering road/water traffic.</li>
<li>For video productions of, among other things, billboards etc.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Risks for this operation</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Collision with traffic due to loss of control of the UAS</li>
<li>Traffic distraction with the risk of an accident.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Pre-flight measures</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>[OPERATOR] coordinates the planned work with RWS (in the flight preparation phase). This will usually take place directly with the administrator of RWS, or through the contracting party. Alternative it is <a href="mailto:droneloket@rws.nl">droneloket@rws.nl</a>.</li>
<li>[OPERATOR] provides a flight plan for this.</li>
<li>RWS requires that an operator also coordinate such an operation with local authorities. If RWS sees no objections, they will issue a “declaration of no objection”.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Additional mitigating measures</strong><br>In addition, the following additional mitigating measures apply to limit the risk for road users and the crew:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_12" data-is-focusable="true">Minimum</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_13" data-is-focusable="true">horizontal</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_14" data-is-focusable="true">distance</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_15" data-is-focusable="true">to</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_16" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_17" data-is-focusable="true">road</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_18" data-is-focusable="true">is</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_19" data-is-focusable="true">10</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_20" data-is-focusable="true">meters</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_21" data-is-focusable="true">.</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_22" data-is-focusable="true">Experience</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_23" data-is-focusable="true">shows</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_24" data-is-focusable="true">that</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_25" data-is-focusable="true">traffic</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_26" data-is-focusable="true">users</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_27" data-is-focusable="true">hardly</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_28" data-is-focusable="true">see</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_29" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_30" data-is-focusable="true">drone</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_31" data-is-focusable="true">.</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_32" data-is-focusable="true">By</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_33" data-is-focusable="true">flying</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_34" data-is-focusable="true">in</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_35" data-is-focusable="true">strips</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_36" data-is-focusable="true">,</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_37" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_38" data-is-focusable="true">correct</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_39" data-is-focusable="true">3</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_40" data-is-focusable="true">D</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_41" data-is-focusable="true">and</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_42" data-is-focusable="true">inspection</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_43" data-is-focusable="true">images</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_44" data-is-focusable="true">can</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_45" data-is-focusable="true">still</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_46" data-is-focusable="true">be</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_47" data-is-focusable="true">collected</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_48" data-is-focusable="true">.</span></li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_49" data-is-focusable="true">Set</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_50" data-is-focusable="true">a</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_51" data-is-focusable="true">minimum</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_52" data-is-focusable="true">flight</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_53" data-is-focusable="true">altitude</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_54" data-is-focusable="true">of</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_55" data-is-focusable="true">at</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_56" data-is-focusable="true">least</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_57" data-is-focusable="true">20</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_58" data-is-focusable="true">meters</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_59" data-is-focusable="true">higher</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_60" data-is-focusable="true">than</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_61" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_62" data-is-focusable="true">road</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_63" data-is-focusable="true">.</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_64" data-is-focusable="true">Due</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_65" data-is-focusable="true">to</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_66" data-is-focusable="true">this</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_67" data-is-focusable="true">height</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_68" data-is-focusable="true">,</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_69" data-is-focusable="true">motorists</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_70" data-is-focusable="true">hardly</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_71" data-is-focusable="true">see</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_72" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_73" data-is-focusable="true">drone</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_74" data-is-focusable="true">and</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_75" data-is-focusable="true">it</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_76" data-is-focusable="true">ensures</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_77" data-is-focusable="true">minimal</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_78" data-is-focusable="true">distraction</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_79" data-is-focusable="true">.</span></li>
<li>When arranging the crew and the take-off and landing area, distraction from road users and the safety of the crew must be taken into account, preferably from a lower part, ashore or from the water. In any case, outside the obstacle-free zone of 13 meters next to the road.</li>
<li>To have a shortest possible time of exposure, and thus cross at right angles. Do not hover above the road.</li>
<li>The wind direction and strength influence the size of the fall area in the event of a critical disturbance. This is taken into account during flight preparation. Flights are therefore flown in strips parallel to the highway, so that in the event of an engine failure, the chance of a crash on the road is small.</li>
<li>Fly for the shortest period possible over the road, i.e., cross it at a right angle.</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_ICIUUuO9Al263jWSenNA" class="not_editable" data-id="ICIUUuO9Al263jWSenNA">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1gf5tglhd7n" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="ICIUUuO9Al263jWSenNA"><span class="shortcode">[C3.5.10]</span> <span class="name">Flight over Road or Waterway</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FPictogram%20Droneconsultancy%20overvliegen%20weg%20waterweg.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=d43400de-a4f8-46dd-9c81-cfce2270cd70" alt="" width="77"> The following additional measures must be taken for these operations:</p>
<ul>
<li>Several observers are deployed and correctly positioned to monitor the airspace and to keep an eye on traffic, so that they can inform the pilot in good time by shouting 'Traffic of Traffic'. This gives the pilot the opportunity to take timely action if traffic arrives. Crossing can be done by staying at a distance (hovering) from traffic (that is, uninvolved people). Use the minimum distance as described in the determination of the ground risk buffer, see <a href="#article_NiCKFeVZ0akFej1WJJki">[A6.4] Operational Volume determination</a>.</li>
<li>Only when the Observer gives the pilot the command 'Traffic clear', the pilot can fly over it. The pilot indicates when the UA is outside the ground risk buffer of the (water)way by shouting 'Clear or Free'.</li>
<li>The drone must cross the surface of (water) road in such a way that the time spent above is minimized (if possible)&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_A7GaJ58A9hGmEzTClHXo" class="not_editable" data-id="A7GaJ58A9hGmEzTClHXo">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="A7GaJ58A9hGmEzTClHXo" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11m"><span class="shortcode">[C3.6]</span> <span class="name">Cinematography - flying close to people and buildings on film sets over controlled ground</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FCinematografie.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=a5556cc1-c55f-4294-9756-82ceb8dce8fe" alt="" width="81"> This procedure involves operations on a professional film set with involved persons and flying close to buildings and objects where uninvolved persons may be present inside.</p>
<p>Drones can be used for a variety of photography, film and video applications such as corporate movies, commercials, branding and all kinds of photography. Drone images are of great value to the commercial industry.</p>
<p>Also, the use of drones for marketing and event campaigns will greatly change the way of communication and reach the public. Due to the small size of drones, high quality cameras and flexibility, fun videos and photos can be taken for marketing campaigns. Even during public events, drones are used for live broadcasts from positions that were impossible to capture in the traditional way.</p>
<p>The biggest risks of this operation are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Injure a person/animal on set (risk of collision)</li>
<li>Flying unusual maneuvers with sensor resulting in collision/crash.</li>
</ol>
<p>The most important specific mitigation measures for this operation are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Before the shooting starts, the film crew will receive:
<ul>
<li>A safety instruction</li>
<li>A communication protocol</li>
<li>Explanation about privacy legislation</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>UAS features obstacle detection to ensure distance between actors and UAS. Note: obstacle detection only works if there is sufficient ambient lighting. Check the technical specifications of the UAS.</li>
<li>During flight preparation, the mass of the UA is taken into account by design a flight path or trajectory in which as much as possible is flown away from people (i.e. not towards people).</li>
<li>It is flown at low speed and based on waypoints.</li>
<li>Set a geofence with max radius and max height to keep the drone within the controlled area.</li>
<li>UAS has 'motor stop' and can be switched off mid-air immediately.</li>
<li>Use of prop guards to prevent injury.</li>
<li>The minimum distance between UAS and actor is 5 meters.</li>
<li>Set up a cordon using plates, cones and red/white ribbon. If necessary, an extra observer can be deployed to stop uninvolved persons.</li>
<li>The pilot has specific knowledge of the technical limitations and of the flight behavior with specific sensors.</li>
<li>Inform payload operator in advance about flight scenarios so that communication during the flight is kept to a minimum.</li>
<li>The owner(s) of the film set provides pre-authorization before a flight is operated.</li>
<li>The pilot must have a good view of the set, if this is not possible, an additional observer must be deployed.</li>
<li>Cables must be secured to the floor so that no one can fall over them.</li>
<li>The pilot is in a cable-free place.</li>
<li>Flight crew or film crew has first-aid (EHBO) certificate.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_0mniRsUtYjorX7wUeIHQ" class="not_editable" data-id="0mniRsUtYjorX7wUeIHQ">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="0mniRsUtYjorX7wUeIHQ" id="mcetoc_1in3piideit"><span class="shortcode">[C3.8]</span> <span class="name">Procedure Flying near Vital Infrastructure</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FEM%20veld.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=ea8a5de5-5101-4692-975c-d60edb31384d" alt="" width="72"> In the Netherlands, according to the website of ILT <sup><span style="font-size: 8pt;">1</span></sup>, the following institutes and areas are considered Vital Infrastructure&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 8pt;"><sup>2</sup></span>:&nbsp;</p>
<ol>
<li>Intake points and production sites for the drinking water supply.</li>
<li>The high-voltage network for national and regional transmission and distribution of electricity.</li>
<li>Large Sea Ports.</li>
<li>High Risk Companies (BRZO)</li>
<li>Security Areas</li>
<li>Airports within a CTR (Controlled Traffic Region): an additional procedure in the manual is required (C3.3)</li>
</ol>
<p>These locations are visible on <a aria-label="GoDrone kaart (opens external website)" href="https://map.godrone.nl/"><span dir="ltr">GoDrone</span> map</a>.</p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;"><sup>1</sup>Source: ILT website <a href="https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/drones/categorie-specifiek/vliegen-bij-vitale-infrastructuur">https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/drones/categorie-specifiek/vliegen-bij-vitale-infrastructuur. </a></span><span style="font-size: 8pt;"><sup>2</sup>Risk profile of UA's flight are considered relevant for these institutes.</span></p>
<p></p>
<p><strong>Risks</strong></p>
<p>Risks for flying near/in these areas are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Crash on the vital object resulting in pollution (battery) and/or (long-term) disruption of the vital process.</li>
<li>Loss of control of the UA due to signal loss due to EM radiation /distortion.</li>
</ol>
<h4>General Mitigations</h4>
<p>Flying near vital infrastructure will always require the performance of a risk assessment that needs to be created in accordance with the owner/responsible of the infrastructure.</p>
<p>[OPERATOR] flies in the Specific category via an Operational Authorisation (OA), draws up an Operational Plan (OP) that includes the risk assessment for these flights and follows the normal procedures from this Operational Manual.</p>
<p>When the operation takes place in proximity to vital infrastructure, the additional measures are taken. The proximity means that the object of the vital infrastructure or area is within the operational volume and ground risk buffer.</p>
<ol>
<li>Contact the organisation responsible for the vital infrastructure;</li>
<li>[OPERATOR] must have permission from&nbsp;the organisation responsible for the infrastructure.</li>
<li>Collectively identify risks together with the organisation;</li>
<li>Processed the mitigations of risks per flight in the operational plan;</li>
<li>[OPERATOR] prepares the specific procedure in an operational plan during the flight preparation phase. It should clearly state the mitigating measures as agreed with the organisation.</li>
</ol>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">Source: </span>Vliegen bij vitale infrastructuur van de <a href="https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/drones/categorie-specifiek/vliegen-bij-vitale-infrastructuur">ILT</a>&nbsp;</span><span lang="EN-GB"></span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_PN4b00kxivuYKIAhHKfG" class="not_editable" data-id="PN4b00kxivuYKIAhHKfG">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="PN4b00kxivuYKIAhHKfG"><span class="shortcode">[C3.9]</span> <span class="name">Flight Outside UDP (Night Flight)</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fbuiten%20udp.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=e34e59b2-98cb-4e9e-a644-dedae9fee8b1" alt="" width="90" height="40"> For all flights outside UDP, the additional procedures have been compiled. This is because there are additional risks, for which mitigating measures must be taken to reduce the risks to an acceptable level. In addition, all flights must be conducted in accordance with standard operating methods as described Chapter A6: Normal Operation Strategy.</p>
<p>The additional risks and the associated mitigating measures are described in the table below and then further elaborated in this chapter.</p>

<p><em></em></p>
<p><strong>Training</strong><em></em></p>
<p>Flights outside UDP are only performed by trained pilots. These pilots are listed in the organisational overview in Appendix A. They have completed the training and test "<span style="font-size: 12pt;">Endorsement Module Night Operations</span>”. <a href="#article_UVSP7ZfC6dMWXa4JfPFo">See [D2.6] Training Night-VLOS.</a></p>
<p><strong></strong></p>
<p><strong>Night flight procedure</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<ul style="list-style-type: circle;">
<li>Night flights are only operated under conditions normally considered to be VMC (Visual Meteorological Conditions). Preparation for each flight always includes a detailed assessment of the weather forecasts to ensure that the VMC conditions are addressed.</li>
<li>Flight altitude is a maximum of 120 meters above the ground or water, unless a different maximum altitude applies at the location of the flight.</li>
<li>In addition, there will also be an on-site surveillance by the PIC to ensure that the flight is conducted within VMC.</li>
<li>All flights are flown in (E)VLOS.</li>
<li>The crew members are trained and briefed, see Appendix E, Briefing for night flights.</li>
<li>Breaks are extended by 15 minutes.</li>
<li>Flights are prepared and operated as in the Operational Plan for flights outside UDP, see format in Appendix E.</li>
<li>Each flight preparation for a night flight includes an on-site survey within UDP and under VMC. This site survey is used to identify obstacles and hazards that might not be apparent to a pilot flying at night, e.g., high voltage cables, antennas on buildings and so on.</li>
<li>The Operational Plan and the exemption are present and can be shown by [OPERATOR] during the drone flight.</li>
<li>The pilot has been trained according to the [D2.6] Training syllabus Night-VLOS (outside UDP flight) and is prepared to operate the UAS outside UDP.</li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_0" data-is-focusable="true">Set</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_1" data-is-focusable="true">a</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_2" data-is-focusable="true">minimum</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_3" data-is-focusable="true">safe</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_4" data-is-focusable="true">flight</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_5" data-is-focusable="true">altitude</span> for RTH <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_6" data-is-focusable="true">(</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_7" data-is-focusable="true">to</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_8" data-is-focusable="true">avoid</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_9" data-is-focusable="true">obstacles using the procedure, loss of view or orientation</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_10" data-is-focusable="true">).</span></li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_0" data-is-focusable="true">Coordinate</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_1" data-is-focusable="true">with</span> the local government (usually the Municipality) if the location or time of the flight may cause inconvenience to local residents.</li>
<li>The rules and restrictions of the operating statement or operating licence continue to apply.</li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'Calibri Light', sans-serif;"></span>At least 24 hours in advance: Submit a Notice to Airman (NOTAM). Send an email to the LVNL Operational Helpdesk at ops_helpdesk@lvnl.nl, including the following details:<o:p></o:p>
<ul>
<li>
<p class="MsoNormal">Name of the location;&nbsp;Coordinates of the flight area in degrees, minutes, and seconds;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p>Radius of the flight area;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p>Flight altitude;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p>Date and time(s), specifying whether local time or UTC;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p>Contact details.<o:p></o:p></p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Mandatory notification by email to the following organisations:</li>
</ul>
<table height="139" style="width: 94.7037%; height: 120.136px; border-collapse: collapse; border-style: solid;" border="1">
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 52.0682px;">
<td width="302" style="width: 48.0984%;">
<p>Inspectie Leefomgeving en Transport (ILT)</p>
</td>
<td width="302" style="width: 48.0984%;">
<p><a href="mailto:drones.toezicht@ilent.nl">drones.toezicht@ilent.nl</a></p>
</td>
</tr>

<td width="302" style="width: 48.0984%;">
<p>Luchtvaartpolitie</p>
</td>
<td width="302" style="width: 48.0984%;">
<p><a href="mailto:luchtvaarttoezicht@politie.nl">luchtvaarttoezicht@politie.nl</a></p>
</td>
