<p>With the following content:</p>
<ul>
<li>In Subject: "Notification UAS flight outside UDP"</li>
<li>In Body:
<ul>
<li>Name Operator</li>
<li>Document number from the flight authority regards to the exemption from UDP</li>
<li>Location of flights</li>
<li>Date and time of flights</li>
<li>Maximum flight heights</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Procedure loss of view of the UAS or loss of orientation (including failure of UAS lighting).</span></strong></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">When the sight of the UA is lost during the night flight, the pilot shall immediately start return-to-home (RTH) procedure. This procedure is also valid when the loss of orientation occurs and/or the UAS lighting fails. For the procedure 'Return to home', please refer&nbsp;<a href="#article_TzRYcwXshMEKczmolbeL">[C4.1.1] Return to Home (RTH)</a>.</span></p>
<p><strong>Night lighting of the</strong> <strong>UA</strong></p>
<p>The UA shall be provided with adequate lighting to ensure both clear airborne recognition by the PIC as well as to allow proper assessment of orientation and direction of the UA by the PIC in a visual manner. SERA.3215 requires the lights an aircraft must carry. In addition, EASA requires the use of a green flashing anti-collision light.</p>
<table border="1" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; border-width: 1px; border-style: none;"><colgroup><col style="width: 99.8836%;"></colgroup>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/dronestart-production.appspot.com/o/images%2Fgeneral%2Fdrone%20met%20lichten.png?alt=media&amp;token=cfc83983-5bc7-489f-accf-78340f19d84a" alt="" width="250" height="207" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p></p>
<p>&nbsp;The UA has the following lighting for flying outside UDP:</p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type: none;">
<ol>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_0" data-is-focusable="true">The</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_1" data-is-focusable="true">drone</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_2" data-is-focusable="true">has</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_3" data-is-focusable="true">red</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_4" data-is-focusable="true">light</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_5" data-is-focusable="true">on</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_6" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_7" data-is-focusable="true">left</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_8" data-is-focusable="true">.</span>&nbsp;</li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_9" data-is-focusable="true">The</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_10" data-is-focusable="true">drone</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element-highlighted" id="tgtAlignment_11" data-is-focusable="true">has</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element-highlighted" id="tgtAlignment_12" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_13" data-is-focusable="true">green</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_14" data-is-focusable="true">light</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_15" data-is-focusable="true">on</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_16" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_17" data-is-focusable="true">right</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_18" data-is-focusable="true">.</span>&nbsp;</li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_19" data-is-focusable="true">The</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_20" data-is-focusable="true">drone</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_21" data-is-focusable="true">has</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_22" data-is-focusable="true">white</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_23" data-is-focusable="true">stern</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_24" data-is-focusable="true">light</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_25" data-is-focusable="true">at</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_26" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_27" data-is-focusable="true">back</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_28" data-is-focusable="true">.</span>&nbsp;</li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_29" data-is-focusable="true">The</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_30" data-is-focusable="true">drone</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_31" data-is-focusable="true">has</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_32" data-is-focusable="true">green</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_33" data-is-focusable="true">flashing</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_34" data-is-focusable="true">light</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_35" data-is-focusable="true">to</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_36" data-is-focusable="true">indicate</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_37" data-is-focusable="true">the</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_38" data-is-focusable="true">difference</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_39" data-is-focusable="true">between</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_40" data-is-focusable="true">a</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_41" data-is-focusable="true">manned</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_42" data-is-focusable="true">and</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_43" data-is-focusable="true">unmanned</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_44" data-is-focusable="true">aerial</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_45" data-is-focusable="true">vehiclel.</span></li>
</ol>
</li>
</ol>
<p><span class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true">Lateral movement should be avoided as much as possible. If it is necessary, the movement must be carried out in such a way that the red light is visible on the left side of the direction of travel and the green light on the right.</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_75" data-is-focusable="true"></span></p>
<p><strong>Battery Monitoring Procedure</strong></p>
<p>The pilot is responsible for monitoring the battery level through the HMI or relevant applications and must account for the increased power consumption caused by night lighting. Battery status is typically displayed using an icon or other visual indicator on the HMI. See the example below.</p>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FScreenshot%202023-01-23%20at%2016.11.16.png?alt=media&amp;token=7e0a4444-dcc3-44bc-a2fa-542c5b536e51" alt="" width="557" height="64" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;">Figure: The battery indicator is shown on the monitor.</p>
<p>The battery icon is typically located in the top-right corner of the display, although this may vary depending on the type or brand of the UAS. For more detailed information, refer to Part B or the manufacturer's user manual.</p>
<div class="ms-Grid-row">
<div class="ts-textfield-container ts-larger-font" lang="en">
<div class="ts-alignment-view-container">
<div id="ts-alignment-view-idtgt" class="ts-alignment-view  ms-font-m ts-alignment-view-tgt ts-ltr-left-zero" aria-hidden="false" aria-label="Vertaling in het Engels." tabindex="0">
<div role="label" tabindex="-1"><strong><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_0" data-is-focusable="true">Adequate</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_1" data-is-focusable="true">ground</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_2" data-is-focusable="true">lighting</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_3" data-is-focusable="true">or</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_4" data-is-focusable="true">red</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_5" data-is-focusable="true">light</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_6" data-is-focusable="true">flashlights</span></strong></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The PIC must ensure that all take-off and landing areas (primary and alternative) are sufficiently lit for the pilot to take off and land safely. For this, red LED beacon lights or red light flashlights can be used to mark the take-off and landing zone. An alternate landing zone is also marked.&nbsp;</p>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FUDP%20Ground%20Lights.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=8f006863-884c-4cec-ad7b-af1ae2a2a9eb" alt="" width="247" height="124" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"><strong></strong></p>
<p><strong>Safety in the air</strong></p>
<p>[OPERATOR] shall take the following measures to reduce the air risk:</p>
<ul>
<li>The PIC ensures that the brightness of the UAS controller's screen is reduced to help maintain night vision.</li>
<li>The UAS used in night flight must be equipped with the following features, including red, green, and white lights (See the table in [C3.9] for additional risks and the associated mitigating measures).&nbsp;They are checked as part of each relevant pre-flight procedure and included in the maintenance program. The pre-flight check and maintenance programme is adapted accordingly.</li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_0" data-is-focusable="true">Note</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_1" data-is-focusable="true">:</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_2" data-is-focusable="true">Obstacle</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_3" data-is-focusable="true">Avoidance</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_4" data-is-focusable="true">does</span> not <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_5" data-is-focusable="true">work</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_6" data-is-focusable="true">or</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_7" data-is-focusable="true">does</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_8" data-is-focusable="true">not</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_9" data-is-focusable="true">work</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_10" data-is-focusable="true">sufficiently</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_11" data-is-focusable="true">at</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_12" data-is-focusable="true">night</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_13" data-is-focusable="true">at</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_14" data-is-focusable="true">most</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_15" data-is-focusable="true">UAs</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_16" data-is-focusable="true">.</span></li>
<li><span class="ts-alignment-element" data-is-focusable="true"><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_0" data-is-focusable="true">Consider</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_1" data-is-focusable="true">short</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_2" data-is-focusable="true">battery</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_3" data-is-focusable="true">life</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_4" data-is-focusable="true">due</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_5" data-is-focusable="true">to</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_6" data-is-focusable="true">power</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_7" data-is-focusable="true">consumption</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_8" data-is-focusable="true">of</span> <span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_9" data-is-focusable="true">lighting</span><span class="ts-alignment-element" id="tgtAlignment_10" data-is-focusable="true">.</span></span></li>
<li>The GPS unit must be serviceable, so that accurate data for GPS hold and RTH functionality can always be available</li>
<li>Telemetry data that shows when a good GPS lock has been established. A minimum of 7 satellites is active, otherwise the flight will not be carried out.</li>
<li>The PIC must have telemetry data at the place where it operates the UAS (base station) that shows the position of the UAS in 3D space. This means: distance from and course in relation to the PIC and the height AGL.</li>
<li>The night flight is not performed when rain or thunderstorms are observed or predicted within 5 (five) kilometres of the Operational Volume limit (see Image Operational Volume).</li>
<li>At least one observer is present.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Safety on the ground</strong></p>
<p><em>[OPERATOR] takes the following measures to reduce the ground risk:</em></p>
<ul>
<li>Leave the UA and all ground equipment in the setup area so that it is not a hazard or damaged.</li>
<li>If the area around the take-off/landing zone is easily accessible and passers-by can be expected, the area is cordoned off with a clearly visible barrier.</li>
<li>Furthermore, a minimum crew of RPIC and an observer is provided. This ensures that the public stays at a distance from the take-off/landing zone.</li>
<li>When the recce/site survey within UDP raises this, an extra observer can be deployed.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Personnel / Physiological aspects</strong></p>
<p>Flights outside of UDP require more of the crew's physical and cognitive abilities. The pilot must be aware of the time it takes for the eyes to adjust to the dark. Therefore, the following points of attention are addressed during the training (Annex II to ED Decision 2022/002/R (Operation Specific Endorsement Module):</p>
<ul>
<li>General points of attention for night flying, such as the definition of night, use of infrared and night lighting on the UA.</li>
<li>Degradation of visual acuity caused by increasing pupil size</li>
<li>Night illusion and the blind spot (see image below).
<ul>
<li>Because other eye cells are used in darkness (the rods), this means that the part of the eye with which you see most sharply in daylight contributes less to vision at night. This creates a blind spot ('Night blind spot').&nbsp;</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Other visual scanning techniques</li>
<li>Other identification of obstacles</li>
</ul>
<p>Only a remote pilot authorized for night flights performs a night flight. (He has successfully completed the training and test "Night VLOS". See [D2.6] Training Night VLOS.</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FNachtelijke%20blindspot.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=36a2f00b-db07-4fb9-a4a1-b1b852c0ea47" alt="" width="203" height="259" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"><em>Image: blindspot at night</em></p>
<p style="text-align: left;"><span style="font-size: 8pt;">Source: <a href="https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/drones/categorie-specifiek/ontheffingen/vliegen-buiten-de-uniforme-daglicht-periode-udp">https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/drones/categorie-specifiek/ontheffingen/vliegen-buiten-de-uniforme-daglicht-periode-udp</a></span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;">Source: Annex II to ED Decision 2022/002/R (Operation Specific Endorsement Module)</span><span style="font-size: 8pt;"></span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_JmFvcg9TfE6bbNVgn1WX" class="not_editable" data-id="JmFvcg9TfE6bbNVgn1WX">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="JmFvcg9TfE6bbNVgn1WX" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7124f"><span class="shortcode">[C3.11]</span> <span class="name">Procedure Flying near buildings/object within populated and controlled ground area</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fnabij%20boven%20bebouwing%20en%20steden.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=018e9455-24f1-4494-943d-60ea332f395d" alt="" width="88"> For flying near/in/above populated area, [OPERATOR] uses the procedure that was known under Dutch regulations under the name STS2a.</p>
<p><strong>Starting points for flights above buildings in urban areas</strong></p>
<p>Flights may take place above buildings (compared to the normal procedures and standard working methods) when applying additional mitigations:</p>
<ol>
<li>Low flight speed (= &lt; 5m/s), such that the UA cannot crash outside the operational volume in the event of an engine failure;</li>
<li>Controlled Ground Area in the Operational Volume as valid for [OPERATOR];</li>
<li>Maximum distance around the object to be measured/photographed of 30 meters (= Atypical Airspace). Flying further away is only allowed in controlled airspace (= regarded safe due to contact with ATC (LVNL));</li>
<li>with a maximum flight height above the ground/water set in the flight plan.</li>
<li>without invading the privacy of people on the ground or in buildings.</li>
<li>with an adequate ERP, should something go wrong. For this purpose, the standard emergency procedures of [OPERATOR] are used, see [NOP] emergency procedures.</li>
<li>[OPERATOR] ensures with deposition and/or additional observers that no uninvolved people can enter the Operational Volume.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Controlled Ground Area within Operational Volume</strong></p>
<p>Within the controlled ground area (= Operational Volume, see chapter A6.4) there are <u>only persons actively involved in the operation</u> who:</p>
<ol>
<li>are familiar with the risks of UAS operations;</li>
<li>have accepted these risks (in writing);</li>
<li>have been informed of the relevant emergency procedures;</li>
</ol>
<p>Controlled areas also include roof terraces and balconies.</p>
<p>The controlled territory shall be separated from uncontrolled territory with:</p>
<ol>
<li>Drop-off ribbons (red/white) and/or additional observers with tools to detect and warn non-involved persons not to enter the area in a timely manner.</li>
<li>Signs – with, for example, 'ATTENTION, DRONE OPERATION ACTIVE or other means of communication.</li>
</ol>
<p>When selecting and setting up this area, the following shall be noted in the flight plan:</p>
<ol>
<li>Minimum and maximum height above the object;</li>
<li>The set height of the RTH function;</li>
<li>The flight area containing the 30 meter zone of the controlled area;</li>
<li>Maximum height above ground/water;</li>
<li>The horizontal speed (low speed = &lt; 5 m/s);</li>
<li>Wind speed and wind direction;</li>
<li>Turbulence around the object and the 'venturi effect'</li>
<li>The proximity and number of expected 'uninvolved' persons;</li>
<li>Number of required observers and any traffic controllers.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Uninvolved person enters the Operational Volume</strong></p>
<p>If, despite the measures taken as described above, uninvolved persons enter the Operational Volume, the observer shall:</p>
<ul>
<li>Address these people and ask to leave the area immediately, but</li>
<li>If that is not adequate, the observer will instruct the pilot to land the UA as soon as possible.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Ground Risk Buffer</strong></p>
<p>If the UA has to operate at a height of 100 meters, the ground risk buffer must be at least 100 meters. The buffer shall apply in relation to the area with a higher risk than where the operation takes place; For operations over controlled area (this procedure), this buffer applies compared to uncontrolled ground area. For the determination of the Ground Risk Buffer, the ballistic method from section A6.4.3 can also be used.</p>
<p><strong>Reliable connection with C3 link</strong></p>
<p>A malfunction must not lead to an incident. [OPERATOR] selects and tests the quality of the connection between the transmitter and the UA, taking into account:</p>
<ol>
<li>Correct radio frequency (RF) for local conditions</li>
<li>Data security, spoofing and hacking</li>
</ol>
<p>The airworthy and maintained UAS that is flown above populated areas must meet a number of minimum technical requirements, including lost link management, return to home procedures, geofencing, possibility for manual flying in case of GNSS problems, et cetera. The starting point is that a malfunction may not immediately lead to an incident.</p>
<p>In the event of a failure of the transmitter, the UA automatically chooses the set home position and flight altitude.</p>
<p><strong>Use of external data sources, such as weather, air traffic, etc.</strong></p>
<p>[OPERATOR] must verify during flight preparation and prior flight whether the information presented on drone apps and flight management systems corresponds to official information such as KNMI and LVNL (notams, no fly zones).</p>
<p><strong>Emergency Response Plan (ERP)&nbsp;</strong></p>
<p>In addition to the standard emergency procedures in this manual, see chapter C5: Emergency procedures, an emergency plan (ERP) is necessary for this type of operation. This plan is intended to limit crash-escalating effects by, for example, alerting emergency services. [OPERATOR] shall go through this contingency plan with all relevant third parties identified in the plan.</p>
<ol>
<li>The ERP is validated by means of a representative exercise on the tabletop (e.g. chronological discussion of steps during a possible incident or accident);</li>
<li>The ERP must be consistent with the ERP training system, see section D2 Training;</li>
<li>An ERP training program is available. A record of the ERP training followed by the relevant staff is established and updated. In addition, the competences of the relevant personnel are verified by a competent third party (ILT) through the approval of this manual.</li>
</ol>
<p>In the event of a crash or another emergency services are called in see ERP in chapter C6 and the example flight plan in appendix C1.</p>
<p><strong>VLOS Deconfliction Scheme – phraseology</strong></p>
<p>During the operation, the phraseology from this manual is used as described in chapter A5 Crew Communication.</p>
<p><strong>UAS Maintenance</strong><strong> </strong></p>
<p>The maintenance procedures from this manual are used and the maintenance carried out is recorded, see chapter A8 General Maintenance.</p>
<p><strong>Operational procedures, contingency and emergency procedures</strong></p>
<p>Specifically for this scenario, the contingency and emergency procedures are important where the greatest risks to flying within urban areas are mitigated. Include the following considerations in the Emergency Response Plan and in the Flight Plan:</p>
<ol>
<li>In particular, the wind turbulence is a point of attention with the risk of loss of control and a crash, see chapter [D1.6] Turbulence/Venturi effect. In flight preparation, conduct research into the wind speeds and venturi effects in the flight area.</li>
<li>In addition, there is the risk of injury due to ungovernability. Therefore, the area above which flown is secured with temporary deposits and /or traffic controllers.</li>
<li>Information boards will be placed.</li>
<li>In addition to the pilot, an observer must be present. This observer has the task of communicating well with those involved in the environment and keeping people away.</li>
<li>The UAS is flown at a low speed to minimize the effects of a crash.</li>
<li>The ERP/flight plan contains the current numbers of the emergency workers in the vicinity of the flight operation. The ERP is present at the flight location.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Training</strong></p>
<p>For this specific scenario, a so-called 'self-declaration' is required for a training course containing the following additional components:</p>
<ol>
<li>Application and training of operational procedures</li>
<li>Communication</li>
<li>UAS Flight Planning</li>
<li>Leadership, teamwork and self-management</li>
<li>Problem solving and decision-making</li>
<li>Situational Awareness</li>
<li>Managing work</li>
<li>Coordination and transfer of tasks.</li>
</ol>
<p>These aspects have been added to [OPERATOR]'s basic training program in D2 Training. Self-declaration means that the operator can prove that the pilot has been trained on the above aspects.</p>
<p><strong>Privacy aspects</strong></p>
<p>If recordings are made of homes or business premises (for example for inspections), the residents will have to be informed in advance about the operation and, according to the GDPR, the operator must make clear, among other things, for what purpose recordings are made, how the data is processed and who has access to the data. See also chapter D1.2 Privacy and laws and regulations.</p>
</article>
<p><em></em></p>
<article id="article_LY6CLJFYbhgyBkW25jd5" class="not_editable" data-id="LY6CLJFYbhgyBkW25jd5">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="LY6CLJFYbhgyBkW25jd5" id="mcetoc_1in3piidej0"><span class="shortcode">[C3.12]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying near/above railway</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fboven%20spoorlijnen.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=7ca12dfa-02dc-4fa0-a994-dcacacb0a7b1" alt="" width="86"> UAS operations over railways and the associated infrastructure in both rural and populated areas in the Netherlands are desirable. Numerous innovative UAS applications will be made possible by allowing these operations, which serve not only the commercial interest of the operators, but also the public interest. An example of this are maintenance inspections of railway lines, railway bridges and trains.</p>
<p>Under EU regulations, people on trains are seen as 'not involved', but there are no formal requirements for flying near railways. However, the following procedure has been agreed with Prorail. These additional instructions are followed by [OPERATOR].</p>
<p>Conditions:</p>
<ul>
<li>VLOS of EVLOS</li>
<li>VFR: operations take place in visual meteorological conditions (VMC)</li>
<li>During daytime (Uniform Daylight Period).</li>
<li>Low flight speed to prevent the drone from getting outside the flight area if one or more engines fail.</li>
<li>Atypical airspace: defined as airspace where manned aircraft normally cannot go. Therefore, operators keep the UAS within 30 meters of buildings or structures (objects) to sufficiently reduce the risk of a collision with manned aircraft.</li>
<li>SERA: not in airspace C and D without additional permission.</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Ground Area</strong></p>
<p>Operations take place over railways in a densely populated area or sparsely populated area. There are currently two definitions of a populated area available:</p>
<ol>
<li>A city, suburb, suburb, residential area, urban, subway, city, and/or gathering of people in the open air.&nbsp;Defined as a buffer of 1⁄2 nm (3038 ft.) around all urbanized areas. Urbanized areas are defined as an area with an average population of 500 people per square mile (1295 people per square kilometer).</li>
<li>A sparsely populated area is defined as: All areas that are not defined as populated areas and not within an airport environment.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Controlled Ground Area and active participants</strong></p>
<p>In the Operational Volume, only active participants are present. Active participants are those individuals who are directly involved in the UAS operation or are fully aware that the UAS operation takes place near them performed and have accepted these risks. Active participants are informed about and can follow relevant effective emergency procedures and/or emergency plans.</p>
<p>Inactive participants are those individuals who are in the vicinity of a UAS operation and may or may not be aware that a UAS operation is taking place. Inactive participants are not aware of the risks associated with the surgery and have not accepted these risks.</p>
<p><em>Scenario's</em></p>
<p>UAS activities over railways and the associated infrastructure can be divided into two operational scenarios, with the second scenario having two sub-scenarios:</p>
<ol>
<li>UAS operations with railway lines in use;</li>
<li>UAS activities with unused tracks:</li>
</ol>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">2.a UAS activities during a planned closure</p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">2b. UAS operations during a calamity</p>
<p><em>&nbsp;</em><em>General working environment</em></p>
<p>The working environment when performing UAS operations over railways rural areas and populated areas is defined in the Voorschrift Veilig Werken (VVW). This document (available from ProRail and (sub)contractors) describes the applicable dimensions when working on or near railway infrastructure.</p>
<p>Workplace safety when working on or near railway infrastructure is determined by two risks:</p>
<ol>
<li>The risk of a collision with people and/or equipment due to track-related equipment (e.g. trains, work trains, maintenance equipment, etc.);</li>
<li>The risk of electrocution by contact of persons and/or equipment with electrically charged parts of the power supply or train protection installation.</li>
</ol>
<p>The VVW defines three zones (A - C) where these risks occur and determines rules and guidelines on how employees can safely set up their workplace.</p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FGevarenzones%20rondom%20spoor.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=b2ae6b7a-8c66-48ea-b875-c2573e56f1a1" alt="" width="353"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Image: danger zone around the track</em></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20Rode%20meetgebied%20rondom%20spoor.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=635e5be1-0ad8-4f41-9902-a1f938040e83" alt="" width="283"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Image red measuring area</em></p>
<p>The danger zone (A) is the zone where there is a risk of collision. The dimensions of this zone depend on the speed of the train or other track-related equipment. Outside the danger zone, there are two zones (B and C) which, due to the proximity of danger zone A, are exposed to side effects of passing runway equipment. Requirements are imposed on these zones to control the risk of entering danger zone A. The requirements for zone B are stricter than for zone C. Furthermore, a safety zone (refuge) has been defined where workers can position themselves to avoid being exposed to the risk of a collision when trackside equipment passes by.</p>
<p><em>Dimensions</em></p>
<p>The limit of danger zone A depends on the maximum permitted speed on the track. The table below defines the dimensions that apply to the different travel speeds.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20Tabel%20met%20afmetingen%20nabij%20spoor.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=3823119c-d4b6-4812-8db0-3ae9e7de35ee" alt="" width="571"><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20HSL%20spoor%20tekst.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=706edab6-d22a-485a-86c4-0c768593bc18" alt=""></p>
<p>Danger zone B has a standard size of 1 meter and starts at the boundary of danger zone A. Proximity zone C has a standard size of 1.75 meters and starts at the boundary of proximity zone B. For all activities within the three zones, a separate risk inventory and evaluation (RI&amp;E) must determine how the risks arising from the nearby danger zone A are managed.</p>
<p>The safety zone has a minimum size of 0.8 meters. This zone is an area where workers, with or without their materials and equipment, can position themselves to eliminate the risk of a collision. The safety zone must be accessible without passing obstacles (e.g. a fence or stairs). Furthermore, it is forbidden to pass an active track to reach the safety zone. The safety zone should always be placed outside the danger zone A and the dimensions depend on the number of people and equipment/materials in use.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20omvang%20treinen%20en%20maten%20veilige%20plek.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=75fbd0c2-5cdb-4708-b457-51d9028d31dd" alt="" width="321"></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Image danger zone (Zone A)</em></p>
<p><em>&nbsp;</em></p>
<p><em>High Voltage Risk</em></p>
<p>International standards describe the conditions under which it is permitted to operate on or near high-voltage components of the railway infrastructure. Working in danger zone A is only permitted if there is no voltage on the installation. When carrying out activities in proximity zones B and C, strict requirements apply to the minimum distances to be maintained. The table below shows for different voltages what the minimum distances are for people, vehicles and electrically charged objects.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20Tabel%20deel%201%20nabijheidzone%20electrocutie.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=c3287c6e-55d5-461d-8426-7ee3adf93d64" alt="" width="503"></p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20Tabel%20deel%202%20nabijheidzone%20electrocutie.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=d3d3b78b-878d-4a33-b3ca-74ea794ad90d" alt="" width="496"></p>
<p><strong><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FSporen%20Opmerkingen%20bij%20tabellen%20spoor.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=dac13ebf-0ab7-4443-b5ae-08d94d31f2ca" alt=""></strong></p>
<p><em>Scenario 1: UAS operations with used railway lines</em></p>
<p>During UAS operations with railway lines in use, the crew should be aware of the fact that trains may be present in the operational volume. These trains can have different speeds and can pass in both directions (depending on the number and configuration of the track surface(s)). During these operations, there will normally be a high voltage on the power lines of the railway infrastructure. The high voltage in combination with passing trains can cause fluctuations in the electromagnetic field. These fluctuations can affect the control and navigation of the UAS.</p>
<p>Therefore, operations within the red measurement zone (red measuring area, see figure 14) are not permitted when the track is in use. Operations above the track are permitted during automated flights (e.g. map flying), but the flight crew must be able to take over manual control at all times.</p>
<p>Over-track operations are not permitted during manual flights when a train passes (e.g. close-up inspections), therefore the UAS should be placed above proximity zone C (or beyond) and at a minimum distance or height of 25 meters from the railway infrastructure when a train passes by.</p>
<p>Operations in this scenario shall be performed at a minimum altitude of 5 meters (manual flights) or 25 meters (automated flights) above the highest point of the railway infrastructure, except where the UAS is protected from electromagnetic interference (EMI).</p>
<p>During these operations, the crew can reduce the risk of collision by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Controlled access of trains (Beheerste Toelating, BT)</li>
<li>A physical barrier (Fysieke Afscherming, FA)</li>
<li>A physical barrier (Gegarandeerde Waarschuwing, GW)</li>
<li>A physical barrier (Persoonlijke Waarnemer PW, door Grenswachter (GRW) of Veiligheidsman (VHM))</li>
<li>A personal safety instruction (Taak Eigen Veiligheid)</li>
</ul>
<p>A detailed description of these measures is available in chapter 4.3.1 of the VVW. The function of ‘Grenswachter’ and ‘Veiligheidsman’ shall not be combined with the function of observer in the crew.</p>
<p>Before starting the operation, the person responsible for engineering workplace safety should be informed (V&amp;G coordinator or workplace security guard). He is responsible for including the UAS operation in the instruction provided by the ‘leider werkplekbeveiliging’ (LWB) to the people who work in and around the workplace.</p>
<p>Operations in this scenario must be performed in accordance with the requirements, regulations, and guidelines in the Normenkader Veilig Werken (NVW), het Voorschrift Veilig Werken - Trein (VVW), de Life Saving Rules (LSR), Directive: rules of conduct on railway property (RLN00300). The NVW sets the framework for the organisation of a safe working environment in the railway infrastructure. The VVW translates this framework into concrete rules for the specific (sub) environments and installations.</p>
<p>&nbsp;<em>Scenario 2: UAS activities with unused railway lines</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><em>Sub-scenario a: UAS operations during a scheduled shutdown</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">When performing UAS operations during a planned shutdown, there are no trains present in the operational volume. Please refer to the VVW (notification 2) for the two applicable safety scales that prevent trains from entering the track. However, there may be a high voltage on the power lines of the railway infrastructure. Therefore, it is only allowed to operate a UAS within the red measurement zone (red measuring area) with the permission of the local ‘veiligheidsleider’ (Leider Lokale Veiligheid) and when the UAS &nbsp;is protected from electromagnetic interference (EMI).</p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">Before starting the operation, the person responsible for engineering workplace safety should be informed (V &amp; G-coördinator of werkplekbeveiliger). He is responsible for including the UAS operation in the instruction that the ‘leider werkplekbeveiliging’ (LWB) to the people who work in and around the workplace. Operations in this scenario must be performed in accordance with the requirements, regulations, and guidelines in the Normenkader Veilig Werken (NVW), het Voorschrift Veilig Werken - Trein (VVW), de Life Saving Rules (LSR), Richtlijn: gedragsregels op spoorwegterrein ( RLN00300).</p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><em>Sub-scenario b: UAS operations during a calamity</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">When performing UAS operations during an emergency, there is no (normal) train traffic present in the Operational Volume. The treindienstleider (TRDL) takes the necessary measures to ensure the safety of emergency personnel and to prevent danger to passengers and road users (see VVW notification 4). However, there may be a high voltage on the power lines of the railway infrastructure. Therefore, it is only permitted to operate a UAS within the red measurement zone (red measuring area) with the permission of the officier van dienst (officier van Dienst, OvD) and when the UAS &nbsp;is protected from electromagnetic interference (EMI)</p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">UAS operations during an emergency may only be carried out by ProRail (or parties contracted by ProRail) and emergency services (e.g. police, fire brigade, Rijkswaterstaat, etc.) in accordance with the applicable safety documentation (available from ProRail or prorail partners/contractors or from organisations carrying out activities in the vicinity of the railway site). Before the start of the operation (outside or inside the red measuring zone), permission must be obtained from the ‘officier van dienst’ (OvD). The OvD will inform the TRDL, which will inform the operators of other runway equipment that the UAS operation is taking place.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;">Operations in this scenario must be performed in accordance with the requirements, regulations, and guidelines in the Normenkader Veilig Werken (NVW), het Voorschrift Veilig Werken - Trein (VVW), de Life Saving Rules (LSR), Richtlijn: gedragsregels op spoorwegterrein ( RLN00300). Permission is required from ProRail when processing data obtained from a UAS operation during an emergency.</p>
<p><em>Additional terms and conditions</em></p>
<p>The UAS must be protected against EM fields for operations within the red measurement zone. If not inspected, the [OPERATOR] automatically flies no closer than 25 meters near railway lines. Manually no closer than 5 meters.</p>
<p>During flight preparation, information shall be collected on:</p>
<ol>
<li>Danger zone (A) and approach zones (B and C) at the intended flight location. Fill in the distances to be used in the operational plan;</li>
<li>Location of TAKE-OFF and landing area (zone C or further) on the location sketch in the plan.</li>
<li>Mapping (railway) infrastructure including high-voltage power lines</li>
<li>Trains and other trackside equipment.</li>
<li>Altitude above ground (or water): note in flight plan.</li>
<li>Horizontal maximum speed of UAS for the purpose of this mission.</li>
<li>Wind speed and direction on the day of execution.</li>
<li>The effects of turbulence and the Venturi effect.</li>
<li>Estimation of the proximity and the number of expected (un)involved parties.</li>
</ol>
<p><em>Operational procedures</em></p>
<ol>
<li>Emergency procedures (to cope with abnormal situations) are defined.</li>
<li>The limitations of the external systems that support UAS for safe operation are recorded in a operating manual.</li>
<li>The operational procedures can be tested by the applicant (for example in a simulated environment or in the Railcenter in Amersfoort).</li>
<li>Procedures for take-off and landing near railway lines are defined (e.g. Zone C or further, "always take-off with wind at the back").</li>
<li>Procedures to safely "hold" to the passage of a train during manual operations have been established.</li>
<li>Procedures for the coordination of operation with the person responsible for the applicable track (e.g. OvD) are laid down.</li>
<li>Procedures for informing inactive participants (e.g. signs and clothing) and checking controlled ground surface have been established.</li>
</ol>
<p><em>Emergency Response Plan (ERP) (M3=high)</em></p>
<ol>
<li>[OPERATOR] coordinates an Emergency Response Plan (ERP) with all relevant third parties (ProRail or (sub)contractors) identified in the plan.</li>
<li>The ERP is validated by means of a representative exercise on the tabletop (e.g. chronological discussion of steps during a possible incident or accident) between the operator and the contracting party.</li>
<li>The ERP must be in accordance with the contingency plan in the V&amp;G plan of ProRail (or subcontractor of ProRail).</li>
<li>The representativeness of the table exercise is validated by a competent third party (ILT).</li>
<li>The ERP must be consistent with the ERP training system.</li>
<li>An ERP training program (explaining how and how often the crew is trained on the ERP) is available. A record of the ERP training followed by the relevant staff is established and updated. In addition, the competences of the relevant personnel are verified by a competent third party (ILT).</li>
</ol>
<p><em>Education and training</em></p>
<p>Training elements related to drone operations over railways are included in a crew qualification schedule. This training contains all the details covered in this standard scenario (e.g. RailAlert requirements such as a 'Digital Safety Passport' or a 'Day Pass').</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_l5TjwRClKuy3ET49j8a9" class="not_editable" data-id="l5TjwRClKuy3ET49j8a9">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="l5TjwRClKuy3ET49j8a9" id="mcetoc_1itg4ja7124g"><span class="shortcode">[C3.13]</span> <span class="name">Procedure flying in other EU member states</span></h2>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fpictogrammen%20Drone%20Consultancy%20Ad-hoc.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=107b0037-fdc3-4e08-a3fb-bbe02169015e" alt="" width="93"> This procedure shall include additional measures, which may slightly vary from one Member State to another. For the basic procedure for applying for an operation in another Member State, <a href="#article_wbmNMlvDzMrnhZBjHT6y">see [A7.24] flying in other EU countries.</a></p>
<p>First of all, a UAS operator that intends to conduct an operation, for which an operational authorisation is required, partially or fully in a Member State other than the State of registration, should already be in possess of any required authorisation (OA) for that operation from the State of registration.</p>
<p>In addition, the operator should research the applicable local conditions and national regulations where the operator intends to conduct an operation. If it is necessary, the operational procedures should be adapted. Moreover, update on the application of the mitigation means and local conditions. The identification of the location(s) should contain the full operational volume and ground risk buffer (see [A.6.4] Operational Volume Determination and [APPENDIX C3.1] Flight Preparation Phase 1 and 2 and ERP).</p>
<p>Finally, submit to the competent authority of the MS of operation (refer to <span class="s2"><a href="https://www.easa.europa.eu/domains/civil-drones/naa">https://www.easa.europa.eu/domains/civil-drones/naa</a> </span>for the links to the NAA websites) an application for a cross-border operation using the form<sup>1</sup> attaching the following documents:<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<ol>
<li>a copy of the operational authorisation.</li>
<li>those chapter(s)/section(s) of the OM (or Operational Plan (OP) providing the operational procedures and the relevant information, amended as necessary, to comply with the local conditions and apply the mitigation measures to the intended location(s).</li>
</ol>
<p>Once the competent authority in the member state of operation is satisfied, they will provide the competent authority (ILT) and the UAS operator with the confirmation of<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>acceptability.</p>
<p><sup>1</sup>See Appendix H for an example of an application for for cross-border operations.</p>
<p>For specific member states, procedures are noted here if applicable.</p>
</article>
<p>Belgium</p>
<ul>
<li>A copy of the operational authorization granted to the UAS operator</li>
<li>The location(s) of the intended operation including the updated mitigation measures, if needed, to address those risks identified which are specific to the local airspace, terrain and population characteristics and the climatic conditions</li>
<li>Send to <a href="mailto:uas@mobilit.fgov.be">uas@mobilit.fgov.be</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Germany</p>
<ul>
<li>A duly signed and completed <a href="https://www.lba.de/SharedDocs/Downloads/DE/Formulare/B5/B53/Formulare_Englisch/FV.GO-UASOPA-0102.pdf?__blob=publicationFile&amp;v=11">application form</a>.</li>
<li>A copy of the operational authorisation from the national aviation authority of your country of residency that need to include the initial GRC, ARC and the mitigations.</li>
<li>The operating location(s) in Germany including operational volume and risk buffer description and updated mitigation measures.</li>
<li>Send to <a href="mailto:UAS@Lba.de">UAS@Lba.de</a></li>
</ul>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>

<h1 id="mcetoc_1fdf7ngrq1rd8">Chapter C4: CONTINGENCY PROCEDURES<span style="color: #ced4d9; font-size: 10pt;">[APE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_aZ4WuqiQRlsuJfSTHMw7" class="not_editable" data-id="aZ4WuqiQRlsuJfSTHMw7">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="aZ4WuqiQRlsuJfSTHMw7" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11u"><span class="shortcode">[C4.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Contingency Procedures</span></h2>
<p>Contingency Procedures are designed for unexpected or abnormal situations. The operation however is still under control. The objective for the Contingency Procedures is to return as quickly as possible to normal operations. For loss of control situations, the <a href="#article_LrAA5evvw7TdPnUu9z9C">emergency procedures are described in chapter C5</a>.</p>
<p>The difference between the procedures is explained in this picture:</p>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FAbnormale%20of%20Continengy%20procedures.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=c66a58a3-d2f3-40a8-ad6d-6b7e8012fd76" alt=""></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_9lW5NbSuYFIc7JWn1brq" class="not_editable" data-id="9lW5NbSuYFIc7JWn1brq">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757ak8" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="9lW5NbSuYFIc7JWn1brq"><span class="shortcode">[C4.1]</span> <span class="name">Unmanned Aircraft leaves the Flight Geography</span></h2>
<p>In case of (almost) leaving the Flight Geography, the following procedures should be used:</p>
</article>
<article id="article_TzRYcwXshMEKczmolbeL" class="not_editable" data-id="TzRYcwXshMEKczmolbeL">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="TzRYcwXshMEKczmolbeL" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln11v"><span class="shortcode">[C4.1.1]</span> <span class="name">Return to Home (RtH)</span></h2>
<ol>
<li>Press home button on controller hold until confirmation is given on controller that the RTH procedure is active.</li>
<li>Pressing the RTH within 25 meters of the pre-programmed landing location (take-off point), the UAS will slowly land in a constant straight down.</li>
<li>Outside this 25m, the UAS will climb to set RTH height and then fly back in a straight line to the landing point, where the landing will be started.</li>
<li>The UAS also has a failsafe so that when the controller is switched off, the autonomous RTH procedure is automatically activated after 10 seconds.</li>
</ol>
<p>Please note that it only works if there are no GNSS disruptions.</p>
</article>
<article id="article_JrHc9zwIKCPbZuzAlDI2" class="not_editable" data-id="JrHc9zwIKCPbZuzAlDI2">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhmla0m6m" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="JrHc9zwIKCPbZuzAlDI2"><span class="shortcode">[C4.1.2]</span> <span class="name">Mid-Air Stop DJI</span></h2>
<p>In case the UAS is not responding and crossing the contingency volume, the motors are turned off remotely and the UAS will crash.</p>
<div>
<p><span lang="EN">Actions:</span></p>
</div>
<div>
<ol>
<li><span lang="EN">Pay attention to the environment and ensure that there are no people underneath the UAS;</span></li>
<li>Stay calm and inform the crew;</li>
<li>Warn crewmembers;</li>
<li><span lang="EN">Press RTH while pulling the left stick to the bottom inner corner.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_Xqo5l6ltRJimL7fVDwgm" class="not_editable" data-id="Xqo5l6ltRJimL7fVDwgm">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="Xqo5l6ltRJimL7fVDwgm" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln120"><span class="shortcode">[C4.2]</span> <span class="name">Uninvolved persons enter the controlled area</span></h2>
<p>The observer is responsible for keeping watchers (= Uninvolved persons) away so that the UAS pilot can maintain focus on the operation.</p>
<p>Actions:</p>
<ol>
<li>The observer addresses uninvolved persons who are about to enter the flying area and kindly asks them to keep their distance.</li>
<li>The observer tries to operate in a de-escalating manner so that the pilot can remain focused on the operation.</li>
<li>The observer will remain between the pilot and the uninvolved persons in case of aggression.</li>
<li>Escalation? The pilot lands the UAS safely and clear it away.</li>
<li>Should this escalate further, the observer or pilot will contact the police.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_VSe5v9SmcaGsdm7U7Mpy" class="not_editable" data-id="VSe5v9SmcaGsdm7U7Mpy">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757akb" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="VSe5v9SmcaGsdm7U7Mpy"><span class="shortcode">[C4.3]</span> <span class="name">Adverse operating conditions</span></h2>
<p>During operations, the conditions can change unexpected. For example, weather conditions change rapidly, or an accident happens nearby. These procedures describe the steps to take.</p>
</article>
<article id="article_43NMW0dnkoHm9ze2hpyu" class="not_editable" data-id="43NMW0dnkoHm9ze2hpyu">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhmla0m6n" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="43NMW0dnkoHm9ze2hpyu"><span class="shortcode">[C4.3.1]</span> <span class="name">Adverse weather conditions</span></h2>
<p>Precipitation and fog can cause a short circuit in the UAS. When icing, the upward force and balance of the UAS is compromised.</p>
<p>Action:</p>
<ol>
<li>Stay calm and inform the crew;</li>
<li>Land as soon as possible.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<article id="article_HzPpmVf84SDd5kpzqjQe" class="not_editable" data-id="HzPpmVf84SDd5kpzqjQe">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757akc" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="HzPpmVf84SDd5kpzqjQe"><span class="shortcode">[C4.3.2]</span> <span class="name">Turbulence or extreme windspeeds / venturi effect</span></h2>
<p>In certain specific operations, such as near industry and/or urban areas, turbulence due to the venturi effect is to be expected. In addition, in these areas there is a greater chance of a loose off link due to EM disruption.</p>
<p><strong>Signals:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Notification on controller (High wind);</li>
<li>The UAS does not fly stably in the air.</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;<strong>Actions:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Stay calm and inform the crew;</li>
<li>Fly with the airflow and keep your distance from objects;</li>
<li>Try to fly out of the turbulence in a safe location;</li>
<li>Land as soon as possible.</li>
</ol>
<p>More about the Venturi-effect: <a href="#article_u6S19kJ8tnIBziluhJoS">Chapter D1.6 Turbulence </a></p>
</article>
<article id="article_qdSSq724tVRnjIIOLw03" class="not_editable" data-id="qdSSq724tVRnjIIOLw03">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="qdSSq724tVRnjIIOLw03" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln121"><span class="shortcode">[C4.3.3]</span> <span class="name">Bird Attack</span></h2>
<p><span>Birds can certainly be aggressive against a UAS in the breeding season. Especially the larger birds will confront. Oystercatchers and crows are also known for their aggressive behavior.</span></p>
<p><span>Actions</span></p>
<ol>
<li><span>Stay calm and inform the crew;</span></li>
<li><span>Move the UAS to a calmer area;</span></li>
<li><span>With persistent aggressiveness back to landing site.</span></li>
</ol>
</article>
<article id="article_GX5sEiT15ZmNCsvJllP2" class="not_editable" data-id="GX5sEiT15ZmNCsvJllP2">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757ake" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="GX5sEiT15ZmNCsvJllP2"><span class="shortcode">[C4.3.4]</span> <span class="name">Accident in proximity or other distraction</span></h2>
<p>An incident nearby can always happen. This can be both a stand-alone incident and the result of distraction from the operation.</p>
<p><strong>Actions:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Stay calm and inform the crew;</li>
<li>Hover the UAS in a safe location;</li>
<li>Determines the severity of the incident;</li>
</ol>
<p>Need first aid?</p>
<ol>
<li>Abort mission;</li>
<li>Call first responds and emergency services (112);</li>
</ol>
<p>Operation hamper for emergency services?</p>
<ol>
<li>Yes, abort mission</li>
<li>No, continue mission;</li>
</ol>
<p>Keep an eye on the situation.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_dKPqtLo0MiHvLaYP9ywq" class="not_editable" data-id="dKPqtLo0MiHvLaYP9ywq">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fr2f6tog1c3" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="dKPqtLo0MiHvLaYP9ywq"><span class="shortcode">[C4.4]</span> <span class="name">Failure of external systems supporting the flight operations</span></h2>
<p>Sometimes external systems fail (temporarily). The procedures for this failure are written here.</p>
</article>
<article id="article_gn2WVhcLYc4c3wHPouQU" class="not_editable" data-id="gn2WVhcLYc4c3wHPouQU">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="gn2WVhcLYc4c3wHPouQU" id="mcetoc_1ib4kg3vdu"><span class="shortcode">[C4.4.1]</span> <span class="name">GNSS signal failure</span></h2>
<p><span>If the GNSS signal is disturbed (see controller) and it is not recovered quick by the system via RTH itself, the UAS pilot proceeds as follows: </span></p>
<p><strong>Actions</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><span>Stay calm and inform the crew;</span></li>
<li><span>Switch to ATTI mode on controller (if possible);</span></li>
<li><span>Pause the mission by hovering or returning to the home position</span></li>
<li><span>Resume mission after recovery.</span></li>
</ol>
<p><strong>No recovery?</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><span>Return home manually and land directly.</span></li>
</ol>
<p><span>&nbsp;</span><span>Note the autonomous RTH procedure of the UAS does not work without GNSS.</span></p>
</article>
<article id="article_vvikiuMGYNYHKyHf2NDY" class="not_editable" data-id="vvikiuMGYNYHKyHf2NDY">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fr2f6tog1c5" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="vvikiuMGYNYHKyHf2NDY"><span class="shortcode">[C4.4.2]</span> <span class="name">Autopilot Failure</span></h2>
<p>Autopilot failure occurs during a flight in which the flight takes place using an intelligent flight mode where the UA system uses, for example, waypoints entered by the pilot. During this flight mode, a pilot will be present at all times with remote control in his hands. If the autopilot fails, he will immediately have to be able to manually take over control by activating the manual mode.</p>
<p>To minimize the chance of an autopilot failure occurring again, the UA will have to be landed to check all systems. Recheck the Kp-index as it may affect failure. When the mission is resumed, the analysis will have to be taken into account and an adjusted flight path and/or manual flight mode may have to be used.</p>
<p>Signals:</p>
<ul>
<li>LEDs on UAS flash yellow.</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;Actions:</p>
<ol>
<li>Stay calm and inform the crew;</li>
<li>Interrupt program by touching the sticks;</li>
<li>Optionally, the program may need to be paused on the controller/tablet;</li>
<li>Optional short-term change of flight mode on controller;</li>
<li>Bring UAS back to landing site;</li>
<li>Check UAS.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<article id="article_dfbw5DeAzMkVj65fD7zp" class="not_editable" data-id="dfbw5DeAzMkVj65fD7zp">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fr2f6tog1c6" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="dfbw5DeAzMkVj65fD7zp"><span class="shortcode">[C4.4.3]</span> <span class="name">Low Battery Voltage</span></h2>
<p>In the event of a low battery voltage or low battery the following signals will appear:</p>
<ul>
<li>Controller shows low percentage;</li>
<li>Controller gives audible signal;</li>
<li>LEDs flash red (Low battery warning);</li>
<li>LEDs flash red quickly (Critical battery warning).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Actions</strong></p>
<p>Set the battery level warning threshold lower, so that UA can fly back to the location before the battery becomes empty.</p>
<p>Fly directly back to the take-off and landing location.</p>
<p>It can also happen that the battery voltage suddenly drops faster than expected. There are 3 options available:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fly back to the take-off and landing location</li>
<li>Landing at an alternative take-off and landing location</li>
<li>Land the UAS immediately.</li>
</ul>
<p>In this situation, the UAS pilot will decide the correct option, whether or not in consultation with the observer.</p>
</article>
<article class="not_editable" data-id="geIRWVO3hq4bd5MpWKY4" id="article_geIRWVO3hq4bd5MpWKY4">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="geIRWVO3hq4bd5MpWKY4" id="mcetoc_1i1cgdiinee"><span class="shortcode">[C4.4.4]</span> <span class="name">Navigation Failure</span></h2>
<p class="p2">In case of navigation failure, control of the UA will be taken over manually, because the reliability of the GNSS can no longer be guaranteed. The UA will then be flown to the holding area. The loss of<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>navigation can be the result of an interrupted or lost GNSS connection. A potential source of interference causing navigation failure can also cause steering or connectivity failure. So it is crucial to act cautiously in case of navigation failure. If the fault continues, it is important to find out what the cause is. For each incident, the PIC should estimate whether the operation can be continued safely without navigation (GNSS) and whether the operation can be manually conducted and does not have to depend on GNSS.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_47consH3pQ76mhQ7I0Q6" class="not_editable" data-id="47consH3pQ76mhQ7I0Q6">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="47consH3pQ76mhQ7I0Q6" id="mcetoc_1i2bqufunc"><span class="shortcode">[C4.5]</span> <span class="name">Avoid conflicts with other airspace users</span></h2>
<span style="font-size: 12pt;">Safe and efficient drone operation in shared airspace environments is crucial. With the increasing use of drones across various industries, it is essential for operators to navigate shared airspace responsibly. This section provides guidance on avoiding conflicts with other airspace users, ensuring safety and compliance.To mitigate conflicts and promote safe airspace usage, drone operators should prioritize the following principles:</span>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Airspace Awareness: Understand airspace classifications, regulations, and restrictions. Stay updated on airspace dynamics to assess collision risks and navigate safely.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Situational Awareness: Stay alert to surrounding airspace conditions. Continuously monitor for other aircraft, obstacles, and hazards. Adjust flight path or altitude as needed to ensure safe navigation.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">VLOS (Visual Line of Sight): Maintain direct visual contact with the drone throughout its flight to enhance situational awareness and respond to potential conflicts.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">Communication: Establish clear communication with other airspace users, air traffic control, and authorities. Coordinate movements, share operational information, and resolve conflicts effectively.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt;">These principles promote safe and compliant drone operations, enhancing overall airspace safety and efficiency.</span></p>
</article>
<article id="article_U2jxv8w6blwwH0Sh7ySl" class="not_editable" data-id="U2jxv8w6blwwH0Sh7ySl">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="U2jxv8w6blwwH0Sh7ySl" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln122"><span class="shortcode">[C4.5.1]</span> <span class="name">Avoiding Other Air Traffic</span></h2>
<p>An intruder is another aircraft that enters the operational volume. The deconfliction scheme contains all possible actions and considerations.</p>
<p><img style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy.appspot.com/o/images%2FDe-confliction%20scheme%20aircraft%20in%20Operational%20Volume.png?alt=media&amp;token=4246a10e-cc5d-45da-9fb2-c9333b577984" alt=""></p>
<p>Actions:</p>
<ol>
<li>The observer identifies air traffic and transmits information to the pilot;</li>
<li>The observer shall inform the pilot of the direction and, if possible, of the altitude of the other air traffic,</li>
<li>Lower the UAS quickly, preferably to the holding area and/or on the landing platform</li>
<li>If on the same course and no possibility to descend: swerve to the right;</li>
<li>Pause the operation until the other air traffic has passed or stop the entire operation.</li>
</ol>
</article>
<article id="article_4B9hhuaR7vZT7aGIiIYS" class="not_editable" data-id="4B9hhuaR7vZT7aGIiIYS">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="4B9hhuaR7vZT7aGIiIYS" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln123"><span class="shortcode">[C4.5.2]</span> <span class="name">Communication Problem with Air Traffic Control (LVNL)</span></h2>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Due to occupied frequencies by another parties, signals may deteriorate.</span></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true"><strong>Signals:</strong><br></span></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">No contact with ATC;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">No clearly audible response ATC;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Report of poor reception by ATC.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Mitigating measure</span></strong></p>
<ul>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Radio check in advance with Air Traffic Control;</span></li>
<li><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Telephone numbers in the Emergency Response Plan (enclosed in Operations Flight Plan)</span></li>
</ul>
<p><strong><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Action</span></strong></p>
<p><span data-preserver-spaces="true">Calling Air Traffic Control by mobile phone. The number is stated by default in the Operations Flight Plan.</span></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p><div class="page-break"></div><p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f6k76vm36v9">PART C5: EMERGENCY PROCEDURES<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[NOPE]</span></h1>
<article id="article_LrAA5evvw7TdPnUu9z9C" class="not_editable" data-id="LrAA5evvw7TdPnUu9z9C">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="LrAA5evvw7TdPnUu9z9C" id="mcetoc_1in3piidej1"><span class="shortcode">[C5.0]</span> <span class="name">Introduction Emergency Procedures</span></h2>
<p>Operational control is lost. In this chapter several procedures to cope with loss of operational control are described.</p>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FNoodprocedures.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=b6b1f045-bc25-4ca1-8943-8205b2c5deb0" alt=""></p>
<p>Several scenarios can occur during an emergency. For each situation, it is be described how the pilot and observer of [OPERATOR] will act during these situations. These emergency procedures are regularly trained, see <a href="#article_Amg1RhPJCEGzwnk6E53X">Chapter D2 Training.</a></p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_YW1f57Pvi7KomxoTjURa" class="not_editable" data-id="YW1f57Pvi7KomxoTjURa">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1gf5tglhd80" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="YW1f57Pvi7KomxoTjURa"><span class="shortcode">[C5.1]</span> <span class="name">Fly Away (Loss of Link)</span></h2>
<p class="p1">A "fly away" is a situation in which the UAS no longer responds to input from the controller(s)/RTH function and flies away uncontrollably.<span class="Apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p>To support the safety situation in the event of a loss or link, a home position must be set by the ground station before the flight operation. The correct setting of the return to home function is necessary to be able to use the function safely during the loss of link.&nbsp;</p>
<p>When the communication between UAS and the remote controller is lost, the UAS will automatically activate the return to home function and the UAS will start the landing procedure.</p>
<ol>
<li data-xf-list-type="ul">Attempt to initiate RTH</li>
<li data-xf-list-type="ul">Try and re-establish connection by turning off and rebooting remote</li>
<li data-xf-list-type="ul">Since you are aware of your own aircrafts flight duration - Note battery level, bearing and altitude, speed and time the signal was lost. From this you will be able to approximate (with the help of maps) the rough area your aircraft will ditch/attempt to land. Give this information to your local police explaining the reasons etc - see ERP.</li>
</ol>
<p>When the connection is restored, it may be possible to regain control, when the connection between the remote control and UAS is restored it will be visible on the ground station.</p>
<p>In any case, it is necessary to land the UAS and perform a technical check before the mission can continue.</p>
<p>In the event of Loss of Link due to hijacking, the authorities must be notified immediately as noted in the flight plan, see the section <a href="#article_HZqMod6IwVtQbkSvAi0H">[APPENDIX C] Flight Plan and Check Lists</a>.</p>
<p>Also, report the incident afterwards at ILT (<a href="https://www.ilent.nl/onderwerpen/voorvallen-luchtvaart">https://www.ILT.nl/onderwerpen/voorvallen-luchtvaart</a>). In the event of a fly-away during an operation near a CTR, the relevant operator is immediately notified.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_gE60tchHFr4jgJ0XB6CP" class="not_editable" data-id="gE60tchHFr4jgJ0XB6CP">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757akk" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="gE60tchHFr4jgJ0XB6CP"><span class="shortcode">[C5.2]</span> <span class="name">Engine Failure</span></h2>
<p>If an engine failure, the UAS will have to be grounded as soon as possible at a selected fall-back location, which will be stated in the flight plan.</p>
<p>When all engines fail, this must be immediately reported to the surroundings because the UAS can no longer be controlled in a standard procedure and that might result in an uncontrolled crash.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_Z1y0j0rnCftzgpEAPrC1" class="not_editable" data-id="Z1y0j0rnCftzgpEAPrC1">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="Z1y0j0rnCftzgpEAPrC1" id="mcetoc_1h4is3uln124"><span class="shortcode">[C5.3]</span> <span class="name">Pilot Unwell</span></h2>
<p>When a pilot becomes unwell, other crew members must have options to safely ground the UAS. Part of the briefing to the observer is explaining how to activate a failsafe mode with a return to home function. This is also part of the practical training.</p>
<p>In the event of a pilot who has become unwell, the observer can then take over control and activate the return to home function of the UAS.</p>
<p>Should medical attention be required, the observer will call emergency services and manage the area. Should a safety risk arise during a flight, the observer will take control and perform the landing. This action will be practiced during practical training.</p>
<p>The Accountable Manager must be notified as soon as possible.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_l1IeW8Gu76Znc0rBWoSH" class="not_editable" data-id="l1IeW8Gu76Znc0rBWoSH">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757akm" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="l1IeW8Gu76Znc0rBWoSH"><span class="shortcode">[C5.4]</span> <span class="name">Fatal Error</span></h2>
<p>In the event of a crash, the UA will have to be approached with caution and the fire and/or safety situation will have to be assessed by the PIC. Fire extinguishers must be taken to the location of the crash. Affected institutions or organisations must be warned in case of damage to the environment, people or animals, see section <a href="#article_ME8TopExIqtaPvt2Ywoj">[A4.3] Reporting Accident</a> <a href="#article_V28zgwoWrmKWuTmVRuFo">[A11.1] Reporting Procedures</a>&nbsp;and <a href="#article_WdXhvMUctC5u9FmE8sm6">[C6.1] Emergency Response Plan (ERP)</a>.<br>In particular, LiPo batteries from the UA can be in an unstable state after a crash with possible ignition hazard. If a crash or collision can be avoided by switching off the engines, the PIC must make a timely decision. In the event of a collision with air traffic, people or the environment, the UA and the engines must be switched off immediately.</p>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_BtX641FrV8c1D8N1jZNe" class="not_editable" data-id="BtX641FrV8c1D8N1jZNe">
<h2 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757akn" class="mceNonEditable" data-id="BtX641FrV8c1D8N1jZNe"><span class="shortcode">[C5.5]</span> <span class="name">UAS or Battery Fire</span></h2>
<p>In the event of a fire at the UAS or LiPos, the pilot is responsible for assessing the situation and choosing an approach.</p>
<p>The pilot will perform the following actions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Shout “FIRE, FIRE”.</li>
<li>Manoeuvre the UAS to a safe landing site.</li>
<li>Switch "Fly" to "Land"</li>
<li>Land the drone as soon as possible.</li>
</ul>
<p>The observer will perform the following actions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Looking for a safe landing site.</li>
<li>Informs the pilot about the area and keeps an eye on the UAS.</li>
<li>Ensures that the area is safe and remains safe.</li>
</ul>
<p>Once the UAS has landed, the crew will monitor the fire. This incident should be filled in the logbook later.</p>
<p>The surrounding fire will either be extinguished by using the CO<sub>2</sub> extinguisher or the authorities must be notified immediately. After a fire situation, all affected parts will have to be properly disposed of.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The Accountable Manager must be notified as soon as possible. If the fire becomes dangerous, the fire brigade must be informed.</p>
</article>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1f6k76vm36va"></h1>
<h1 id="mcetoc_1fmhnu757ako"><div class="page-break"></div>CHAPTER C6: EMERGENCY RESPONSE PLAN (ERP)<span style="font-size: 10pt; color: #ced4d9;">[ERPE]<br></span></h1>
<article id="article_FvkKfqttIhBBbmN026vW" class="not_editable" data-id="FvkKfqttIhBBbmN026vW">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="FvkKfqttIhBBbmN026vW" id="mcetoc_1in3piidfj2"><span class="shortcode">[C6.1]</span> <span class="name">Purpose of the ERP</span></h2>
<p><span>[OPERATOR] should, in cooperation with other stakeholders, if applicable, develop, coordinate, and maintain an ERP that ensures orderly and safe transition from normal operation to emergency and return to normal operation. The ERP includes the actions to be taken by the UAS operator or specified individuals in an emergency, and indicate the size, nature, and complexity of the activities to be performed by the UAS operator.</span></p>
<p><span>This procedure has been updated according to ED Decision 2022-002 R.</span></p>
<p><span>As for emergency procedures, an ERP is implemented by [OPERATOR] to address emergency situations. However, an ERP is specifically developed to:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span>limit any escalating effect of the emergency situation;</span></li>
<li><span>meet the conditions to alert the relevant authorities and entities.</span></li>
<li><span>The ERP should contain all the necessary information about the role of the relevant personnel in an emergency and about their response to it.</span><span></span></li>
</ul>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_mGNqkDnwrXlWRbKln6Kr" class="not_editable" data-id="mGNqkDnwrXlWRbKln6Kr">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="mGNqkDnwrXlWRbKln6Kr" id="mcetoc_1in3piidfj3"><span class="shortcode">[C6.2M]</span> <span class="name">Effectiveness of the ERP Medium level of Integrity</span></h2>
<p><span>For M3 Emergency Response Plan at Medium Level, additional means of compliance have been issued in Annex II to ED Decision 2022/002/R.</span></p>
<p><span>AMC/GM to the annex to regulation EU 2019-947- issue 1 amendment 2 states that f</span>or medium level of integrity the following requirements should be met:</p>
<table height="771" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; height: 212px; border-color: #000000; border-style: solid;">
<tbody>
<tr style="height: 23px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 23px; background-color: #e03e2d;">
<p style="text-align: center;"><span style="color: #ffffff;"><strong>Level of Integrity, the ERP:</strong></span></p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 23px; background-color: #e03e2d;">
<p><span style="color: #ffffff;"><strong>Proof / see OM chapter: </strong></span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 107px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 59px;">
<p>(a) be appropriate to the size, nature, and complexity of the UAS operation;</p>
<p>(b) be readily accessible by all relevant personnel and by other entities, where applicable;</p>
<p>(c) include procedures and checklists relevant to different or specific emergency situations;</p>
<p>(d) clearly define the roles and responsibilities of the relevant personnel;</p>
<p>(e) have quick-reference contact details of the relevant personnel;</p>
<p>(f) be regularly tested through practical exercises involving the relevant personnel; and</p>
<p>(g) be periodically reviewed and updated, when necessary, to maintain its effectiveness.</p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 59px;">
<p><span>The ERP of [OPERATOR] is developed for our organisation, accessible for our personnel and includes a procedure and checklists.&nbsp;</span></p>
<p><span></span></p>
<p><span>A quick reference card, procedure, roles and responsibility is part of the</span><span> Operational (flight) Plan (OP) of Operator. See also a representative tabletop exercise including ERP (separate document) and [D2.5].</span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 15px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 10px; background-color: #ecf0f1;">
<p><span>Assurance criterion 1 (procedures):</span></p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 10px; background-color: #ecf0f1;">
<p><span>&nbsp;</span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 107px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 32px;">
<p>a)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span>The ERP is developed to standards considered adequate by the competent authority and/or in accordance with means of compliance acceptable to that authority.</span></p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 32px;">
<p><span>This ERP is in accordance with the standards considered adequate by CAA-NL (ILT).</span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 107px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 51px;">

</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 51px;">

</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 23px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 10px; background-color: #ecf0f1;">
<p><span>Assurance criterion 2 (training):</span></p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 10px; background-color: #ecf0f1;">
<p><span>&nbsp;</span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 20px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 10px;">
<p>a)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span>An ERP training syllabus is available.</span></p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 10px;">
<p><span>See <a href="#article_Amg1RhPJCEGzwnk6E53X">chapter training Emergency Procedures</a></span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 63px;">
<td width="320" style="width: 54.2738%; height: 17px;">
<p>b)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span>A record of the ERP training completed by the relevant staff is established and kept up to date.</span></p>
</td>
<td width="294" style="width: 41.3695%; height: 17px;">
<p><span>See <a href="#article_Amg1RhPJCEGzwnk6E53X">chapter training General</a></span></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</article>
<p></p>
<article id="article_vcHOErd6Mp3n5wAKBDPd" class="not_editable" data-id="vcHOErd6Mp3n5wAKBDPd">
<h2 class="mceNonEditable" data-id="vcHOErd6Mp3n5wAKBDPd" id="mcetoc_1in3piidfj4"><span class="shortcode">[C6.3]</span> <span class="name">Activation of ERP</span></h2>
