<td colspan="6" width="633" style="width: 99.956%; border-color: #95a5a6;">
<p><strong>Operational Volume and ground buffer</strong></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="height: 1451.48px;">
<td colspan="6" width="633" style="width: 99.956%; border-color: #95a5a6;">
<p style="text-align: center;"><em></em></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em></em></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em></em></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em></em></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>a. Overview map with location Operational Volume</em></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>b. Air risk / Airspace operational volume (Godrone)</em></p>
<p><em></em></p>
<p><em></em></p>
<p><em></em></p>
<p></p>
<p><em>&nbsp;</em></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>c. Map showing dimensions of the Operational Volume (Flight area and Contingency Area)</em></p>
<p></p>
<p><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FGRbuffer.png?alt=media&amp;token=e9fdf311-6a65-4fbd-8bae-69134fe7cd27" alt="" width="230" height="143" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"></p>
<p>Ground risk depends on several factors, such as wind, the UAS used, flight speed and the expected number of people. Calculate the dimensions using the ballistic method or the 1:1 rule (see OM). Note in the chart:</p>
<ul>
<li>The dimensions of the Operational Volume (flight area as well as the Contingency Area)</li>
<li>The dimensions of the Ground Risk Buffer</li>
<li>The take-off and landing location</li>
<li>Location of crew members</li>
<li>Flight altitude (in relation to the Ground Risk Buffer)&nbsp;</li>
</ul>

<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;"><em>*&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </em>Indicative: depends on the size of the Company and volume of business.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FScreenshot%202023-02-02%20at%2017.13.33.png?alt=media&amp;token=391fa203-9e7c-4f12-911f-97e0fd7ebf2e" alt="" width="766" height="193"></span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 8pt;">Source: EHEST-Safety Management Toolkit-Guidance-NCO - V.2 30 Sep</span></p>
<p><strong>Unacceptable Risk Level -</strong> the <strong>red</strong> zone in the matrix: risk is too high to continue operating.</p>
<p><u>Action required</u>: Prohibit/suspend the operation.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Tolerable Risk Level</strong> - the <strong>yellow</strong> zone in the matrix: the risk level can be tolerated for the operation, providing that appropriate mitigation measures are in place.</p>
<p><u>Action required</u>: Introduce appropriate mitigation measures.</p>
<p><strong>Acceptable Risk Level</strong> - the <strong>green </strong>zone in the matrix: risk is tolerable and can be accepted for the operation.</p>
<p><!-- pagebreak --></p>
<p><strong>Crew briefing flying outside UDP</strong></p>
<p>This briefing is conducted by the pilot with night flight experience and training according to the Syllabus.</p>
<p>Night flying has a number of additional risks:</p>
<ul>
<li>More difficult to find reference points to control the drone or to see where you are. Certain landmarks that you would use during the day are not visible in the dark. And what you can see is different from what it looks like during the day.</li>
<li>Decreased visual cues and increased likelihood of perceptual illusions and the resulting risk of spatial disorientation.</li>
<li>In the case of an emergency or precautionary landing, there is an increased risk in the dark due to the lack of visual reference points. The outcome of an accident at night is often more serious than an accident that occurs during the day. For example, it is difficult to find an obstacle-free emergency landing field in the dark.</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;Other than during the day:</p>
<ul>
<li>The drone has extra lighting. In addition, the take-off and landing location is cordoned off (and illuminated);</li>
<li>Your eyes can quickly become dazzled by bright lighting, for example from cars. It takes a while to get used to it. Should that happen: Should something like this occur and you can foresee it in time, cover one eye, or close one eye. Then that eye at least retains its adaptation to the dark;</li>
<li>The pilot flies on instrument more than during the day and is even more dependent on the observer who:
<ul>
<li>Listens carefully to aircraft noise and look at a white flashing light which may be an aircraft;</li>
<li>Sees/hears aircraft, should shout “Aircraft, down” at once.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Nighttime illusions can cause unwanted confusion and distraction. Flickering lights can cause vertigo (balance disorder). Cities, lanterns, illuminated wind farms are clearly visible and this often gives the feeling that you can see further;</li>
<li>Cloud layers and light patterns on the ground can be mistaken for the horizon (false horizon);</li>
<li>So an incipient fatigue is an absolute no-go for flying. Do not be pressured to continue the flight, for whatever the reason is;</li>
<li>Because flying outside UDP requires more eyesight and concentration, a PIC flies a maximum of 2 hours outside UDP per 24 hours;</li>
<li>When viewing, keep in mind that you have to look 5-10 degrees next to an object to see it. See image below:</li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2FUDP%20Nachtelijke%20blindspot.jpg?alt=media&amp;token=0af3b985-53bb-4314-b2a9-1645b9560948" alt=""></p>
<table width="100%" height="746" style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%; height: 1792.41px; border-color: #95a5a6;" border="1">

<p>Data protection: Personal data included in this application is processed by the competent authority pursuant to Regulation (EU) 2016/679 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 27 April 2016 on the protection of natural persons with regard to the processing of personal data and on the free movement of such data, and repealing Directive 95/46/EC (General Data Protection Regulation). Personal data will be processed for the purposes of the performance, management and follow-up of the application by the competent authority in accordance with Articles 12 and 13 of Regulation (EU) 2019/947 of 24 May 2019 on the rules and procedures for the operation of unmanned aircraft.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>If the applicant requires further information concerning the processing of their personal data or exercising their rights (e.g. to access or rectify any inaccurate or incomplete data), they should refer to the point of contact of their competent authority.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>The applicant has the right to file a complaint regarding the processing of their personal data at any time to the national data protection supervisory authority.</p>

<p><u>Instructions for filling in the application form</u></p>
<p>If the application relates to an amendment to a confirmation of acceptability for a cross-border UAS operation, please indicate the number of the confirmation of acceptability and fill out in red the fields that are amended compared to the last confirmation of acceptability.</p>
<p>1.1 UAS operator registration number in accordance with Article 14 of the UAS Regulation.</p>
<p>1.2 UAS operator’s name as declared during the registration process.</p>
<p>1.2 Contact details of the person responsible for the operation, in charge to answer possible operational questions raised by the competent Contact details of the person responsible for the operation, in charge to answer possible operational</p>
<p>1.4 Select one of the two</p>
<p>1.4.1. Number of the operational authorization or of the LUC terms of approval issued by the MS of The referenced document should be attached to the application.</p>
<p>1.4.2.Expiry date of the document listed in 1.4.2. If the validity is unlimited, indicate ‘Unlimited’.</p>
<p>2.1 Date on which the UAS operator expects to start the</p>
<p>2.2 Date on which the UAS operator expects to end the operation. The UAS operator may ask for an unlimited duration; in this case, indicate ‘Unlimited’.</p>
<p>2.3 Location(s) in the MS of operation where the UAS operator intends to conduct the UAS. The identification of the location(s) should contain the full operational volume and ground risk buffer (the red line in figure x). The location(s) should be expressed in the same way as in the operational authorization (e.g. ‘generic’ or ‘precise’, (refer to GM2 UAS.SPEC.030(2))).</p>
<p></p>
<p>&nbsp;<img src="https://firebasestorage.googleapis.com/v0/b/drone-consultancy-test.appspot.com/o/images_new%2F82HBR8nAdGoyZMspNn99%2Fcross%20boarder%20formulier.png?alt=media&amp;token=330dc167-48f9-42d2-bad4-f6feb1c67717" alt="" width="651"></p>
<p style="text-align: left;">&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; Figure 1 — Operational area and ground risk buffer</p>
<p style="text-align: left;"></p>
<p>2.4 Insert the upper limit, expressed in meters and feet in parenthesis, of the contingency volume (adding the air risk buffer if applicable) using the AGL - <u>A</u>bove <u>G</u>round <u>L</u>evel reference when the upper limit is below 150 m (500 ft), or use the MSL – <u>M</u>ean <u>S</u>ea <u>L</u>evel - reference when the upper limit is above 150 m (500 ft).</p>
<p>2.5 Select one or more of the nine Select ‘other’ in case none of the previous is applicable (i.e. military areas).</p>
<p>2.6 List the local conditions applicable to the location(s) defined in point 2.3 (e.g. special frequency to be avoided, national insurance regulation, ). If needed a separate document may be attached.</p>
<p>3.1 If operational procedures need to be updated to take into account the new locations or the local conditions, indicate either the identification and revision number of the OM or the document providing an extract of the OM including the chapter describing the operational procedures and the relevant information, amended by the UAS This document should be attached to the application. Otherwise indicate N/A.</p>
<p>3.2 If procedures are updated to address the characteristics of the new location or to meet the local conditions, indicate the compliance evidence file identification and revision This document should be attached to the application. Otherwise indicate N/A.</p>
<p>4. Free-text field for the addition of any relevant</p>
<p>Note: In case of LUC, point 3 should not be filled in if according to the LUC terms of approval the organization has the privilege to extend the operational authorization to different locations.</p>
</article>
